"1984" 1998 "What have we in common with the rose-bud, which trembleth because a drop"
"1985" 1998 "of dew hath formed upon it?"
"1986" 1998 ""
"1987" 1998 "It is true we love life; not because we are wont to live, but because we"
"1988" 1998 "are wont to love."
"1989" 1998 ""
"1990" 1998 "There is always some madness in love. But there is always, also, some"
"1991" 1998 "method in madness."
"1992" 1998 ""
"1993" 1998 "And to me also, who appreciate life, the butterflies, and soap-bubbles,"
"1994" 1998 "and whatever is like them amongst us, seem most to enjoy happiness."
"1995" 1998 ""
"1996" 1998 "To see these light, foolish, pretty, lively little sprites flit"
"1997" 1998 "about--that moveth Zarathustra to tears and songs."
"1998" 1998 ""
"1999" 1998 "I should only believe in a God that would know how to dance."
"2000" 1998 ""
"2001" 1998 "And when I saw my devil, I found him serious, thorough, profound,"
"2002" 1998 "solemn: he was the spirit of gravity--through him all things fall."
"2003" 1998 ""
"2004" 1998 "Not by wrath, but by laughter, do we slay. Come, let us slay the spirit"
"2005" 1998 "of gravity!"
"2006" 1998 ""
"2007" 1998 "I learned to walk; since then have I let myself run. I learned to fly;"
"2008" 1998 "since then I do not need pushing in order to move from a spot."
"2009" 1998 ""
"2010" 1998 "Now am I light, now do I fly; now do I see myself under myself. Now"
"2011" 1998 "there danceth a God in me.--"
"2012" 1998 ""
"2013" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"2014" 1998 ""
"2015" 1998 ""
"2016" 1998 ""
"2017" 1998 ""
"2018" 1998 "VIII. THE TREE ON THE HILL."
"2019" 1998 ""
"2020" 1998 "Zarathustra's eye had perceived that a certain youth avoided him. And as"
"2021" 1998 "he walked alone one evening over the hills surrounding the town called"
"2022" 1998 "\"The Pied Cow,\" behold, there found he the youth sitting leaning against"
"2023" 1998 "a tree, and gazing with wearied look into the valley. Zarathustra"
"2024" 1998 "thereupon laid hold of the tree beside which the youth sat, and spake"
"2025" 1998 "thus:"
"2026" 1998 ""
"2027" 1998 "\"If I wished to shake this tree with my hands, I should not be able to"
"2028" 1998 "do so."
"2029" 1998 ""
"2030" 1998 "But the wind, which we see not, troubleth and bendeth it as it listeth."
"2031" 1998 "We are sorest bent and troubled by invisible hands.\""
"2032" 1998 ""
"2033" 1998 "Thereupon the youth arose disconcerted, and said: \"I hear Zarathustra,"
"2034" 1998 "and just now was I thinking of him!\" Zarathustra answered:"
"2035" 1998 ""
"2036" 1998 "\"Why art thou frightened on that account?--But it is the same with man"
"2037" 1998 "as with the tree."
"2038" 1998 ""
"2039" 1998 "The more he seeketh to rise into the height and light, the more"
"2040" 1998 "vigorously do his roots struggle earthward, downward, into the dark and"
"2041" 1998 "deep--into the evil.\""
"2042" 1998 ""
"2043" 1998 "\"Yea, into the evil!\" cried the youth. \"How is it possible that thou"
"2044" 1998 "hast discovered my soul?\""
"2045" 1998 ""
"2046" 1998 "Zarathustra smiled, and said: \"Many a soul one will never discover,"
"2047" 1998 "unless one first invent it.\""
"2048" 1998 ""
"2049" 1998 "\"Yea, into the evil!\" cried the youth once more."
"2050" 1998 ""
"2051" 1998 "\"Thou saidst the truth, Zarathustra. I trust myself no longer since I"
"2052" 1998 "sought to rise into the height, and nobody trusteth me any longer; how"
"2053" 1998 "doth that happen?"
"2054" 1998 ""
"2055" 1998 "I change too quickly: my to-day refuteth my yesterday. I often overleap"
"2056" 1998 "the steps when I clamber; for so doing, none of the steps pardons me."
"2057" 1998 ""
"2058" 1998 "When aloft, I find myself always alone. No one speaketh unto me; the"
"2059" 1998 "frost of solitude maketh me tremble. What do I seek on the height?"
"2060" 1998 ""
"2061" 1998 "My contempt and my longing increase together; the higher I clamber, the"
"2062" 1998 "more do I despise him who clambereth. What doth he seek on the height?"
"2063" 1998 ""
"2064" 1998 "How ashamed I am of my clambering and stumbling! How I mock at my"
"2065" 1998 "violent panting! How I hate him who flieth! How tired I am on the"
"2066" 1998 "height!\""
"2067" 1998 ""
"2068" 1998 "Here the youth was silent. And Zarathustra contemplated the tree beside"
"2069" 1998 "which they stood, and spake thus:"
"2070" 1998 ""
"2071" 1998 "\"This tree standeth lonely here on the hills; it hath grown up high"
"2072" 1998 "above man and beast."
"2073" 1998 ""
"2074" 1998 "And if it wanted to speak, it would have none who could understand it:"
"2075" 1998 "so high hath it grown."
"2076" 1998 ""
"2077" 1998 "Now it waiteth and waiteth,--for what doth it wait? It dwelleth too"
"2078" 1998 "close to the seat of the clouds; it waiteth perhaps for the first"
"2079" 1998 "lightning?\""
"2080" 1998 ""
"2081" 1998 "When Zarathustra had said this, the youth called out with violent"
"2082" 1998 "gestures: \"Yea, Zarathustra, thou speakest the truth. My destruction"
"2083" 1998 "I longed for, when I desired to be on the height, and thou art the"
"2084" 1998 "lightning for which I waited! Lo! what have I been since thou hast"
"2085" 1998 "appeared amongst us? It is mine envy of thee that hath destroyed"
"2086" 1998 "me!\"--Thus spake the youth, and wept bitterly. Zarathustra, however, put"
"2087" 1998 "his arm about him, and led the youth away with him."
"2088" 1998 ""
"2089" 1998 "And when they had walked a while together, Zarathustra began to speak"
"2090" 1998 "thus:"
"2091" 1998 ""
"2092" 1998 "It rendeth my heart. Better than thy words express it, thine eyes tell"
"2093" 1998 "me all thy danger."
"2094" 1998 ""
"2095" 1998 "As yet thou art not free; thou still SEEKEST freedom. Too unslept hath"
"2096" 1998 "thy seeking made thee, and too wakeful."
"2097" 1998 ""
"2098" 1998 "On the open height wouldst thou be; for the stars thirsteth thy soul."
"2099" 1998 "But thy bad impulses also thirst for freedom."
"2100" 1998 ""
"2101" 1998 "Thy wild dogs want liberty; they bark for joy in their cellar when thy"
"2102" 1998 "spirit endeavoureth to open all prison doors."
"2103" 1998 ""
"2104" 1998 "Still art thou a prisoner--it seemeth to me--who deviseth liberty"
"2105" 1998 "for himself: ah! sharp becometh the soul of such prisoners, but also"
"2106" 1998 "deceitful and wicked."
"2107" 1998 ""
"2108" 1998 "To purify himself, is still necessary for the freedman of the spirit."
"2109" 1998 "Much of the prison and the mould still remaineth in him: pure hath his"
"2110" 1998 "eye still to become."
"2111" 1998 ""
"2112" 1998 "Yea, I know thy danger. But by my love and hope I conjure thee: cast not"
"2113" 1998 "thy love and hope away!"
"2114" 1998 ""
"2115" 1998 "Noble thou feelest thyself still, and noble others also feel thee still,"
"2116" 1998 "though they bear thee a grudge and cast evil looks. Know this, that to"
"2117" 1998 "everybody a noble one standeth in the way."
"2118" 1998 ""
"2119" 1998 "Also to the good, a noble one standeth in the way: and even when they"
"2120" 1998 "call him a good man, they want thereby to put him aside."
"2121" 1998 ""
"2122" 1998 "The new, would the noble man create, and a new virtue. The old, wanteth"
"2123" 1998 "the good man, and that the old should be conserved."
"2124" 1998 ""
"2125" 1998 "But it is not the danger of the noble man to turn a good man, but lest"
"2126" 1998 "he should become a blusterer, a scoffer, or a destroyer."
"2127" 1998 ""
"2128" 1998 "Ah! I have known noble ones who lost their highest hope. And then they"
"2129" 1998 "disparaged all high hopes."
"2130" 1998 ""
"2131" 1998 "Then lived they shamelessly in temporary pleasures, and beyond the day"
"2132" 1998 "had hardly an aim."
"2133" 1998 ""
"2134" 1998 "\"Spirit is also voluptuousness,\"--said they. Then broke the wings of"
"2135" 1998 "their spirit; and now it creepeth about, and defileth where it gnaweth."
"2136" 1998 ""
"2137" 1998 "Once they thought of becoming heroes; but sensualists are they now. A"
"2138" 1998 "trouble and a terror is the hero to them."
"2139" 1998 ""
"2140" 1998 "But by my love and hope I conjure thee: cast not away the hero in thy"
"2141" 1998 "soul! Maintain holy thy highest hope!--"
"2142" 1998 ""
"2143" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"2144" 1998 ""
"2145" 1998 ""
"2146" 1998 ""
"2147" 1998 ""
"2148" 1998 "IX. THE PREACHERS OF DEATH."
"2149" 1998 ""
"2150" 1998 "There are preachers of death: and the earth is full of those to whom"
"2151" 1998 "desistance from life must be preached."
"2152" 1998 ""
"2153" 1998 "Full is the earth of the superfluous; marred is life by the"
"2154" 1998 "many-too-many. May they be decoyed out of this life by the \"life"
"2155" 1998 "eternal\"!"
"2156" 1998 ""
"2157" 1998 "\"The yellow ones\": so are called the preachers of death, or \"the black"
"2158" 1998 "ones.\" But I will show them unto you in other colours besides."
"2159" 1998 ""
"2160" 1998 "There are the terrible ones who carry about in themselves the beast of"
"2161" 1998 "prey, and have no choice except lusts or self-laceration. And even their"
"2162" 1998 "lusts are self-laceration."
"2163" 1998 ""
"2164" 1998 "They have not yet become men, those terrible ones: may they preach"
"2165" 1998 "desistance from life, and pass away themselves!"
"2166" 1998 ""
"2167" 1998 "There are the spiritually consumptive ones: hardly are they born when"
"2168" 1998 "they begin to die, and long for doctrines of lassitude and renunciation."
"2169" 1998 ""
"2170" 1998 "They would fain be dead, and we should approve of their wish! Let"
"2171" 1998 "us beware of awakening those dead ones, and of damaging those living"
"2172" 1998 "coffins!"
"2173" 1998 ""
"2174" 1998 "They meet an invalid, or an old man, or a corpse--and immediately they"
"2175" 1998 "say: \"Life is refuted!\""
"2176" 1998 ""
"2177" 1998 "But they only are refuted, and their eye, which seeth only one aspect of"
"2178" 1998 "existence."
"2179" 1998 ""
"2180" 1998 "Shrouded in thick melancholy, and eager for the little casualties that"
"2181" 1998 "bring death: thus do they wait, and clench their teeth."
"2182" 1998 ""
"2183" 1998 "Or else, they grasp at sweetmeats, and mock at their childishness"
"2184" 1998 "thereby: they cling to their straw of life, and mock at their still"
"2185" 1998 "clinging to it."
"2186" 1998 ""
"2187" 1998 "Their wisdom speaketh thus: \"A fool, he who remaineth alive; but so far"
"2188" 1998 "are we fools! And that is the foolishest thing in life!\""
"2189" 1998 ""
"2190" 1998 "\"Life is only suffering\": so say others, and lie not. Then see to it"
"2191" 1998 "that YE cease! See to it that the life ceaseth which is only suffering!"
"2192" 1998 ""
"2193" 1998 "And let this be the teaching of your virtue: \"Thou shalt slay thyself!"
"2194" 1998 "Thou shalt steal away from thyself!\"--"
"2195" 1998 ""
"2196" 1998 "\"Lust is sin,\"--so say some who preach death--\"let us go apart and beget"
"2197" 1998 "no children!\""
"2198" 1998 ""
"2199" 1998 "\"Giving birth is troublesome,\"--say others--\"why still give birth? One"
"2200" 1998 "beareth only the unfortunate!\" And they also are preachers of death."
"2201" 1998 ""
"2202" 1998 "\"Pity is necessary,\"--so saith a third party. \"Take what I have! Take"
"2203" 1998 "what I am! So much less doth life bind me!\""
"2204" 1998 ""
"2205" 1998 "Were they consistently pitiful, then would they make their neighbours"
"2206" 1998 "sick of life. To be wicked--that would be their true goodness."
"2207" 1998 ""
"2208" 1998 "But they want to be rid of life; what care they if they bind others"
"2209" 1998 "still faster with their chains and gifts!--"
"2210" 1998 ""
"2211" 1998 "And ye also, to whom life is rough labour and disquiet, are ye not very"
"2212" 1998 "tired of life? Are ye not very ripe for the sermon of death?"
"2213" 1998 ""
"2214" 1998 "All ye to whom rough labour is dear, and the rapid, new, and strange--ye"
"2215" 1998 "put up with yourselves badly; your diligence is flight, and the will to"
"2216" 1998 "self-forgetfulness."
"2217" 1998 ""
"2218" 1998 "If ye believed more in life, then would ye devote yourselves less to the"
"2219" 1998 "momentary. But for waiting, ye have not enough of capacity in you--nor"
"2220" 1998 "even for idling!"
"2221" 1998 ""
"2222" 1998 "Everywhere resoundeth the voices of those who preach death; and the"
"2223" 1998 "earth is full of those to whom death hath to be preached."
"2224" 1998 ""
"2225" 1998 "Or \"life eternal\"; it is all the same to me--if only they pass away"
"2226" 1998 "quickly!--"
"2227" 1998 ""
"2228" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"2229" 1998 ""
"2230" 1998 ""
"2231" 1998 ""
"2232" 1998 ""
"2233" 1998 "X. WAR AND WARRIORS."
"2234" 1998 ""
"2235" 1998 "By our best enemies we do not want to be spared, nor by those either"
"2236" 1998 "whom we love from the very heart. So let me tell you the truth!"
"2237" 1998 ""
"2238" 1998 "My brethren in war! I love you from the very heart. I am, and was ever,"
"2239" 1998 "your counterpart. And I am also your best enemy. So let me tell you the"
"2240" 1998 "truth!"
"2241" 1998 ""
"2242" 1998 "I know the hatred and envy of your hearts. Ye are not great enough not"
"2243" 1998 "to know of hatred and envy. Then be great enough not to be ashamed of"
"2244" 1998 "them!"
"2245" 1998 ""
"2246" 1998 "And if ye cannot be saints of knowledge, then, I pray you, be at least"
"2247" 1998 "its warriors. They are the companions and forerunners of such saintship."
"2248" 1998 ""
"2249" 1998 "I see many soldiers; could I but see many warriors! \"Uniform\" one"
"2250" 1998 "calleth what they wear; may it not be uniform what they therewith hide!"
"2251" 1998 ""
"2252" 1998 "Ye shall be those whose eyes ever seek for an enemy--for YOUR enemy. And"
"2253" 1998 "with some of you there is hatred at first sight."
"2254" 1998 ""
"2255" 1998 "Your enemy shall ye seek; your war shall ye wage, and for the sake of"
"2256" 1998 "your thoughts! And if your thoughts succumb, your uprightness shall"
"2257" 1998 "still shout triumph thereby!"
"2258" 1998 ""
"2259" 1998 "Ye shall love peace as a means to new wars--and the short peace more"
"2260" 1998 "than the long."
"2261" 1998 ""
"2262" 1998 "You I advise not to work, but to fight. You I advise not to peace, but"
"2263" 1998 "to victory. Let your work be a fight, let your peace be a victory!"
"2264" 1998 ""
"2265" 1998 "One can only be silent and sit peacefully when one hath arrow and bow;"
"2266" 1998 "otherwise one prateth and quarrelleth. Let your peace be a victory!"
"2267" 1998 ""
"2268" 1998 "Ye say it is the good cause which halloweth even war? I say unto you: it"
"2269" 1998 "is the good war which halloweth every cause."
"2270" 1998 ""
"2271" 1998 "War and courage have done more great things than charity. Not your"
"2272" 1998 "sympathy, but your bravery hath hitherto saved the victims."
"2273" 1998 ""
"2274" 1998 "\"What is good?\" ye ask. To be brave is good. Let the little girls say:"
"2275" 1998 "\"To be good is what is pretty, and at the same time touching.\""
"2276" 1998 ""
"2277" 1998 "They call you heartless: but your heart is true, and I love the"
"2278" 1998 "bashfulness of your goodwill. Ye are ashamed of your flow, and others"
"2279" 1998 "are ashamed of their ebb."
"2280" 1998 ""
"2281" 1998 "Ye are ugly? Well then, my brethren, take the sublime about you, the"
"2282" 1998 "mantle of the ugly!"
"2283" 1998 ""
"2284" 1998 "And when your soul becometh great, then doth it become haughty, and in"
"2285" 1998 "your sublimity there is wickedness. I know you."
"2286" 1998 ""
"2287" 1998 "In wickedness the haughty man and the weakling meet. But they"
"2288" 1998 "misunderstand one another. I know you."
"2289" 1998 ""
"2290" 1998 "Ye shall only have enemies to be hated, but not enemies to be despised."
"2291" 1998 "Ye must be proud of your enemies; then, the successes of your enemies"
"2292" 1998 "are also your successes."
"2293" 1998 ""
"2294" 1998 "Resistance--that is the distinction of the slave. Let your distinction"
"2295" 1998 "be obedience. Let your commanding itself be obeying!"
"2296" 1998 ""
"2297" 1998 "To the good warrior soundeth \"thou shalt\" pleasanter than \"I will.\" And"
"2298" 1998 "all that is dear unto you, ye shall first have it commanded unto you."
"2299" 1998 ""
"2300" 1998 "Let your love to life be love to your highest hope; and let your highest"
"2301" 1998 "hope be the highest thought of life!"
"2302" 1998 ""
"2303" 1998 "Your highest thought, however, ye shall have it commanded unto you by"
"2304" 1998 "me--and it is this: man is something that is to be surpassed."
"2305" 1998 ""
"2306" 1998 "So live your life of obedience and of war! What matter about long life!"
"2307" 1998 "What warrior wisheth to be spared!"
"2308" 1998 ""
"2309" 1998 "I spare you not, I love you from my very heart, my brethren in war!--"
"2310" 1998 ""
"2311" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"2312" 1998 ""
"2313" 1998 ""
"2314" 1998 ""
"2315" 1998 ""
"2316" 1998 "XI. THE NEW IDOL."
"2317" 1998 ""
"2318" 1998 "Somewhere there are still peoples and herds, but not with us, my"
"2319" 1998 "brethren: here there are states."
"2320" 1998 ""
"2321" 1998 "A state? What is that? Well! open now your ears unto me, for now will I"
"2322" 1998 "say unto you my word concerning the death of peoples."
"2323" 1998 ""
"2324" 1998 "A state, is called the coldest of all cold monsters. Coldly lieth"
"2325" 1998 "it also; and this lie creepeth from its mouth: \"I, the state, am the"
"2326" 1998 "people.\""
"2327" 1998 ""
"2328" 1998 "It is a lie! Creators were they who created peoples, and hung a faith"
"2329" 1998 "and a love over them: thus they served life."
"2330" 1998 ""
"2331" 1998 "Destroyers, are they who lay snares for many, and call it the state:"
"2332" 1998 "they hang a sword and a hundred cravings over them."
"2333" 1998 ""
"2334" 1998 "Where there is still a people, there the state is not understood, but"
"2335" 1998 "hated as the evil eye, and as sin against laws and customs."
"2336" 1998 ""
"2337" 1998 "This sign I give unto you: every people speaketh its language of good"
"2338" 1998 "and evil: this its neighbour understandeth not. Its language hath it"
"2339" 1998 "devised for itself in laws and customs."
"2340" 1998 ""
"2341" 1998 "But the state lieth in all languages of good and evil; and whatever it"
"2342" 1998 "saith it lieth; and whatever it hath it hath stolen."
"2343" 1998 ""
"2344" 1998 "False is everything in it; with stolen teeth it biteth, the biting one."
"2345" 1998 "False are even its bowels."
"2346" 1998 ""
"2347" 1998 "Confusion of language of good and evil; this sign I give unto you as"
"2348" 1998 "the sign of the state. Verily, the will to death, indicateth this sign!"
"2349" 1998 "Verily, it beckoneth unto the preachers of death!"
"2350" 1998 ""
"2351" 1998 "Many too many are born: for the superfluous ones was the state devised!"
"2352" 1998 ""
"2353" 1998 "See just how it enticeth them to it, the many-too-many! How it"
"2354" 1998 "swalloweth and cheweth and recheweth them!"
"2355" 1998 ""
"2356" 1998 "\"On earth there is nothing greater than I: it is I who am the regulating"
"2357" 1998 "finger of God\"--thus roareth the monster. And not only the long-eared"
"2358" 1998 "and short-sighted fall upon their knees!"
"2359" 1998 ""
"2360" 1998 "Ah! even in your ears, ye great souls, it whispereth its gloomy lies!"
"2361" 1998 "Ah! it findeth out the rich hearts which willingly lavish themselves!"
"2362" 1998 ""
"2363" 1998 "Yea, it findeth you out too, ye conquerors of the old God! Weary ye"
"2364" 1998 "became of the conflict, and now your weariness serveth the new idol!"
"2365" 1998 ""
"2366" 1998 "Heroes and honourable ones, it would fain set up around it, the new"
"2367" 1998 "idol! Gladly it basketh in the sunshine of good consciences,--the cold"
"2368" 1998 "monster!"
"2369" 1998 ""
"2370" 1998 "Everything will it give YOU, if YE worship it, the new idol: thus it"
"2371" 1998 "purchaseth the lustre of your virtue, and the glance of your proud eyes."
"2372" 1998 ""
"2373" 1998 "It seeketh to allure by means of you, the many-too-many! Yea, a hellish"
"2374" 1998 "artifice hath here been devised, a death-horse jingling with the"
"2375" 1998 "trappings of divine honours!"
"2376" 1998 ""
"2377" 1998 "Yea, a dying for many hath here been devised, which glorifieth itself as"
"2378" 1998 "life: verily, a hearty service unto all preachers of death!"
"2379" 1998 ""
"2380" 1998 "The state, I call it, where all are poison-drinkers, the good and the"
"2381" 1998 "bad: the state, where all lose themselves, the good and the bad: the"
"2382" 1998 "state, where the slow suicide of all--is called \"life.\""
"2383" 1998 ""
"2384" 1998 "Just see these superfluous ones! They steal the works of the inventors"
"2385" 1998 "and the treasures of the wise. Culture, they call their theft--and"
"2386" 1998 "everything becometh sickness and trouble unto them!"
"2387" 1998 ""
"2388" 1998 "Just see these superfluous ones! Sick are they always; they vomit their"
"2389" 1998 "bile and call it a newspaper. They devour one another, and cannot even"
"2390" 1998 "digest themselves."
"2391" 1998 ""
"2392" 1998 "Just see these superfluous ones! Wealth they acquire and become poorer"
"2393" 1998 "thereby. Power they seek for, and above all, the lever of power, much"
"2394" 1998 "money--these impotent ones!"
"2395" 1998 ""
"2396" 1998 "See them clamber, these nimble apes! They clamber over one another, and"
"2397" 1998 "thus scuffle into the mud and the abyss."
"2398" 1998 ""
"2399" 1998 "Towards the throne they all strive: it is their madness--as if happiness"
"2400" 1998 "sat on the throne! Ofttimes sitteth filth on the throne.--and ofttimes"
"2401" 1998 "also the throne on filth."
"2402" 1998 ""
"2403" 1998 "Madmen they all seem to me, and clambering apes, and too eager. Badly"
"2404" 1998 "smelleth their idol to me, the cold monster: badly they all smell to me,"
"2405" 1998 "these idolaters."
"2406" 1998 ""
"2407" 1998 "My brethren, will ye suffocate in the fumes of their maws and appetites!"
"2408" 1998 "Better break the windows and jump into the open air!"
"2409" 1998 ""
"2410" 1998 "Do go out of the way of the bad odour! Withdraw from the idolatry of the"
"2411" 1998 "superfluous!"
"2412" 1998 ""
"2413" 1998 "Do go out of the way of the bad odour! Withdraw from the steam of these"
"2414" 1998 "human sacrifices!"
"2415" 1998 ""
"2416" 1998 "Open still remaineth the earth for great souls. Empty are still many"
"2417" 1998 "sites for lone ones and twain ones, around which floateth the odour of"
"2418" 1998 "tranquil seas."
"2419" 1998 ""
"2420" 1998 "Open still remaineth a free life for great souls. Verily, he who"
"2421" 1998 "possesseth little is so much the less possessed: blessed be moderate"
"2422" 1998 "poverty!"
"2423" 1998 ""
"2424" 1998 "There, where the state ceaseth--there only commenceth the man who is not"
"2425" 1998 "superfluous: there commenceth the song of the necessary ones, the single"
"2426" 1998 "and irreplaceable melody."
"2427" 1998 ""
"2428" 1998 "There, where the state CEASETH--pray look thither, my brethren! Do ye"
"2429" 1998 "not see it, the rainbow and the bridges of the Superman?--"
"2430" 1998 ""
"2431" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"2432" 1998 ""
"2433" 1998 ""
"2434" 1998 ""
"2435" 1998 ""
"2436" 1998 "XII. THE FLIES IN THE MARKET-PLACE."
"2437" 1998 ""
"2438" 1998 "Flee, my friend, into thy solitude! I see thee deafened with the noise"
"2439" 1998 "of the great men, and stung all over with the stings of the little ones."
"2440" 1998 ""
"2441" 1998 "Admirably do forest and rock know how to be silent with thee. Resemble"
"2442" 1998 "again the tree which thou lovest, the broad-branched one--silently and"
"2443" 1998 "attentively it o'erhangeth the sea."
"2444" 1998 ""
"2445" 1998 "Where solitude endeth, there beginneth the market-place; and where the"
"2446" 1998 "market-place beginneth, there beginneth also the noise of the great"
"2447" 1998 "actors, and the buzzing of the poison-flies."
"2448" 1998 ""
"2449" 1998 "In the world even the best things are worthless without those who"
"2450" 1998 "represent them: those representers, the people call great men."
"2451" 1998 ""
"2452" 1998 "Little do the people understand what is great--that is to say, the"
"2453" 1998 "creating agency. But they have a taste for all representers and actors"
"2454" 1998 "of great things."
"2455" 1998 ""
"2456" 1998 "Around the devisers of new values revolveth the world:--invisibly it"
"2457" 1998 "revolveth. But around the actors revolve the people and the glory: such"
"2458" 1998 "is the course of things."
"2459" 1998 ""
"2460" 1998 "Spirit, hath the actor, but little conscience of the spirit. He"
"2461" 1998 "believeth always in that wherewith he maketh believe most strongly--in"
"2462" 1998 "HIMSELF!"
"2463" 1998 ""
"2464" 1998 "Tomorrow he hath a new belief, and the day after, one still newer. Sharp"
"2465" 1998 "perceptions hath he, like the people, and changeable humours."
"2466" 1998 ""
"2467" 1998 "To upset--that meaneth with him to prove. To drive mad--that meaneth"
"2468" 1998 "with him to convince. And blood is counted by him as the best of all"
"2469" 1998 "arguments."
"2470" 1998 ""
"2471" 1998 "A truth which only glideth into fine ears, he calleth falsehood and"
"2472" 1998 "trumpery. Verily, he believeth only in Gods that make a great noise in"
"2473" 1998 "the world!"
"2474" 1998 ""
"2475" 1998 "Full of clattering buffoons is the market-place,--and the people glory"
"2476" 1998 "in their great men! These are for them the masters of the hour."
"2477" 1998 ""
"2478" 1998 "But the hour presseth them; so they press thee. And also from thee"
"2479" 1998 "they want Yea or Nay. Alas! thou wouldst set thy chair betwixt For and"
"2480" 1998 "Against?"
"2481" 1998 ""
"2482" 1998 "On account of those absolute and impatient ones, be not jealous, thou"
"2483" 1998 "lover of truth! Never yet did truth cling to the arm of an absolute one."
"2484" 1998 ""
"2485" 1998 "On account of those abrupt ones, return into thy security: only in the"
"2486" 1998 "market-place is one assailed by Yea? or Nay?"
"2487" 1998 ""
"2488" 1998 "Slow is the experience of all deep fountains: long have they to wait"
"2489" 1998 "until they know WHAT hath fallen into their depths."
"2490" 1998 ""
"2491" 1998 "Away from the market-place and from fame taketh place all that is great:"
"2492" 1998 "away from the market-Place and from fame have ever dwelt the devisers of"
"2493" 1998 "new values."
"2494" 1998 ""
"2495" 1998 "Flee, my friend, into thy solitude: I see thee stung all over by the"
"2496" 1998 "poisonous flies. Flee thither, where a rough, strong breeze bloweth!"
"2497" 1998 ""
"2498" 1998 "Flee into thy solitude! Thou hast lived too closely to the small and the"
"2499" 1998 "pitiable. Flee from their invisible vengeance! Towards thee they have"
"2500" 1998 "nothing but vengeance."
"2501" 1998 ""
"2502" 1998 "Raise no longer an arm against them! Innumerable are they, and it is not"
"2503" 1998 "thy lot to be a fly-flap."
"2504" 1998 ""
"2505" 1998 "Innumerable are the small and pitiable ones; and of many a proud"
"2506" 1998 "structure, rain-drops and weeds have been the ruin."
"2507" 1998 ""
"2508" 1998 "Thou art not stone; but already hast thou become hollow by the numerous"
"2509" 1998 "drops. Thou wilt yet break and burst by the numerous drops."
"2510" 1998 ""
"2511" 1998 "Exhausted I see thee, by poisonous flies; bleeding I see thee, and torn"
"2512" 1998 "at a hundred spots; and thy pride will not even upbraid."
"2513" 1998 ""
"2514" 1998 "Blood they would have from thee in all innocence; blood their bloodless"
"2515" 1998 "souls crave for--and they sting, therefore, in all innocence."
"2516" 1998 ""
"2517" 1998 "But thou, profound one, thou sufferest too profoundly even from small"
"2518" 1998 "wounds; and ere thou hadst recovered, the same poison-worm crawled over"
"2519" 1998 "thy hand."
"2520" 1998 ""
"2521" 1998 "Too proud art thou to kill these sweet-tooths. But take care lest it be"
"2522" 1998 "thy fate to suffer all their poisonous injustice!"
"2523" 1998 ""
"2524" 1998 "They buzz around thee also with their praise: obtrusiveness, is their"
"2525" 1998 "praise. They want to be close to thy skin and thy blood."
"2526" 1998 ""
"2527" 1998 "They flatter thee, as one flattereth a God or devil; they whimper before"
"2528" 1998 "thee, as before a God or devil. What doth it come to! Flatterers are"
"2529" 1998 "they, and whimperers, and nothing more."
"2530" 1998 ""
"2531" 1998 "Often, also, do they show themselves to thee as amiable ones. But that"
"2532" 1998 "hath ever been the prudence of the cowardly. Yea! the cowardly are wise!"
"2533" 1998 ""
"2534" 1998 "They think much about thee with their circumscribed souls--thou art"
"2535" 1998 "always suspected by them! Whatever is much thought about is at last"
"2536" 1998 "thought suspicious."
"2537" 1998 ""
"2538" 1998 "They punish thee for all thy virtues. They pardon thee in their inmost"
"2539" 1998 "hearts only--for thine errors."
"2540" 1998 ""
"2541" 1998 "Because thou art gentle and of upright character, thou sayest:"
"2542" 1998 "\"Blameless are they for their small existence.\" But their circumscribed"
"2543" 1998 "souls think: \"Blamable is all great existence.\""
"2544" 1998 ""
"2545" 1998 "Even when thou art gentle towards them, they still feel themselves"
"2546" 1998 "despised by thee; and they repay thy beneficence with secret"
"2547" 1998 "maleficence."
"2548" 1998 ""
"2549" 1998 "Thy silent pride is always counter to their taste; they rejoice if once"
"2550" 1998 "thou be humble enough to be frivolous."
"2551" 1998 ""
"2552" 1998 "What we recognise in a man, we also irritate in him. Therefore be on"
"2553" 1998 "your guard against the small ones!"
"2554" 1998 ""
"2555" 1998 "In thy presence they feel themselves small, and their baseness gleameth"
"2556" 1998 "and gloweth against thee in invisible vengeance."
"2557" 1998 ""
"2558" 1998 "Sawest thou not how often they became dumb when thou approachedst them,"
"2559" 1998 "and how their energy left them like the smoke of an extinguishing fire?"
"2560" 1998 ""
"2561" 1998 "Yea, my friend, the bad conscience art thou of thy neighbours; for they"
"2562" 1998 "are unworthy of thee. Therefore they hate thee, and would fain suck thy"
"2563" 1998 "blood."
"2564" 1998 ""
"2565" 1998 "Thy neighbours will always be poisonous flies; what is great in"
"2566" 1998 "thee--that itself must make them more poisonous, and always more"
"2567" 1998 "fly-like."
"2568" 1998 ""
"2569" 1998 "Flee, my friend, into thy solitude--and thither, where a rough strong"
"2570" 1998 "breeze bloweth. It is not thy lot to be a fly-flap.--"
"2571" 1998 ""
"2572" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"2573" 1998 ""
"2574" 1998 ""
"2575" 1998 ""
"2576" 1998 ""
"2577" 1998 "XIII. CHASTITY."
"2578" 1998 ""
"2579" 1998 "I love the forest. It is bad to live in cities: there, there are too"
"2580" 1998 "many of the lustful."
"2581" 1998 ""
"2582" 1998 "Is it not better to fall into the hands of a murderer, than into the"
"2583" 1998 "dreams of a lustful woman?"
"2584" 1998 ""
"2585" 1998 "And just look at these men: their eye saith it--they know nothing better"
"2586" 1998 "on earth than to lie with a woman."
"2587" 1998 ""
"2588" 1998 "Filth is at the bottom of their souls; and alas! if their filth hath"
"2589" 1998 "still spirit in it!"
"2590" 1998 ""
"2591" 1998 "Would that ye were perfect--at least as animals! But to animals"
"2592" 1998 "belongeth innocence."
"2593" 1998 ""
"2594" 1998 "Do I counsel you to slay your instincts? I counsel you to innocence in"
"2595" 1998 "your instincts."
"2596" 1998 ""
"2597" 1998 "Do I counsel you to chastity? Chastity is a virtue with some, but with"
"2598" 1998 "many almost a vice."
"2599" 1998 ""
"2600" 1998 "These are continent, to be sure: but doggish lust looketh enviously out"
"2601" 1998 "of all that they do."
"2602" 1998 ""
"2603" 1998 "Even into the heights of their virtue and into their cold spirit doth"
"2604" 1998 "this creature follow them, with its discord."
"2605" 1998 ""
"2606" 1998 "And how nicely can doggish lust beg for a piece of spirit, when a piece"
"2607" 1998 "of flesh is denied it!"
"2608" 1998 ""
"2609" 1998 "Ye love tragedies and all that breaketh the heart? But I am distrustful"
"2610" 1998 "of your doggish lust."
"2611" 1998 ""
"2612" 1998 "Ye have too cruel eyes, and ye look wantonly towards the sufferers."
"2613" 1998 "Hath not your lust just disguised itself and taken the name of"
"2614" 1998 "fellow-suffering?"
"2615" 1998 ""
"2616" 1998 "And also this parable give I unto you: Not a few who meant to cast out"
"2617" 1998 "their devil, went thereby into the swine themselves."
"2618" 1998 ""
"2619" 1998 "To whom chastity is difficult, it is to be dissuaded: lest it become the"
"2620" 1998 "road to hell--to filth and lust of soul."
"2621" 1998 ""
"2622" 1998 "Do I speak of filthy things? That is not the worst thing for me to do."
"2623" 1998 ""
"2624" 1998 "Not when the truth is filthy, but when it is shallow, doth the"
"2625" 1998 "discerning one go unwillingly into its waters."
"2626" 1998 ""
"2627" 1998 "Verily, there are chaste ones from their very nature; they are gentler"
"2628" 1998 "of heart, and laugh better and oftener than you."
"2629" 1998 ""
"2630" 1998 "They laugh also at chastity, and ask: \"What is chastity?"
"2631" 1998 ""
"2632" 1998 "Is chastity not folly? But the folly came unto us, and not we unto it."
"2633" 1998 ""
"2634" 1998 "We offered that guest harbour and heart: now it dwelleth with us--let it"
"2635" 1998 "stay as long as it will!\"--"
"2636" 1998 ""
"2637" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"2638" 1998 ""
"2639" 1998 ""
"2640" 1998 ""
"2641" 1998 ""
"2642" 1998 "XIV. THE FRIEND."
"2643" 1998 ""
"2644" 1998 "\"One, is always too many about me\"--thinketh the anchorite. \"Always once"
"2645" 1998 "one--that maketh two in the long run!\""
"2646" 1998 ""
"2647" 1998 "I and me are always too earnestly in conversation: how could it be"
"2648" 1998 "endured, if there were not a friend?"
"2649" 1998 ""
"2650" 1998 "The friend of the anchorite is always the third one: the third one is"
"2651" 1998 "the cork which preventeth the conversation of the two sinking into the"
"2652" 1998 "depth."
"2653" 1998 ""
"2654" 1998 "Ah! there are too many depths for all anchorites. Therefore, do they"
"2655" 1998 "long so much for a friend, and for his elevation."
"2656" 1998 ""
"2657" 1998 "Our faith in others betrayeth wherein we would fain have faith in"
"2658" 1998 "ourselves. Our longing for a friend is our betrayer."
"2659" 1998 ""
"2660" 1998 "And often with our love we want merely to overleap envy. And often we"
"2661" 1998 "attack and make ourselves enemies, to conceal that we are vulnerable."
"2662" 1998 ""
"2663" 1998 "\"Be at least mine enemy!\"--thus speaketh the true reverence, which doth"
"2664" 1998 "not venture to solicit friendship."
"2665" 1998 ""
"2666" 1998 "If one would have a friend, then must one also be willing to wage war"
"2667" 1998 "for him: and in order to wage war, one must be CAPABLE of being an"
"2668" 1998 "enemy."
"2669" 1998 ""
"2670" 1998 "One ought still to honour the enemy in one's friend. Canst thou go nigh"
"2671" 1998 "unto thy friend, and not go over to him?"
"2672" 1998 ""
"2673" 1998 "In one's friend one shall have one's best enemy. Thou shalt be closest"
"2674" 1998 "unto him with thy heart when thou withstandest him."
"2675" 1998 ""
"2676" 1998 "Thou wouldst wear no raiment before thy friend? It is in honour of thy"
"2677" 1998 "friend that thou showest thyself to him as thou art? But he wisheth thee"
"2678" 1998 "to the devil on that account!"
"2679" 1998 ""
"2680" 1998 "He who maketh no secret of himself shocketh: so much reason have ye"
"2681" 1998 "to fear nakedness! Aye, if ye were Gods, ye could then be ashamed of"
"2682" 1998 "clothing!"
"2683" 1998 ""
"2684" 1998 "Thou canst not adorn thyself fine enough for thy friend; for thou shalt"
"2685" 1998 "be unto him an arrow and a longing for the Superman."
"2686" 1998 ""
"2687" 1998 "Sawest thou ever thy friend asleep--to know how he looketh? What is"
"2688" 1998 "usually the countenance of thy friend? It is thine own countenance, in a"
"2689" 1998 "coarse and imperfect mirror."
"2690" 1998 ""
"2691" 1998 "Sawest thou ever thy friend asleep? Wert thou not dismayed at thy friend"
"2692" 1998 "looking so? O my friend, man is something that hath to be surpassed."
"2693" 1998 ""
"2694" 1998 "In divining and keeping silence shall the friend be a master: not"
"2695" 1998 "everything must thou wish to see. Thy dream shall disclose unto thee"
"2696" 1998 "what thy friend doeth when awake."
"2697" 1998 ""
"2698" 1998 "Let thy pity be a divining: to know first if thy friend wanteth pity."
"2699" 1998 "Perhaps he loveth in thee the unmoved eye, and the look of eternity."
"2700" 1998 ""
"2701" 1998 "Let thy pity for thy friend be hid under a hard shell; thou shalt bite"
"2702" 1998 "out a tooth upon it. Thus will it have delicacy and sweetness."
"2703" 1998 ""
"2704" 1998 "Art thou pure air and solitude and bread and medicine to thy friend?"
"2705" 1998 "Many a one cannot loosen his own fetters, but is nevertheless his"
"2706" 1998 "friend's emancipator."
"2707" 1998 ""
"2708" 1998 "Art thou a slave? Then thou canst not be a friend. Art thou a tyrant?"
"2709" 1998 "Then thou canst not have friends."
"2710" 1998 ""
"2711" 1998 "Far too long hath there been a slave and a tyrant concealed in woman."
"2712" 1998 "On that account woman is not yet capable of friendship: she knoweth only"
"2713" 1998 "love."
"2714" 1998 ""
"2715" 1998 "In woman's love there is injustice and blindness to all she doth not"
"2716" 1998 "love. And even in woman's conscious love, there is still always surprise"
"2717" 1998 "and lightning and night, along with the light."
"2718" 1998 ""
"2719" 1998 "As yet woman is not capable of friendship: women are still cats, and"
"2720" 1998 "birds. Or at the best, cows."
"2721" 1998 ""
"2722" 1998 "As yet woman is not capable of friendship. But tell me, ye men, who of"
"2723" 1998 "you are capable of friendship?"
"2724" 1998 ""
"2725" 1998 "Oh! your poverty, ye men, and your sordidness of soul! As much as ye"
"2726" 1998 "give to your friend, will I give even to my foe, and will not have"
"2727" 1998 "become poorer thereby."
"2728" 1998 ""
"2729" 1998 "There is comradeship: may there be friendship!"
"2730" 1998 ""
"2731" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"2732" 1998 ""
"2733" 1998 ""
"2734" 1998 ""
"2735" 1998 ""
"2736" 1998 "XV. THE THOUSAND AND ONE GOALS."
"2737" 1998 ""
"2738" 1998 "Many lands saw Zarathustra, and many peoples: thus he discovered the"
"2739" 1998 "good and bad of many peoples. No greater power did Zarathustra find on"
"2740" 1998 "earth than good and bad."
"2741" 1998 ""
"2742" 1998 "No people could live without first valuing; if a people will maintain"
"2743" 1998 "itself, however, it must not value as its neighbour valueth."
"2744" 1998 ""
"2745" 1998 "Much that passed for good with one people was regarded with scorn and"
"2746" 1998 "contempt by another: thus I found it. Much found I here called bad,"
"2747" 1998 "which was there decked with purple honours."
"2748" 1998 ""
"2749" 1998 "Never did the one neighbour understand the other: ever did his soul"
"2750" 1998 "marvel at his neighbour's delusion and wickedness."
"2751" 1998 ""
"2752" 1998 "A table of excellencies hangeth over every people. Lo! it is the table"
"2753" 1998 "of their triumphs; lo! it is the voice of their Will to Power."
"2754" 1998 ""
"2755" 1998 "It is laudable, what they think hard; what is indispensable and hard"
"2756" 1998 "they call good; and what relieveth in the direst distress, the unique"
"2757" 1998 "and hardest of all,--they extol as holy."
"2758" 1998 ""
"2759" 1998 "Whatever maketh them rule and conquer and shine, to the dismay and envy"
"2760" 1998 "of their neighbours, they regard as the high and foremost thing, the"
"2761" 1998 "test and the meaning of all else."
"2762" 1998 ""
"2763" 1998 "Verily, my brother, if thou knewest but a people's need, its land,"
"2764" 1998 "its sky, and its neighbour, then wouldst thou divine the law of its"
"2765" 1998 "surmountings, and why it climbeth up that ladder to its hope."
"2766" 1998 ""
"2767" 1998 "\"Always shalt thou be the foremost and prominent above others: no one"
"2768" 1998 "shall thy jealous soul love, except a friend\"--that made the soul of a"
"2769" 1998 "Greek thrill: thereby went he his way to greatness."
"2770" 1998 ""
"2771" 1998 "\"To speak truth, and be skilful with bow and arrow\"--so seemed it alike"
"2772" 1998 "pleasing and hard to the people from whom cometh my name--the name which"
"2773" 1998 "is alike pleasing and hard to me."
"2774" 1998 ""
"2775" 1998 "\"To honour father and mother, and from the root of the soul to do their"
"2776" 1998 "will\"--this table of surmounting hung another people over them, and"
"2777" 1998 "became powerful and permanent thereby."
"2778" 1998 ""
"2779" 1998 "\"To have fidelity, and for the sake of fidelity to risk honour and"
"2780" 1998 "blood, even in evil and dangerous courses\"--teaching itself so, another"
"2781" 1998 "people mastered itself, and thus mastering itself, became pregnant and"
"2782" 1998 "heavy with great hopes."
"2783" 1998 ""
"2784" 1998 "Verily, men have given unto themselves all their good and bad. Verily,"
"2785" 1998 "they took it not, they found it not, it came not unto them as a voice"
"2786" 1998 "from heaven."
"2787" 1998 ""
"2788" 1998 "Values did man only assign to things in order to maintain himself--he"
"2789" 1998 "created only the significance of things, a human significance!"
"2790" 1998 "Therefore, calleth he himself \"man,\" that is, the valuator."
"2791" 1998 ""
"2792" 1998 "Valuing is creating: hear it, ye creating ones! Valuation itself is the"
"2793" 1998 "treasure and jewel of the valued things."
"2794" 1998 ""
"2795" 1998 "Through valuation only is there value; and without valuation the nut of"
"2796" 1998 "existence would be hollow. Hear it, ye creating ones!"
"2797" 1998 ""
"2798" 1998 "Change of values--that is, change of the creating ones. Always doth he"
"2799" 1998 "destroy who hath to be a creator."
"2800" 1998 ""
"2801" 1998 "Creating ones were first of all peoples, and only in late times"
"2802" 1998 "individuals; verily, the individual himself is still the latest"
"2803" 1998 "creation."
"2804" 1998 ""
"2805" 1998 "Peoples once hung over them tables of the good. Love which would rule"
"2806" 1998 "and love which would obey, created for themselves such tables."
"2807" 1998 ""
"2808" 1998 "Older is the pleasure in the herd than the pleasure in the ego: and as"
"2809" 1998 "long as the good conscience is for the herd, the bad conscience only"
"2810" 1998 "saith: ego."
"2811" 1998 ""
"2812" 1998 "Verily, the crafty ego, the loveless one, that seeketh its advantage in"
"2813" 1998 "the advantage of many--it is not the origin of the herd, but its ruin."
"2814" 1998 ""
"2815" 1998 "Loving ones, was it always, and creating ones, that created good and"
"2816" 1998 "bad. Fire of love gloweth in the names of all the virtues, and fire of"
"2817" 1998 "wrath."
"2818" 1998 ""
"2819" 1998 "Many lands saw Zarathustra, and many peoples: no greater power did"
"2820" 1998 "Zarathustra find on earth than the creations of the loving ones--\"good\""
"2821" 1998 "and \"bad\" are they called."
"2822" 1998 ""
"2823" 1998 "Verily, a prodigy is this power of praising and blaming. Tell me, ye"
"2824" 1998 "brethren, who will master it for me? Who will put a fetter upon the"
"2825" 1998 "thousand necks of this animal?"
"2826" 1998 ""
"2827" 1998 "A thousand goals have there been hitherto, for a thousand peoples have"
"2828" 1998 "there been. Only the fetter for the thousand necks is still lacking;"
"2829" 1998 "there is lacking the one goal. As yet humanity hath not a goal."
"2830" 1998 ""
"2831" 1998 "But pray tell me, my brethren, if the goal of humanity be still lacking,"
"2832" 1998 "is there not also still lacking--humanity itself?--"
"2833" 1998 ""
"2834" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"2835" 1998 ""
"2836" 1998 ""
"2837" 1998 ""
"2838" 1998 ""
"2839" 1998 "XVI. NEIGHBOUR-LOVE."
"2840" 1998 ""
"2841" 1998 "Ye crowd around your neighbour, and have fine words for it. But I say"
"2842" 1998 "unto you: your neighbour-love is your bad love of yourselves."
"2843" 1998 ""
"2844" 1998 "Ye flee unto your neighbour from yourselves, and would fain make a"
"2845" 1998 "virtue thereof: but I fathom your \"unselfishness.\""
"2846" 1998 ""
"2847" 1998 "The THOU is older than the _I_; the THOU hath been consecrated, but not"
"2848" 1998 "yet the _I_: so man presseth nigh unto his neighbour."
"2849" 1998 ""
"2850" 1998 "Do I advise you to neighbour-love? Rather do I advise you to"
"2851" 1998 "neighbour-flight and to furthest love!"
"2852" 1998 ""
"2853" 1998 "Higher than love to your neighbour is love to the furthest and future"
"2854" 1998 "ones; higher still than love to men, is love to things and phantoms."
"2855" 1998 ""
"2856" 1998 "The phantom that runneth on before thee, my brother, is fairer than"
"2857" 1998 "thou; why dost thou not give unto it thy flesh and thy bones? But thou"
"2858" 1998 "fearest, and runnest unto thy neighbour."
"2859" 1998 ""
"2860" 1998 "Ye cannot endure it with yourselves, and do not love yourselves"
"2861" 1998 "sufficiently: so ye seek to mislead your neighbour into love, and would"
"2862" 1998 "fain gild yourselves with his error."
"2863" 1998 ""
"2864" 1998 "Would that ye could not endure it with any kind of near ones, or their"
"2865" 1998 "neighbours; then would ye have to create your friend and his overflowing"
"2866" 1998 "heart out of yourselves."
"2867" 1998 ""
"2868" 1998 "Ye call in a witness when ye want to speak well of yourselves; and"
"2869" 1998 "when ye have misled him to think well of you, ye also think well of"
"2870" 1998 "yourselves."
"2871" 1998 ""
"2872" 1998 "Not only doth he lie, who speaketh contrary to his knowledge, but more"
"2873" 1998 "so, he who speaketh contrary to his ignorance. And thus speak ye"
"2874" 1998 "of yourselves in your intercourse, and belie your neighbour with"
"2875" 1998 "yourselves."
"2876" 1998 ""
"2877" 1998 "Thus saith the fool: \"Association with men spoileth the character,"
"2878" 1998 "especially when one hath none.\""
"2879" 1998 ""
"2880" 1998 "The one goeth to his neighbour because he seeketh himself, and the other"
"2881" 1998 "because he would fain lose himself. Your bad love to yourselves maketh"
"2882" 1998 "solitude a prison to you."
"2883" 1998 ""
"2884" 1998 "The furthest ones are they who pay for your love to the near ones; and"
"2885" 1998 "when there are but five of you together, a sixth must always die."
"2886" 1998 ""
"2887" 1998 "I love not your festivals either: too many actors found I there, and"
"2888" 1998 "even the spectators often behaved like actors."
"2889" 1998 ""
"2890" 1998 "Not the neighbour do I teach you, but the friend. Let the friend be the"
"2891" 1998 "festival of the earth to you, and a foretaste of the Superman."
"2892" 1998 ""
"2893" 1998 "I teach you the friend and his overflowing heart. But one must know how"
"2894" 1998 "to be a sponge, if one would be loved by overflowing hearts."
"2895" 1998 ""
"2896" 1998 "I teach you the friend in whom the world standeth complete, a capsule"
"2897" 1998 "of the good,--the creating friend, who hath always a complete world to"
"2898" 1998 "bestow."
"2899" 1998 ""
"2900" 1998 "And as the world unrolled itself for him, so rolleth it together again"
"2901" 1998 "for him in rings, as the growth of good through evil, as the growth of"
"2902" 1998 "purpose out of chance."
"2903" 1998 ""
"2904" 1998 "Let the future and the furthest be the motive of thy to-day; in thy"
"2905" 1998 "friend shalt thou love the Superman as thy motive."
"2906" 1998 ""
"2907" 1998 "My brethren, I advise you not to neighbour-love--I advise you to"
"2908" 1998 "furthest love!--"
"2909" 1998 ""
"2910" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"2911" 1998 ""
"2912" 1998 ""
"2913" 1998 ""
"2914" 1998 ""
"2915" 1998 "XVII. THE WAY OF THE CREATING ONE."
"2916" 1998 ""
"2917" 1998 "Wouldst thou go into isolation, my brother? Wouldst thou seek the way"
"2918" 1998 "unto thyself? Tarry yet a little and hearken unto me."
"2919" 1998 ""
"2920" 1998 "\"He who seeketh may easily get lost himself. All isolation is wrong\": so"
"2921" 1998 "say the herd. And long didst thou belong to the herd."
"2922" 1998 ""
"2923" 1998 "The voice of the herd will still echo in thee. And when thou sayest,"
"2924" 1998 "\"I have no longer a conscience in common with you,\" then will it be a"
"2925" 1998 "plaint and a pain."
"2926" 1998 ""
"2927" 1998 "Lo, that pain itself did the same conscience produce; and the last gleam"
"2928" 1998 "of that conscience still gloweth on thine affliction."
"2929" 1998 ""
"2930" 1998 "But thou wouldst go the way of thine affliction, which is the way unto"
"2931" 1998 "thyself? Then show me thine authority and thy strength to do so!"
"2932" 1998 ""
"2933" 1998 "Art thou a new strength and a new authority? A first motion? A"
"2934" 1998 "self-rolling wheel? Canst thou also compel stars to revolve around thee?"
"2935" 1998 ""
"2936" 1998 "Alas! there is so much lusting for loftiness! There are so many"
"2937" 1998 "convulsions of the ambitions! Show me that thou art not a lusting and"
"2938" 1998 "ambitious one!"
"2939" 1998 ""
"2940" 1998 "Alas! there are so many great thoughts that do nothing more than the"
"2941" 1998 "bellows: they inflate, and make emptier than ever."
"2942" 1998 ""
"2943" 1998 "Free, dost thou call thyself? Thy ruling thought would I hear of, and"
"2944" 1998 "not that thou hast escaped from a yoke."
"2945" 1998 ""
"2946" 1998 "Art thou one ENTITLED to escape from a yoke? Many a one hath cast away"
"2947" 1998 "his final worth when he hath cast away his servitude."
"2948" 1998 ""
"2949" 1998 "Free from what? What doth that matter to Zarathustra! Clearly, however,"
"2950" 1998 "shall thine eye show unto me: free FOR WHAT?"
"2951" 1998 ""
"2952" 1998 "Canst thou give unto thyself thy bad and thy good, and set up thy will"
"2953" 1998 "as a law over thee? Canst thou be judge for thyself, and avenger of thy"
"2954" 1998 "law?"
"2955" 1998 ""
"2956" 1998 "Terrible is aloneness with the judge and avenger of one's own law."
"2957" 1998 "Thus is a star projected into desert space, and into the icy breath of"
"2958" 1998 "aloneness."
"2959" 1998 ""
"2960" 1998 "To-day sufferest thou still from the multitude, thou individual; to-day"
"2961" 1998 "hast thou still thy courage unabated, and thy hopes."
"2962" 1998 ""
"2963" 1998 "But one day will the solitude weary thee; one day will thy pride yield,"
"2964" 1998 "and thy courage quail. Thou wilt one day cry: \"I am alone!\""
"2965" 1998 ""
"2966" 1998 "One day wilt thou see no longer thy loftiness, and see too closely thy"
"2967" 1998 "lowliness; thy sublimity itself will frighten thee as a phantom. Thou"
"2968" 1998 "wilt one day cry: \"All is false!\""
"2969" 1998 ""
"2970" 1998 "There are feelings which seek to slay the lonesome one; if they do not"
"2971" 1998 "succeed, then must they themselves die! But art thou capable of it--to"
"2972" 1998 "be a murderer?"
"2973" 1998 ""
"2974" 1998 "Hast thou ever known, my brother, the word \"disdain\"? And the anguish of"
"2975" 1998 "thy justice in being just to those that disdain thee?"
"2976" 1998 ""
"2977" 1998 "Thou forcest many to think differently about thee; that, charge they"
"2978" 1998 "heavily to thine account. Thou camest nigh unto them, and yet wentest"
"2979" 1998 "past: for that they never forgive thee."
"2980" 1998 ""
"2981" 1998 "Thou goest beyond them: but the higher thou risest, the smaller doth the"
"2982" 1998 "eye of envy see thee. Most of all, however, is the flying one hated."
"2983" 1998 ""
"2984" 1998 "\"How could ye be just unto me!\"--must thou say--\"I choose your injustice"
"2985" 1998 "as my allotted portion.\""
"2986" 1998 ""
"2987" 1998 "Injustice and filth cast they at the lonesome one: but, my brother, if"
"2988" 1998 "thou wouldst be a star, thou must shine for them none the less on that"
"2989" 1998 "account!"
"2990" 1998 ""
"2991" 1998 "And be on thy guard against the good and just! They would fain crucify"
"2992" 1998 "those who devise their own virtue--they hate the lonesome ones."
"2993" 1998 ""
"2994" 1998 "Be on thy guard, also, against holy simplicity! All is unholy to it that"
"2995" 1998 "is not simple; fain, likewise, would it play with the fire--of the fagot"
"2996" 1998 "and stake."
"2997" 1998 ""
"2998" 1998 "And be on thy guard, also, against the assaults of thy love! Too readily"
"2999" 1998 "doth the recluse reach his hand to any one who meeteth him."
"3000" 1998 ""
"3001" 1998 "To many a one mayest thou not give thy hand, but only thy paw; and I"
"3002" 1998 "wish thy paw also to have claws."
"3003" 1998 ""
"3004" 1998 "But the worst enemy thou canst meet, wilt thou thyself always be; thou"
"3005" 1998 "waylayest thyself in caverns and forests."
"3006" 1998 ""
"3007" 1998 "Thou lonesome one, thou goest the way to thyself! And past thyself and"
"3008" 1998 "thy seven devils leadeth thy way!"
"3009" 1998 ""
"3010" 1998 "A heretic wilt thou be to thyself, and a wizard and a sooth-sayer, and a"
"3011" 1998 "fool, and a doubter, and a reprobate, and a villain."
"3012" 1998 ""
"3013" 1998 "Ready must thou be to burn thyself in thine own flame; how couldst thou"
"3014" 1998 "become new if thou have not first become ashes!"
"3015" 1998 ""
"3016" 1998 "Thou lonesome one, thou goest the way of the creating one: a God wilt"
"3017" 1998 "thou create for thyself out of thy seven devils!"
"3018" 1998 ""
"3019" 1998 "Thou lonesome one, thou goest the way of the loving one: thou lovest"
"3020" 1998 "thyself, and on that account despisest thou thyself, as only the loving"
"3021" 1998 "ones despise."
"3022" 1998 ""
"3023" 1998 "To create, desireth the loving one, because he despiseth! What knoweth"
"3024" 1998 "he of love who hath not been obliged to despise just what he loved!"
"3025" 1998 ""
"3026" 1998 "With thy love, go into thine isolation, my brother, and with thy"
"3027" 1998 "creating; and late only will justice limp after thee."
"3028" 1998 ""
"3029" 1998 "With my tears, go into thine isolation, my brother. I love him who"
"3030" 1998 "seeketh to create beyond himself, and thus succumbeth.--"
"3031" 1998 ""
"3032" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"3033" 1998 ""
"3034" 1998 ""
"3035" 1998 ""
"3036" 1998 ""
"3037" 1998 "XVIII. OLD AND YOUNG WOMEN."
"3038" 1998 ""
"3039" 1998 "\"Why stealest thou along so furtively in the twilight, Zarathustra? And"
"3040" 1998 "what hidest thou so carefully under thy mantle?"
"3041" 1998 ""
"3042" 1998 "Is it a treasure that hath been given thee? Or a child that hath been"
"3043" 1998 "born thee? Or goest thou thyself on a thief's errand, thou friend of the"
"3044" 1998 "evil?\"--"
"3045" 1998 ""
"3046" 1998 "Verily, my brother, said Zarathustra, it is a treasure that hath been"
"3047" 1998 "given me: it is a little truth which I carry."
"3048" 1998 ""
"3049" 1998 "But it is naughty, like a young child; and if I hold not its mouth, it"
"3050" 1998 "screameth too loudly."
"3051" 1998 ""
"3052" 1998 "As I went on my way alone to-day, at the hour when the sun declineth,"
"3053" 1998 "there met me an old woman, and she spake thus unto my soul:"
"3054" 1998 ""
"3055" 1998 "\"Much hath Zarathustra spoken also to us women, but never spake he unto"
"3056" 1998 "us concerning woman.\""
"3057" 1998 ""
"3058" 1998 "And I answered her: \"Concerning woman, one should only talk unto men.\""
"3059" 1998 ""
"3060" 1998 "\"Talk also unto me of woman,\" said she; \"I am old enough to forget it"
"3061" 1998 "presently.\""
"3062" 1998 ""
"3063" 1998 "And I obliged the old woman and spake thus unto her:"
"3064" 1998 ""
"3065" 1998 "Everything in woman is a riddle, and everything in woman hath one"
"3066" 1998 "solution--it is called pregnancy."
"3067" 1998 ""
"3068" 1998 "Man is for woman a means: the purpose is always the child. But what is"
"3069" 1998 "woman for man?"
"3070" 1998 ""
"3071" 1998 "Two different things wanteth the true man: danger and diversion."
"3072" 1998 "Therefore wanteth he woman, as the most dangerous plaything."
"3073" 1998 ""
"3074" 1998 "Man shall be trained for war, and woman for the recreation of the"
"3075" 1998 "warrior: all else is folly."
"3076" 1998 ""
"3077" 1998 "Too sweet fruits--these the warrior liketh not. Therefore liketh he"
"3078" 1998 "woman;--bitter is even the sweetest woman."
"3079" 1998 ""
"3080" 1998 "Better than man doth woman understand children, but man is more childish"
"3081" 1998 "than woman."
"3082" 1998 ""
"3083" 1998 "In the true man there is a child hidden: it wanteth to play. Up then, ye"
"3084" 1998 "women, and discover the child in man!"
"3085" 1998 ""
"3086" 1998 "A plaything let woman be, pure and fine like the precious stone,"
"3087" 1998 "illumined with the virtues of a world not yet come."
"3088" 1998 ""
"3089" 1998 "Let the beam of a star shine in your love! Let your hope say: \"May I"
"3090" 1998 "bear the Superman!\""
"3091" 1998 ""
"3092" 1998 "In your love let there be valour! With your love shall ye assail him who"
"3093" 1998 "inspireth you with fear!"
"3094" 1998 ""
"3095" 1998 "In your love be your honour! Little doth woman understand otherwise"
"3096" 1998 "about honour. But let this be your honour: always to love more than ye"
"3097" 1998 "are loved, and never be the second."
"3098" 1998 ""
"3099" 1998 "Let man fear woman when she loveth: then maketh she every sacrifice, and"
"3100" 1998 "everything else she regardeth as worthless."
"3101" 1998 ""
"3102" 1998 "Let man fear woman when she hateth: for man in his innermost soul is"
"3103" 1998 "merely evil; woman, however, is mean."
"3104" 1998 ""
"3105" 1998 "Whom hateth woman most?--Thus spake the iron to the loadstone: \"I hate"
"3106" 1998 "thee most, because thou attractest, but art too weak to draw unto thee.\""
"3107" 1998 ""
"3108" 1998 "The happiness of man is, \"I will.\" The happiness of woman is, \"He will.\""
"3109" 1998 ""
"3110" 1998 "\"Lo! now hath the world become perfect!\"--thus thinketh every woman when"
"3111" 1998 "she obeyeth with all her love."
"3112" 1998 ""
"3113" 1998 "Obey, must the woman, and find a depth for her surface. Surface, is"
"3114" 1998 "woman's soul, a mobile, stormy film on shallow water."
"3115" 1998 ""
"3116" 1998 "Man's soul, however, is deep, its current gusheth in subterranean"
"3117" 1998 "caverns: woman surmiseth its force, but comprehendeth it not.--"
"3118" 1998 ""
"3119" 1998 "Then answered me the old woman: \"Many fine things hath Zarathustra said,"
"3120" 1998 "especially for those who are young enough for them."
"3121" 1998 ""
"3122" 1998 "Strange! Zarathustra knoweth little about woman, and yet he is right"
"3123" 1998 "about them! Doth this happen, because with women nothing is impossible?"
"3124" 1998 ""
"3125" 1998 "And now accept a little truth by way of thanks! I am old enough for it!"
"3126" 1998 ""
"3127" 1998 "Swaddle it up and hold its mouth: otherwise it will scream too loudly,"
"3128" 1998 "the little truth.\""
"3129" 1998 ""
"3130" 1998 "\"Give me, woman, thy little truth!\" said I. And thus spake the old"
"3131" 1998 "woman:"
"3132" 1998 ""
"3133" 1998 "\"Thou goest to women? Do not forget thy whip!\"--"
"3134" 1998 ""
"3135" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"3136" 1998 ""
"3137" 1998 ""
"3138" 1998 ""
"3139" 1998 ""
"3140" 1998 "XIX. THE BITE OF THE ADDER."
"3141" 1998 ""
"3142" 1998 "One day had Zarathustra fallen asleep under a fig-tree, owing to the"
"3143" 1998 "heat, with his arms over his face. And there came an adder and bit him"
"3144" 1998 "in the neck, so that Zarathustra screamed with pain. When he had"
"3145" 1998 "taken his arm from his face he looked at the serpent; and then did it"
"3146" 1998 "recognise the eyes of Zarathustra, wriggled awkwardly, and tried to get"
"3147" 1998 "away. \"Not at all,\" said Zarathustra, \"as yet hast thou not received"
"3148" 1998 "my thanks! Thou hast awakened me in time; my journey is yet long.\""
"3149" 1998 "\"Thy journey is short,\" said the adder sadly; \"my poison is fatal.\""
"3150" 1998 "Zarathustra smiled. \"When did ever a dragon die of a serpent's"
"3151" 1998 "poison?\"--said he. \"But take thy poison back! Thou art not rich enough"
"3152" 1998 "to present it to me.\" Then fell the adder again on his neck, and licked"
"3153" 1998 "his wound."
"3154" 1998 ""
"3155" 1998 "When Zarathustra once told this to his disciples they asked him:"
"3156" 1998 "\"And what, O Zarathustra, is the moral of thy story?\" And Zarathustra"
"3157" 1998 "answered them thus:"
"3158" 1998 ""
"3159" 1998 "The destroyer of morality, the good and just call me: my story is"
"3160" 1998 "immoral."
"3161" 1998 ""
"3162" 1998 "When, however, ye have an enemy, then return him not good for evil: for"
"3163" 1998 "that would abash him. But prove that he hath done something good to you."
"3164" 1998 ""
"3165" 1998 "And rather be angry than abash any one! And when ye are cursed, it"
"3166" 1998 "pleaseth me not that ye should then desire to bless. Rather curse a"
"3167" 1998 "little also!"
"3168" 1998 ""
"3169" 1998 "And should a great injustice befall you, then do quickly five small ones"
"3170" 1998 "besides. Hideous to behold is he on whom injustice presseth alone."
"3171" 1998 ""
"3172" 1998 "Did ye ever know this? Shared injustice is half justice. And he who can"
"3173" 1998 "bear it, shall take the injustice upon himself!"
"3174" 1998 ""
"3175" 1998 "A small revenge is humaner than no revenge at all. And if the punishment"
"3176" 1998 "be not also a right and an honour to the transgressor, I do not like"
"3177" 1998 "your punishing."
"3178" 1998 ""
"3179" 1998 "Nobler is it to own oneself in the wrong than to establish one's right,"
"3180" 1998 "especially if one be in the right. Only, one must be rich enough to do"
"3181" 1998 "so."
"3182" 1998 ""
"3183" 1998 "I do not like your cold justice; out of the eye of your judges there"
"3184" 1998 "always glanceth the executioner and his cold steel."
"3185" 1998 ""
"3186" 1998 "Tell me: where find we justice, which is love with seeing eyes?"
"3187" 1998 ""
"3188" 1998 "Devise me, then, the love which not only beareth all punishment, but"
"3189" 1998 "also all guilt!"
"3190" 1998 ""
"3191" 1998 "Devise me, then, the justice which acquitteth every one except the"
"3192" 1998 "judge!"
"3193" 1998 ""
"3194" 1998 "And would ye hear this likewise? To him who seeketh to be just from the"
"3195" 1998 "heart, even the lie becometh philanthropy."
"3196" 1998 ""
"3197" 1998 "But how could I be just from the heart! How can I give every one his"
"3198" 1998 "own! Let this be enough for me: I give unto every one mine own."
"3199" 1998 ""
"3200" 1998 "Finally, my brethren, guard against doing wrong to any anchorite. How"
"3201" 1998 "could an anchorite forget! How could he requite!"
"3202" 1998 ""
"3203" 1998 "Like a deep well is an anchorite. Easy is it to throw in a stone: if"
"3204" 1998 "it should sink to the bottom, however, tell me, who will bring it out"
"3205" 1998 "again?"
"3206" 1998 ""
"3207" 1998 "Guard against injuring the anchorite! If ye have done so, however, well"
"3208" 1998 "then, kill him also!--"
"3209" 1998 ""
"3210" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"3211" 1998 ""
"3212" 1998 ""
"3213" 1998 ""
"3214" 1998 ""
"3215" 1998 "XX. CHILD AND MARRIAGE."
"3216" 1998 ""
"3217" 1998 "I have a question for thee alone, my brother: like a sounding-lead, cast"
"3218" 1998 "I this question into thy soul, that I may know its depth."
"3219" 1998 ""
"3220" 1998 "Thou art young, and desirest child and marriage. But I ask thee: Art"
"3221" 1998 "thou a man ENTITLED to desire a child?"
"3222" 1998 ""
"3223" 1998 "Art thou the victorious one, the self-conqueror, the ruler of thy"
"3224" 1998 "passions, the master of thy virtues? Thus do I ask thee."
"3225" 1998 ""
"3226" 1998 "Or doth the animal speak in thy wish, and necessity? Or isolation? Or"
"3227" 1998 "discord in thee?"
"3228" 1998 ""
"3229" 1998 "I would have thy victory and freedom long for a child. Living monuments"
"3230" 1998 "shalt thou build to thy victory and emancipation."
"3231" 1998 ""
"3232" 1998 "Beyond thyself shalt thou build. But first of all must thou be built"
"3233" 1998 "thyself, rectangular in body and soul."
"3234" 1998 ""
"3235" 1998 "Not only onward shalt thou propagate thyself, but upward! For that"
"3236" 1998 "purpose may the garden of marriage help thee!"
"3237" 1998 ""
"3238" 1998 "A higher body shalt thou create, a first movement, a spontaneously"
"3239" 1998 "rolling wheel--a creating one shalt thou create."
"3240" 1998 ""
"3241" 1998 "Marriage: so call I the will of the twain to create the one that is"
"3242" 1998 "more than those who created it. The reverence for one another, as those"
"3243" 1998 "exercising such a will, call I marriage."
"3244" 1998 ""
"3245" 1998 "Let this be the significance and the truth of thy marriage. But that"
"3246" 1998 "which the many-too-many call marriage, those superfluous ones--ah, what"
"3247" 1998 "shall I call it?"
"3248" 1998 ""
"3249" 1998 "Ah, the poverty of soul in the twain! Ah, the filth of soul in the"
"3250" 1998 "twain! Ah, the pitiable self-complacency in the twain!"
"3251" 1998 ""
"3252" 1998 "Marriage they call it all; and they say their marriages are made in"
"3253" 1998 "heaven."
"3254" 1998 ""
"3255" 1998 "Well, I do not like it, that heaven of the superfluous! No, I do not"
"3256" 1998 "like them, those animals tangled in the heavenly toils!"
"3257" 1998 ""
"3258" 1998 "Far from me also be the God who limpeth thither to bless what he hath"
"3259" 1998 "not matched!"
"3260" 1998 ""
"3261" 1998 "Laugh not at such marriages! What child hath not had reason to weep over"
"3262" 1998 "its parents?"
"3263" 1998 ""
"3264" 1998 "Worthy did this man seem, and ripe for the meaning of the earth: but"
"3265" 1998 "when I saw his wife, the earth seemed to me a home for madcaps."
"3266" 1998 ""
"3267" 1998 "Yea, I would that the earth shook with convulsions when a saint and a"
"3268" 1998 "goose mate with one another."
"3269" 1998 ""
"3270" 1998 "This one went forth in quest of truth as a hero, and at last got for"
"3271" 1998 "himself a small decked-up lie: his marriage he calleth it."
"3272" 1998 ""
"3273" 1998 "That one was reserved in intercourse and chose choicely. But one time he"
"3274" 1998 "spoilt his company for all time: his marriage he calleth it."
"3275" 1998 ""
"3276" 1998 "Another sought a handmaid with the virtues of an angel. But all at once"
"3277" 1998 "he became the handmaid of a woman, and now would he need also to become"
"3278" 1998 "an angel."
"3279" 1998 ""
"3280" 1998 "Careful, have I found all buyers, and all of them have astute eyes. But"
"3281" 1998 "even the astutest of them buyeth his wife in a sack."
"3282" 1998 ""
"3283" 1998 "Many short follies--that is called love by you. And your marriage"
"3284" 1998 "putteth an end to many short follies, with one long stupidity."
"3285" 1998 ""
"3286" 1998 "Your love to woman, and woman's love to man--ah, would that it were"
"3287" 1998 "sympathy for suffering and veiled deities! But generally two animals"
"3288" 1998 "alight on one another."
"3289" 1998 ""
"3290" 1998 "But even your best love is only an enraptured simile and a painful"
"3291" 1998 "ardour. It is a torch to light you to loftier paths."
"3292" 1998 ""
"3293" 1998 "Beyond yourselves shall ye love some day! Then LEARN first of all to"
"3294" 1998 "love. And on that account ye had to drink the bitter cup of your love."
"3295" 1998 ""
"3296" 1998 "Bitterness is in the cup even of the best love: thus doth it cause"
"3297" 1998 "longing for the Superman; thus doth it cause thirst in thee, the"
"3298" 1998 "creating one!"
"3299" 1998 ""
"3300" 1998 "Thirst in the creating one, arrow and longing for the Superman: tell me,"
"3301" 1998 "my brother, is this thy will to marriage?"
"3302" 1998 ""
"3303" 1998 "Holy call I such a will, and such a marriage.--"
"3304" 1998 ""
"3305" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"3306" 1998 ""
"3307" 1998 ""
"3308" 1998 ""
"3309" 1998 ""
"3310" 1998 "XXI. VOLUNTARY DEATH."
"3311" 1998 ""
"3312" 1998 "Many die too late, and some die too early. Yet strange soundeth the"
"3313" 1998 "precept: \"Die at the right time!"
"3314" 1998 ""
"3315" 1998 "Die at the right time: so teacheth Zarathustra."
"3316" 1998 ""
"3317" 1998 "To be sure, he who never liveth at the right time, how could he ever die"
"3318" 1998 "at the right time? Would that he might never be born!--Thus do I advise"
"3319" 1998 "the superfluous ones."
"3320" 1998 ""
"3321" 1998 "But even the superfluous ones make much ado about their death, and even"
"3322" 1998 "the hollowest nut wanteth to be cracked."
"3323" 1998 ""
"3324" 1998 "Every one regardeth dying as a great matter: but as yet death is not"
"3325" 1998 "a festival. Not yet have people learned to inaugurate the finest"
"3326" 1998 "festivals."
"3327" 1998 ""
"3328" 1998 "The consummating death I show unto you, which becometh a stimulus and"
"3329" 1998 "promise to the living."
"3330" 1998 ""
"3331" 1998 "His death, dieth the consummating one triumphantly, surrounded by hoping"
"3332" 1998 "and promising ones."
"3333" 1998 ""
"3334" 1998 "Thus should one learn to die; and there should be no festival at which"
"3335" 1998 "such a dying one doth not consecrate the oaths of the living!"
"3336" 1998 ""
"3337" 1998 "Thus to die is best; the next best, however, is to die in battle, and"
"3338" 1998 "sacrifice a great soul."
"3339" 1998 ""
"3340" 1998 "But to the fighter equally hateful as to the victor, is your grinning"
"3341" 1998 "death which stealeth nigh like a thief,--and yet cometh as master."
"3342" 1998 ""
"3343" 1998 "My death, praise I unto you, the voluntary death, which cometh unto me"
"3344" 1998 "because _I_ want it."
"3345" 1998 ""
"3346" 1998 "And when shall I want it?--He that hath a goal and an heir, wanteth"
"3347" 1998 "death at the right time for the goal and the heir."
"3348" 1998 ""
"3349" 1998 "And out of reverence for the goal and the heir, he will hang up no more"
"3350" 1998 "withered wreaths in the sanctuary of life."
"3351" 1998 ""
"3352" 1998 "Verily, not the rope-makers will I resemble: they lengthen out their"
"3353" 1998 "cord, and thereby go ever backward."
"3354" 1998 ""
"3355" 1998 "Many a one, also, waxeth too old for his truths and triumphs; a"
"3356" 1998 "toothless mouth hath no longer the right to every truth."
"3357" 1998 ""
"3358" 1998 "And whoever wanteth to have fame, must take leave of honour betimes, and"
"3359" 1998 "practise the difficult art of--going at the right time."
"3360" 1998 ""
"3361" 1998 "One must discontinue being feasted upon when one tasteth best: that is"
"3362" 1998 "known by those who want to be long loved."
"3363" 1998 ""
"3364" 1998 "Sour apples are there, no doubt, whose lot is to wait until the last"
"3365" 1998 "day of autumn: and at the same time they become ripe, yellow, and"
"3366" 1998 "shrivelled."
"3367" 1998 ""
"3368" 1998 "In some ageth the heart first, and in others the spirit. And some are"
"3369" 1998 "hoary in youth, but the late young keep long young."
"3370" 1998 ""
"3371" 1998 "To many men life is a failure; a poison-worm gnaweth at their heart."
"3372" 1998 "Then let them see to it that their dying is all the more a success."
"3373" 1998 ""
"3374" 1998 "Many never become sweet; they rot even in the summer. It is cowardice"
"3375" 1998 "that holdeth them fast to their branches."
"3376" 1998 ""
"3377" 1998 "Far too many live, and far too long hang they on their branches. Would"
"3378" 1998 "that a storm came and shook all this rottenness and worm-eatenness from"
"3379" 1998 "the tree!"
"3380" 1998 ""
"3381" 1998 "Would that there came preachers of SPEEDY death! Those would be the"
"3382" 1998 "appropriate storms and agitators of the trees of life! But I hear only"
"3383" 1998 "slow death preached, and patience with all that is \"earthly.\""
"3384" 1998 ""
"3385" 1998 "Ah! ye preach patience with what is earthly? This earthly is it that"
"3386" 1998 "hath too much patience with you, ye blasphemers!"
"3387" 1998 ""
"3388" 1998 "Verily, too early died that Hebrew whom the preachers of slow death"
"3389" 1998 "honour: and to many hath it proved a calamity that he died too early."
"3390" 1998 ""
"3391" 1998 "As yet had he known only tears, and the melancholy of the Hebrews,"
"3392" 1998 "together with the hatred of the good and just--the Hebrew Jesus: then"
"3393" 1998 "was he seized with the longing for death."
"3394" 1998 ""
"3395" 1998 "Had he but remained in the wilderness, and far from the good and just!"
"3396" 1998 "Then, perhaps, would he have learned to live, and love the earth--and"
"3397" 1998 "laughter also!"
"3398" 1998 ""
"3399" 1998 "Believe it, my brethren! He died too early; he himself would have"
"3400" 1998 "disavowed his doctrine had he attained to my age! Noble enough was he to"
"3401" 1998 "disavow!"
"3402" 1998 ""
"3403" 1998 "But he was still immature. Immaturely loveth the youth, and immaturely"
"3404" 1998 "also hateth he man and earth. Confined and awkward are still his soul"
"3405" 1998 "and the wings of his spirit."
"3406" 1998 ""
"3407" 1998 "But in man there is more of the child than in the youth, and less of"
"3408" 1998 "melancholy: better understandeth he about life and death."
"3409" 1998 ""
"3410" 1998 "Free for death, and free in death; a holy Naysayer, when there is no"
"3411" 1998 "longer time for Yea: thus understandeth he about death and life."
"3412" 1998 ""
"3413" 1998 "That your dying may not be a reproach to man and the earth, my friends:"
"3414" 1998 "that do I solicit from the honey of your soul."
"3415" 1998 ""
"3416" 1998 "In your dying shall your spirit and your virtue still shine like an"
"3417" 1998 "evening after-glow around the earth: otherwise your dying hath been"
"3418" 1998 "unsatisfactory."
"3419" 1998 ""
"3420" 1998 "Thus will I die myself, that ye friends may love the earth more for my"
"3421" 1998 "sake; and earth will I again become, to have rest in her that bore me."
"3422" 1998 ""
"3423" 1998 "Verily, a goal had Zarathustra; he threw his ball. Now be ye friends the"
"3424" 1998 "heirs of my goal; to you throw I the golden ball."
"3425" 1998 ""
"3426" 1998 "Best of all, do I see you, my friends, throw the golden ball! And so"
"3427" 1998 "tarry I still a little while on the earth--pardon me for it!"
"3428" 1998 ""
"3429" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"3430" 1998 ""
"3431" 1998 ""
"3432" 1998 ""
"3433" 1998 ""
"3434" 1998 "XXII. THE BESTOWING VIRTUE."
"3435" 1998 ""
"3436" 1998 "1."
"3437" 1998 ""
"3438" 1998 "When Zarathustra had taken leave of the town to which his heart was"
"3439" 1998 "attached, the name of which is \"The Pied Cow,\" there followed him many"
"3440" 1998 "people who called themselves his disciples, and kept him company. Thus"
"3441" 1998 "came they to a crossroad. Then Zarathustra told them that he now wanted"
"3442" 1998 "to go alone; for he was fond of going alone. His disciples, however,"
"3443" 1998 "presented him at his departure with a staff, on the golden handle of"
"3444" 1998 "which a serpent twined round the sun. Zarathustra rejoiced on account"
"3445" 1998 "of the staff, and supported himself thereon; then spake he thus to his"
"3446" 1998 "disciples:"
"3447" 1998 ""
"3448" 1998 "Tell me, pray: how came gold to the highest value? Because it is"
"3449" 1998 "uncommon, and unprofiting, and beaming, and soft in lustre; it always"
"3450" 1998 "bestoweth itself."
"3451" 1998 ""
"3452" 1998 "Only as image of the highest virtue came gold to the highest value."
"3453" 1998 "Goldlike, beameth the glance of the bestower. Gold-lustre maketh peace"
"3454" 1998 "between moon and sun."
"3455" 1998 ""
"3456" 1998 "Uncommon is the highest virtue, and unprofiting, beaming is it, and soft"
"3457" 1998 "of lustre: a bestowing virtue is the highest virtue."
"3458" 1998 ""
"3459" 1998 "Verily, I divine you well, my disciples: ye strive like me for the"
"3460" 1998 "bestowing virtue. What should ye have in common with cats and wolves?"
"3461" 1998 ""
"3462" 1998 "It is your thirst to become sacrifices and gifts yourselves: and"
"3463" 1998 "therefore have ye the thirst to accumulate all riches in your soul."
"3464" 1998 ""
"3465" 1998 "Insatiably striveth your soul for treasures and jewels, because your"
"3466" 1998 "virtue is insatiable in desiring to bestow."
"3467" 1998 ""
"3468" 1998 "Ye constrain all things to flow towards you and into you, so that they"
"3469" 1998 "shall flow back again out of your fountain as the gifts of your love."
"3470" 1998 ""
"3471" 1998 "Verily, an appropriator of all values must such bestowing love become;"
"3472" 1998 "but healthy and holy, call I this selfishness.--"
"3473" 1998 ""
"3474" 1998 "Another selfishness is there, an all-too-poor and hungry kind, which"
"3475" 1998 "would always steal--the selfishness of the sick, the sickly selfishness."
"3476" 1998 ""
"3477" 1998 "With the eye of the thief it looketh upon all that is lustrous; with the"
"3478" 1998 "craving of hunger it measureth him who hath abundance; and ever doth it"
"3479" 1998 "prowl round the tables of bestowers."
"3480" 1998 ""
"3481" 1998 "Sickness speaketh in such craving, and invisible degeneration; of a"
"3482" 1998 "sickly body, speaketh the larcenous craving of this selfishness."
"3483" 1998 ""
"3484" 1998 "Tell me, my brother, what do we think bad, and worst of all? Is it not"
"3485" 1998 "DEGENERATION?--And we always suspect degeneration when the bestowing"
"3486" 1998 "soul is lacking."
"3487" 1998 ""
"3488" 1998 "Upward goeth our course from genera on to super-genera. But a horror to"
"3489" 1998 "us is the degenerating sense, which saith: \"All for myself.\""
"3490" 1998 ""
"3491" 1998 "Upward soareth our sense: thus is it a simile of our body, a simile of"
"3492" 1998 "an elevation. Such similes of elevations are the names of the virtues."
"3493" 1998 ""
"3494" 1998 "Thus goeth the body through history, a becomer and fighter. And the"
"3495" 1998 "spirit--what is it to the body? Its fights' and victories' herald, its"
"3496" 1998 "companion and echo."
"3497" 1998 ""
"3498" 1998 "Similes, are all names of good and evil; they do not speak out, they"
"3499" 1998 "only hint. A fool who seeketh knowledge from them!"
"3500" 1998 ""
"3501" 1998 "Give heed, my brethren, to every hour when your spirit would speak in"
"3502" 1998 "similes: there is the origin of your virtue."
"3503" 1998 ""
"3504" 1998 "Elevated is then your body, and raised up; with its delight, enraptureth"
"3505" 1998 "it the spirit; so that it becometh creator, and valuer, and lover, and"
"3506" 1998 "everything's benefactor."
"3507" 1998 ""
"3508" 1998 "When your heart overfloweth broad and full like the river, a blessing"
"3509" 1998 "and a danger to the lowlanders: there is the origin of your virtue."
"3510" 1998 ""
"3511" 1998 "When ye are exalted above praise and blame, and your will would command"
"3512" 1998 "all things, as a loving one's will: there is the origin of your virtue."
"3513" 1998 ""
"3514" 1998 "When ye despise pleasant things, and the effeminate couch, and cannot"
"3515" 1998 "couch far enough from the effeminate: there is the origin of your"
"3516" 1998 "virtue."
"3517" 1998 ""
"3518" 1998 "When ye are willers of one will, and when that change of every need is"
"3519" 1998 "needful to you: there is the origin of your virtue."
"3520" 1998 ""
"3521" 1998 "Verily, a new good and evil is it! Verily, a new deep murmuring, and the"
