"6398" 1998 ""
"6399" 1998 "And if that be the true virtue which is unconscious of itself--well, the"
"6400" 1998 "vain man is unconscious of his modesty!--"
"6401" 1998 ""
"6402" 1998 "This is, however, my third manly prudence: I am not put out of conceit"
"6403" 1998 "with the WICKED by your timorousness."
"6404" 1998 ""
"6405" 1998 "I am happy to see the marvels the warm sun hatcheth: tigers and palms"
"6406" 1998 "and rattle-snakes."
"6407" 1998 ""
"6408" 1998 "Also amongst men there is a beautiful brood of the warm sun, and much"
"6409" 1998 "that is marvellous in the wicked."
"6410" 1998 ""
"6411" 1998 "In truth, as your wisest did not seem to me so very wise, so found I"
"6412" 1998 "also human wickedness below the fame of it."
"6413" 1998 ""
"6414" 1998 "And oft did I ask with a shake of the head: Why still rattle, ye"

"6416" 1998 ""
"6417" 1998 "Verily, there is still a future even for evil! And the warmest south is"
"6418" 1998 "still undiscovered by man."
"6419" 1998 ""
"6420" 1998 "How many things are now called the worst wickedness, which are only"

"6423" 1998 ""

"6427" 1998 ""

"6617" 1998 "XLV. THE WANDERER."
"6618" 1998 ""
"6619" 1998 "Then, when it was about midnight, Zarathustra went his way over the"
"6620" 1998 "ridge of the isle, that he might arrive early in the morning at the"
"6621" 1998 "other coast; because there he meant to embark. For there was a good"
"6622" 1998 "roadstead there, in which foreign ships also liked to anchor: those"
"6623" 1998 "ships took many people with them, who wished to cross over from the"
"6624" 1998 "Happy Isles. So when Zarathustra thus ascended the mountain, he thought"
"6625" 1998 "on the way of his many solitary wanderings from youth onwards, and how"
"6626" 1998 "many mountains and ridges and summits he had already climbed."
"6627" 1998 ""
"6628" 1998 "I am a wanderer and mountain-climber, said he to his heart, I love not"
"6629" 1998 "the plains, and it seemeth I cannot long sit still."
"6630" 1998 ""
"6631" 1998 "And whatever may still overtake me as fate and experience--a wandering"
"6632" 1998 "will be therein, and a mountain-climbing: in the end one experienceth"
"6633" 1998 "only oneself."
"6634" 1998 ""
"6635" 1998 "The time is now past when accidents could befall me; and what COULD now"
"6636" 1998 "fall to my lot which would not already be mine own!"
"6637" 1998 ""
"6638" 1998 "It returneth only, it cometh home to me at last--mine own Self, and"
"6639" 1998 "such of it as hath been long abroad, and scattered among things and"
"6640" 1998 "accidents."
"6641" 1998 ""
"6642" 1998 "And one thing more do I know: I stand now before my last summit, and"
"6643" 1998 "before that which hath been longest reserved for me. Ah, my hardest path"
"6644" 1998 "must I ascend! Ah, I have begun my lonesomest wandering!"
"6645" 1998 ""
"6646" 1998 "He, however, who is of my nature doth not avoid such an hour: the hour"

"6648" 1998 "Summit and abyss--these are now comprised together!"
"6649" 1998 ""
"6650" 1998 "Thou goest the way to thy greatness: now hath it become thy last refuge,"
"6651" 1998 "what was hitherto thy last danger!"
"6652" 1998 ""
"6653" 1998 "Thou goest the way to thy greatness: it must now be thy best courage"

"6655" 1998 ""
"6656" 1998 "Thou goest the way to thy greatness: here shall no one steal after thee!"
"6657" 1998 "Thy foot itself hath effaced the path behind thee, and over it standeth"

"6659" 1998 ""
"6660" 1998 "And if all ladders henceforth fail thee, then must thou learn to mount"

"6662" 1998 ""
"6663" 1998 "Upon thine own head, and beyond thine own heart! Now must the gentlest"
"6664" 1998 "in thee become the hardest."
"6665" 1998 ""
"6666" 1998 "He who hath always much-indulged himself, sickeneth at last by his"
"6667" 1998 "much-indulgence. Praises on what maketh hardy! I do not praise the land"

"6669" 1998 ""
"6670" 1998 "To learn TO LOOK AWAY FROM oneself, is necessary in order to see MANY"

"6672" 1998 ""
"6673" 1998 "He, however, who is obtrusive with his eyes as a discerner, how can he"

"6675" 1998 ""
"6676" 1998 "But thou, O Zarathustra, wouldst view the ground of everything, and its"

"6679" 1998 ""
"6680" 1998 "Yea! To look down upon myself, and even upon my stars: that only would I"

"6682" 1998 ""
"6683" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra to himself while ascending, comforting his heart"
"6684" 1998 "with harsh maxims: for he was sore at heart as he had never been before."
"6685" 1998 "And when he had reached the top of the mountain-ridge, behold, there"
"6686" 1998 "lay the other sea spread out before him: and he stood still and was"

"6698" 1998 ""

"6751" 1998 "XLVI. THE VISION AND THE ENIGMA."
"6752" 1998 ""
"6753" 1998 "1."
"6754" 1998 ""
"6755" 1998 "When it got abroad among the sailors that Zarathustra was on board the"
"6756" 1998 "ship--for a man who came from the Happy Isles had gone on board along"
"6757" 1998 "with him,--there was great curiosity and expectation. But Zarathustra"
"6758" 1998 "kept silent for two days, and was cold and deaf with sadness; so that he"
"6759" 1998 "neither answered looks nor questions. On the evening of the second day,"
"6760" 1998 "however, he again opened his ears, though he still kept silent: for"
"6761" 1998 "there were many curious and dangerous things to be heard on board the"
"6762" 1998 "ship, which came from afar, and was to go still further. Zarathustra,"
"6763" 1998 "however, was fond of all those who make distant voyages, and dislike to"
"6764" 1998 "live without danger. And behold! when listening, his own tongue was"
"6765" 1998 "at last loosened, and the ice of his heart broke. Then did he begin to"
"6766" 1998 "speak thus:"
"6767" 1998 ""
"6768" 1998 "To you, the daring venturers and adventurers, and whoever hath embarked"
"6769" 1998 "with cunning sails upon frightful seas,--"
"6770" 1998 ""
"6771" 1998 "To you the enigma-intoxicated, the twilight-enjoyers, whose souls are"
"6772" 1998 "allured by flutes to every treacherous gulf:"
"6773" 1998 ""
"6774" 1998 "--For ye dislike to grope at a thread with cowardly hand; and where ye"
"6775" 1998 "can DIVINE, there do ye hate to CALCULATE--"
"6776" 1998 ""
"6777" 1998 "To you only do I tell the enigma that I SAW--the vision of the"
"6778" 1998 "lonesomest one.--"
"6779" 1998 ""
"6780" 1998 "Gloomily walked I lately in corpse-coloured twilight--gloomily and"
"6781" 1998 "sternly, with compressed lips. Not only one sun had set for me."
"6782" 1998 ""
"6783" 1998 "A path which ascended daringly among boulders, an evil, lonesome path,"
"6784" 1998 "which neither herb nor shrub any longer cheered, a mountain-path,"
"6785" 1998 "crunched under the daring of my foot."
"6786" 1998 ""
"6787" 1998 "Mutely marching over the scornful clinking of pebbles, trampling the"
"6788" 1998 "stone that let it slip: thus did my foot force its way upwards."
"6789" 1998 ""
"6790" 1998 "Upwards:--in spite of the spirit that drew it downwards, towards the"
"6791" 1998 "abyss, the spirit of gravity, my devil and arch-enemy."
"6792" 1998 ""
"6793" 1998 "Upwards:--although it sat upon me, half-dwarf, half-mole; paralysed,"
"6794" 1998 "paralysing; dripping lead in mine ear, and thoughts like drops of lead"
"6795" 1998 "into my brain."
"6796" 1998 ""
"6797" 1998 "\"O Zarathustra,\" it whispered scornfully, syllable by syllable, \"thou"
"6798" 1998 "stone of wisdom! Thou threwest thyself high, but every thrown stone"
"6799" 1998 "must--fall!"
"6800" 1998 ""
"6801" 1998 "O Zarathustra, thou stone of wisdom, thou sling-stone, thou"
"6802" 1998 "star-destroyer! Thyself threwest thou so high,--but every thrown"
"6803" 1998 "stone--must fall!"
"6804" 1998 ""
"6805" 1998 "Condemned of thyself, and to thine own stoning: O Zarathustra, far"
"6806" 1998 "indeed threwest thou thy stone--but upon THYSELF will it recoil!\""
"6807" 1998 ""
"6808" 1998 "Then was the dwarf silent; and it lasted long. The silence, however,"
"6809" 1998 "oppressed me; and to be thus in pairs, one is verily lonesomer than when"
"6810" 1998 "alone!"
"6811" 1998 ""
"6812" 1998 "I ascended, I ascended, I dreamt, I thought,--but everything oppressed"
"6813" 1998 "me. A sick one did I resemble, whom bad torture wearieth, and a worse"
"6814" 1998 "dream reawakeneth out of his first sleep.--"
"6815" 1998 ""
"6816" 1998 "But there is something in me which I call courage: it hath hitherto"
"6817" 1998 "slain for me every dejection. This courage at last bade me stand still"
"6818" 1998 "and say: \"Dwarf! Thou! Or I!\"--"
"6819" 1998 ""
"6820" 1998 "For courage is the best slayer,--courage which ATTACKETH: for in every"
"6821" 1998 "attack there is sound of triumph."
"6822" 1998 ""
"6823" 1998 "Man, however, is the most courageous animal: thereby hath he overcome"
"6824" 1998 "every animal. With sound of triumph hath he overcome every pain; human"
"6825" 1998 "pain, however, is the sorest pain."
"6826" 1998 ""
"6827" 1998 "Courage slayeth also giddiness at abysses: and where doth man not stand"
"6828" 1998 "at abysses! Is not seeing itself--seeing abysses?"
"6829" 1998 ""
"6830" 1998 "Courage is the best slayer: courage slayeth also fellow-suffering."
"6831" 1998 "Fellow-suffering, however, is the deepest abyss: as deeply as man"
"6832" 1998 "looketh into life, so deeply also doth he look into suffering."
"6833" 1998 ""
"6834" 1998 "Courage, however, is the best slayer, courage which attacketh: it"
"6835" 1998 "slayeth even death itself; for it saith: \"WAS THAT life? Well! Once"
"6836" 1998 "more!\""
"6837" 1998 ""
"6838" 1998 "In such speech, however, there is much sound of triumph. He who hath"
"6839" 1998 "ears to hear, let him hear.--"
"6840" 1998 ""
"6841" 1998 "2."
"6842" 1998 ""
"6843" 1998 "\"Halt, dwarf!\" said I. \"Either I--or thou! I, however, am the stronger"
"6844" 1998 "of the two:--thou knowest not mine abysmal thought! IT--couldst thou not"
"6845" 1998 "endure!\""
"6846" 1998 ""
"6847" 1998 "Then happened that which made me lighter: for the dwarf sprang from my"
"6848" 1998 "shoulder, the prying sprite! And it squatted on a stone in front of me."
"6849" 1998 "There was however a gateway just where we halted."
"6850" 1998 ""
"6851" 1998 "\"Look at this gateway! Dwarf!\" I continued, \"it hath two faces. Two"
"6852" 1998 "roads come together here: these hath no one yet gone to the end of."
"6853" 1998 ""
"6854" 1998 "This long lane backwards: it continueth for an eternity. And that long"
"6855" 1998 "lane forward--that is another eternity."
"6856" 1998 ""
"6857" 1998 "They are antithetical to one another, these roads; they directly abut on"
"6858" 1998 "one another:--and it is here, at this gateway, that they come together."
"6859" 1998 "The name of the gateway is inscribed above: 'This Moment.'"
"6860" 1998 ""
"6861" 1998 "But should one follow them further--and ever further and further"
"6862" 1998 "on, thinkest thou, dwarf, that these roads would be eternally"
"6863" 1998 "antithetical?\"--"
"6864" 1998 ""
"6865" 1998 "\"Everything straight lieth,\" murmured the dwarf, contemptuously. \"All"
"6866" 1998 "truth is crooked; time itself is a circle.\""
"6867" 1998 ""
"6868" 1998 "\"Thou spirit of gravity!\" said I wrathfully, \"do not take it too"
"6869" 1998 "lightly! Or I shall let thee squat where thou squattest, Haltfoot,--and"
"6870" 1998 "I carried thee HIGH!\""
"6871" 1998 ""
"6872" 1998 "\"Observe,\" continued I, \"This Moment! From the gateway, This Moment,"
"6873" 1998 "there runneth a long eternal lane BACKWARDS: behind us lieth an"
"6874" 1998 "eternity."
"6875" 1998 ""
"6876" 1998 "Must not whatever CAN run its course of all things, have already run"
"6877" 1998 "along that lane? Must not whatever CAN happen of all things have already"
"6878" 1998 "happened, resulted, and gone by?"
"6879" 1998 ""
"6880" 1998 "And if everything have already existed, what thinkest thou, dwarf, of"
"6881" 1998 "This Moment? Must not this gateway also--have already existed?"
"6882" 1998 ""
"6883" 1998 "And are not all things closely bound together in such wise that This"
"6884" 1998 "Moment draweth all coming things after it? CONSEQUENTLY--itself also?"
"6885" 1998 ""
"6886" 1998 "For whatever CAN run its course of all things, also in this long lane"
"6887" 1998 "OUTWARD--MUST it once more run!--"
"6888" 1998 ""
"6889" 1998 "And this slow spider which creepeth in the moonlight, and this moonlight"
"6890" 1998 "itself, and thou and I in this gateway whispering together, whispering"
"6891" 1998 "of eternal things--must we not all have already existed?"
"6892" 1998 ""
"6893" 1998 "--And must we not return and run in that other lane out before us, that"
"6894" 1998 "long weird lane--must we not eternally return?\"--"
"6895" 1998 ""
"6896" 1998 "Thus did I speak, and always more softly: for I was afraid of mine own"
"6897" 1998 "thoughts, and arrear-thoughts. Then, suddenly did I hear a dog HOWL near"
"6898" 1998 "me."
"6899" 1998 ""
"6900" 1998 "Had I ever heard a dog howl thus? My thoughts ran back. Yes! When I was"
"6901" 1998 "a child, in my most distant childhood:"
"6902" 1998 ""
"6903" 1998 "--Then did I hear a dog howl thus. And saw it also, with hair bristling,"
"6904" 1998 "its head upwards, trembling in the stillest midnight, when even dogs"
"6905" 1998 "believe in ghosts:"
"6906" 1998 ""
"6907" 1998 "--So that it excited my commiseration. For just then went the full moon,"
"6908" 1998 "silent as death, over the house; just then did it stand still, a glowing"
"6909" 1998 "globe--at rest on the flat roof, as if on some one's property:--"
"6910" 1998 ""
"6911" 1998 "Thereby had the dog been terrified: for dogs believe in thieves and"
"6912" 1998 "ghosts. And when I again heard such howling, then did it excite my"
"6913" 1998 "commiseration once more."
"6914" 1998 ""
"6915" 1998 "Where was now the dwarf? And the gateway? And the spider? And all the"
"6916" 1998 "whispering? Had I dreamt? Had I awakened? 'Twixt rugged rocks did I"
"6917" 1998 "suddenly stand alone, dreary in the dreariest moonlight."
"6918" 1998 ""
"6919" 1998 "BUT THERE LAY A MAN! And there! The dog leaping, bristling, whining--now"
"6920" 1998 "did it see me coming--then did it howl again, then did it CRY:--had I"
"6921" 1998 "ever heard a dog cry so for help?"
"6922" 1998 ""
"6923" 1998 "And verily, what I saw, the like had I never seen. A young shepherd did"
"6924" 1998 "I see, writhing, choking, quivering, with distorted countenance, and"
"6925" 1998 "with a heavy black serpent hanging out of his mouth."
"6926" 1998 ""
"6927" 1998 "Had I ever seen so much loathing and pale horror on one countenance?"
"6928" 1998 "He had perhaps gone to sleep? Then had the serpent crawled into his"
"6929" 1998 "throat--there had it bitten itself fast."
"6930" 1998 ""
"6931" 1998 "My hand pulled at the serpent, and pulled:--in vain! I failed to pull"
"6932" 1998 "the serpent out of his throat. Then there cried out of me: \"Bite! Bite!"
"6933" 1998 ""
"6934" 1998 "Its head off! Bite!\"--so cried it out of me; my horror, my hatred, my"
"6935" 1998 "loathing, my pity, all my good and my bad cried with one voice out of"
"6936" 1998 "me.--"
"6937" 1998 ""
"6938" 1998 "Ye daring ones around me! Ye venturers and adventurers, and whoever"
"6939" 1998 "of you have embarked with cunning sails on unexplored seas! Ye"
"6940" 1998 "enigma-enjoyers!"
"6941" 1998 ""
"6942" 1998 "Solve unto me the enigma that I then beheld, interpret unto me the"
"6943" 1998 "vision of the lonesomest one!"
"6944" 1998 ""
"6945" 1998 "For it was a vision and a foresight:--WHAT did I then behold in parable?"
"6946" 1998 "And WHO is it that must come some day?"
"6947" 1998 ""
"6948" 1998 "WHO is the shepherd into whose throat the serpent thus crawled? WHO is"
"6949" 1998 "the man into whose throat all the heaviest and blackest will thus crawl?"
"6950" 1998 ""
"6951" 1998 "--The shepherd however bit as my cry had admonished him; he bit with a"
"6952" 1998 "strong bite! Far away did he spit the head of the serpent--: and sprang"
"6953" 1998 "up.--"
"6954" 1998 ""
"6955" 1998 "No longer shepherd, no longer man--a transfigured being, a"
"6956" 1998 "light-surrounded being, that LAUGHED! Never on earth laughed a man as HE"
"6957" 1998 "laughed!"
"6958" 1998 ""
"6959" 1998 "O my brethren, I heard a laughter which was no human laughter,--and now"
"6960" 1998 "gnaweth a thirst at me, a longing that is never allayed."
"6961" 1998 ""
"6962" 1998 "My longing for that laughter gnaweth at me: oh, how can I still endure"
"6963" 1998 "to live! And how could I endure to die at present!--"
"6964" 1998 ""
"6965" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"6966" 1998 ""
"6967" 1998 ""
"6968" 1998 ""
"6969" 1998 ""
"6970" 1998 "XLVII. INVOLUNTARY BLISS."
"6971" 1998 ""
"6972" 1998 "With such enigmas and bitterness in his heart did Zarathustra sail o'er"
"6973" 1998 "the sea. When, however, he was four day-journeys from the Happy"
"6974" 1998 "Isles and from his friends, then had he surmounted all his pain--:"
"6975" 1998 "triumphantly and with firm foot did he again accept his fate. And then"
"6976" 1998 "talked Zarathustra in this wise to his exulting conscience:"
"6977" 1998 ""
"6978" 1998 "Alone am I again, and like to be so, alone with the pure heaven, and the"
"6979" 1998 "open sea; and again is the afternoon around me."
"6980" 1998 ""
"6981" 1998 "On an afternoon did I find my friends for the first time; on an"
"6982" 1998 "afternoon, also, did I find them a second time:--at the hour when all"
"6983" 1998 "light becometh stiller."
"6984" 1998 ""
"6985" 1998 "For whatever happiness is still on its way 'twixt heaven and earth, now"
"6986" 1998 "seeketh for lodging a luminous soul: WITH HAPPINESS hath all light now"
"6987" 1998 "become stiller."
"6988" 1998 ""
"6989" 1998 "O afternoon of my life! Once did my happiness also descend to the valley"
"6990" 1998 "that it might seek a lodging: then did it find those open hospitable"
"6991" 1998 "souls."
"6992" 1998 ""
"6993" 1998 "O afternoon of my life! What did I not surrender that I might have"
"6994" 1998 "one thing: this living plantation of my thoughts, and this dawn of my"
"6995" 1998 "highest hope!"
"6996" 1998 ""
"6997" 1998 "Companions did the creating one once seek, and children of HIS hope: and"
"6998" 1998 "lo, it turned out that he could not find them, except he himself should"
"6999" 1998 "first create them."
"7000" 1998 ""
"7001" 1998 "Thus am I in the midst of my work, to my children going, and from"
"7002" 1998 "them returning: for the sake of his children must Zarathustra perfect"
"7003" 1998 "himself."
"7004" 1998 ""
"7005" 1998 "For in one's heart one loveth only one's child and one's work; and where"
"7006" 1998 "there is great love to oneself, then is it the sign of pregnancy: so"
"7007" 1998 "have I found it."
"7008" 1998 ""
"7009" 1998 "Still are my children verdant in their first spring, standing nigh one"
"7010" 1998 "another, and shaken in common by the winds, the trees of my garden and"
"7011" 1998 "of my best soil."
"7012" 1998 ""
"7013" 1998 "And verily, where such trees stand beside one another, there ARE Happy"
"7014" 1998 "Isles!"
"7015" 1998 ""
"7016" 1998 "But one day will I take them up, and put each by itself alone: that it"
"7017" 1998 "may learn lonesomeness and defiance and prudence."
"7018" 1998 ""
"7019" 1998 "Gnarled and crooked and with flexible hardness shall it then stand by"
"7020" 1998 "the sea, a living lighthouse of unconquerable life."
"7021" 1998 ""
"7022" 1998 "Yonder where the storms rush down into the sea, and the snout of the"
"7023" 1998 "mountain drinketh water, shall each on a time have his day and night"
"7024" 1998 "watches, for HIS testing and recognition."
"7025" 1998 ""
"7026" 1998 "Recognised and tested shall each be, to see if he be of my type and"
"7027" 1998 "lineage:--if he be master of a long will, silent even when he speaketh,"
"7028" 1998 "and giving in such wise that he TAKETH in giving:--"
"7029" 1998 ""
"7030" 1998 "--So that he may one day become my companion, a fellow-creator and"
"7031" 1998 "fellow-enjoyer with Zarathustra:--such a one as writeth my will on my"
"7032" 1998 "tables, for the fuller perfection of all things."
"7033" 1998 ""
"7034" 1998 "And for his sake and for those like him, must I perfect MYSELF:"
"7035" 1998 "therefore do I now avoid my happiness, and present myself to every"
"7036" 1998 "misfortune--for MY final testing and recognition."
"7037" 1998 ""
"7038" 1998 "And verily, it were time that I went away; and the wanderer's shadow and"
"7039" 1998 "the longest tedium and the stillest hour--have all said unto me: \"It is"
"7040" 1998 "the highest time!\""
"7041" 1998 ""
"7042" 1998 "The word blew to me through the keyhole and said \"Come!\" The door sprang"
"7043" 1998 "subtlely open unto me, and said \"Go!\""
"7044" 1998 ""
"7045" 1998 "But I lay enchained to my love for my children: desire spread this"
"7046" 1998 "snare for me--the desire for love--that I should become the prey of my"
"7047" 1998 "children, and lose myself in them."
"7048" 1998 ""
"7049" 1998 "Desiring--that is now for me to have lost myself. I POSSESS YOU, MY"
"7050" 1998 "CHILDREN! In this possessing shall everything be assurance and nothing"
"7051" 1998 "desire."
"7052" 1998 ""
"7053" 1998 "But brooding lay the sun of my love upon me, in his own juice stewed"
"7054" 1998 "Zarathustra,--then did shadows and doubts fly past me."
"7055" 1998 ""
"7056" 1998 "For frost and winter I now longed: \"Oh, that frost and winter would"
"7057" 1998 "again make me crack and crunch!\" sighed I:--then arose icy mist out of"
"7058" 1998 "me."
"7059" 1998 ""
"7060" 1998 "My past burst its tomb, many pains buried alive woke up--: fully slept"
"7061" 1998 "had they merely, concealed in corpse-clothes."
"7062" 1998 ""
"7063" 1998 "So called everything unto me in signs: \"It is time!\" But I--heard not,"
"7064" 1998 "until at last mine abyss moved, and my thought bit me."
"7065" 1998 ""
"7066" 1998 "Ah, abysmal thought, which art MY thought! When shall I find strength to"
"7067" 1998 "hear thee burrowing, and no longer tremble?"
"7068" 1998 ""
"7069" 1998 "To my very throat throbbeth my heart when I hear thee burrowing! Thy"
"7070" 1998 "muteness even is like to strangle me, thou abysmal mute one!"
"7071" 1998 ""
"7072" 1998 "As yet have I never ventured to call thee UP; it hath been enough that"
"7073" 1998 "I--have carried thee about with me! As yet have I not been strong"
"7074" 1998 "enough for my final lion-wantonness and playfulness."
"7075" 1998 ""
"7076" 1998 "Sufficiently formidable unto me hath thy weight ever been: but one day"
"7077" 1998 "shall I yet find the strength and the lion's voice which will call thee"
"7078" 1998 "up!"
"7079" 1998 ""
"7080" 1998 "When I shall have surmounted myself therein, then will I surmount myself"
"7081" 1998 "also in that which is greater; and a VICTORY shall be the seal of my"
"7082" 1998 "perfection!--"
"7083" 1998 ""
"7084" 1998 "Meanwhile do I sail along on uncertain seas; chance flattereth me,"
"7085" 1998 "smooth-tongued chance; forward and backward do I gaze--, still see I no"
"7086" 1998 "end."
"7087" 1998 ""
"7088" 1998 "As yet hath the hour of my final struggle not come to me--or doth it"
"7089" 1998 "come to me perhaps just now? Verily, with insidious beauty do sea and"
"7090" 1998 "life gaze upon me round about:"
"7091" 1998 ""
"7092" 1998 "O afternoon of my life! O happiness before eventide! O haven upon high"
"7093" 1998 "seas! O peace in uncertainty! How I distrust all of you!"
"7094" 1998 ""
"7095" 1998 "Verily, distrustful am I of your insidious beauty! Like the lover am I,"
"7096" 1998 "who distrusteth too sleek smiling."
"7097" 1998 ""
"7098" 1998 "As he pusheth the best-beloved before him--tender even in severity, the"
"7099" 1998 "jealous one--, so do I push this blissful hour before me."
"7100" 1998 ""
"7101" 1998 "Away with thee, thou blissful hour! With thee hath there come to me an"
"7102" 1998 "involuntary bliss! Ready for my severest pain do I here stand:--at the"
"7103" 1998 "wrong time hast thou come!"
"7104" 1998 ""
"7105" 1998 "Away with thee, thou blissful hour! Rather harbour there--with my"
"7106" 1998 "children! Hasten! and bless them before eventide with MY happiness!"
"7107" 1998 ""
"7108" 1998 "There, already approacheth eventide: the sun sinketh. Away--my"
"7109" 1998 "happiness!--"
"7110" 1998 ""
"7111" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra. And he waited for his misfortune the whole"
"7112" 1998 "night; but he waited in vain. The night remained clear and calm, and"
"7113" 1998 "happiness itself came nigher and nigher unto him. Towards morning,"
"7114" 1998 "however, Zarathustra laughed to his heart, and said mockingly:"
"7115" 1998 "\"Happiness runneth after me. That is because I do not run after women."
"7116" 1998 "Happiness, however, is a woman.\""
"7117" 1998 ""
"7118" 1998 ""
"7119" 1998 ""
"7120" 1998 ""
"7121" 1998 "XLVIII. BEFORE SUNRISE."
"7122" 1998 ""
"7123" 1998 "O heaven above me, thou pure, thou deep heaven! Thou abyss of light!"
"7124" 1998 "Gazing on thee, I tremble with divine desires."
"7125" 1998 ""
"7126" 1998 "Up to thy height to toss myself--that is MY depth! In thy purity to hide"
"7127" 1998 "myself--that is MINE innocence!"
"7128" 1998 ""
"7129" 1998 "The God veileth his beauty: thus hidest thou thy stars. Thou speakest"
"7130" 1998 "not: THUS proclaimest thou thy wisdom unto me."
"7131" 1998 ""
"7132" 1998 "Mute o'er the raging sea hast thou risen for me to-day; thy love and thy"
"7133" 1998 "modesty make a revelation unto my raging soul."
"7134" 1998 ""
"7135" 1998 "In that thou camest unto me beautiful, veiled in thy beauty, in that"
"7136" 1998 "thou spakest unto me mutely, obvious in thy wisdom:"
"7137" 1998 ""
"7138" 1998 "Oh, how could I fail to divine all the modesty of thy soul! BEFORE the"
"7139" 1998 "sun didst thou come unto me--the lonesomest one."
"7140" 1998 ""
"7141" 1998 "We have been friends from the beginning: to us are grief, gruesomeness,"
"7142" 1998 "and ground common; even the sun is common to us."
"7143" 1998 ""
"7144" 1998 "We do not speak to each other, because we know too much--: we keep"
"7145" 1998 "silent to each other, we smile our knowledge to each other."
"7146" 1998 ""
"7147" 1998 "Art thou not the light of my fire? Hast thou not the sister-soul of mine"
"7148" 1998 "insight?"
"7149" 1998 ""
"7150" 1998 "Together did we learn everything; together did we learn to ascend beyond"
"7151" 1998 "ourselves to ourselves, and to smile uncloudedly:--"
"7152" 1998 ""
"7153" 1998 "--Uncloudedly to smile down out of luminous eyes and out of miles of"
"7154" 1998 "distance, when under us constraint and purpose and guilt steam like"
"7155" 1998 "rain."
"7156" 1998 ""
"7157" 1998 "And wandered I alone, for WHAT did my soul hunger by night and in"
"7158" 1998 "labyrinthine paths? And climbed I mountains, WHOM did I ever seek, if"
"7159" 1998 "not thee, upon mountains?"
"7160" 1998 ""
"7161" 1998 "And all my wandering and mountain-climbing: a necessity was it merely,"
"7162" 1998 "and a makeshift of the unhandy one:--to FLY only, wanteth mine entire"
"7163" 1998 "will, to fly into THEE!"
"7164" 1998 ""
"7165" 1998 "And what have I hated more than passing clouds, and whatever tainteth"
"7166" 1998 "thee? And mine own hatred have I even hated, because it tainted thee!"
"7167" 1998 ""
"7168" 1998 "The passing clouds I detest--those stealthy cats of prey: they take"
"7169" 1998 "from thee and me what is common to us--the vast unbounded Yea- and"
"7170" 1998 "Amen-saying."
"7171" 1998 ""
"7172" 1998 "These mediators and mixers we detest--the passing clouds: those"
"7173" 1998 "half-and-half ones, that have neither learned to bless nor to curse from"
"7174" 1998 "the heart."
"7175" 1998 ""
"7176" 1998 "Rather will I sit in a tub under a closed heaven, rather will I sit in"
"7177" 1998 "the abyss without heaven, than see thee, thou luminous heaven, tainted"
"7178" 1998 "with passing clouds!"
"7179" 1998 ""
"7180" 1998 "And oft have I longed to pin them fast with the jagged gold-wires of"
"7181" 1998 "lightning, that I might, like the thunder, beat the drum upon their"
"7182" 1998 "kettle-bellies:--"
"7183" 1998 ""
"7184" 1998 "--An angry drummer, because they rob me of thy Yea and Amen!--thou"
"7185" 1998 "heaven above me, thou pure, thou luminous heaven! Thou abyss of"
"7186" 1998 "light!--because they rob thee of MY Yea and Amen."
"7187" 1998 ""
"7188" 1998 "For rather will I have noise and thunders and tempest-blasts, than this"
"7189" 1998 "discreet, doubting cat-repose; and also amongst men do I hate most"
"7190" 1998 "of all the soft-treaders, and half-and-half ones, and the doubting,"
"7191" 1998 "hesitating, passing clouds."
"7192" 1998 ""
"7193" 1998 "And \"he who cannot bless shall LEARN to curse!\"--this clear teaching"
"7194" 1998 "dropt unto me from the clear heaven; this star standeth in my heaven"
"7195" 1998 "even in dark nights."
"7196" 1998 ""
"7197" 1998 "I, however, am a blesser and a Yea-sayer, if thou be but around me, thou"
"7198" 1998 "pure, thou luminous heaven! Thou abyss of light!--into all abysses do I"
"7199" 1998 "then carry my beneficent Yea-saying."
"7200" 1998 ""
"7201" 1998 "A blesser have I become and a Yea-sayer: and therefore strove I long and"
"7202" 1998 "was a striver, that I might one day get my hands free for blessing."
"7203" 1998 ""
"7204" 1998 "This, however, is my blessing: to stand above everything as its own"
"7205" 1998 "heaven, its round roof, its azure bell and eternal security: and blessed"
"7206" 1998 "is he who thus blesseth!"
"7207" 1998 ""
"7208" 1998 "For all things are baptized at the font of eternity, and beyond good and"
"7209" 1998 "evil; good and evil themselves, however, are but fugitive shadows and"
"7210" 1998 "damp afflictions and passing clouds."
"7211" 1998 ""
"7212" 1998 "Verily, it is a blessing and not a blasphemy when I teach that \"above"
"7213" 1998 "all things there standeth the heaven of chance, the heaven of innocence,"
"7214" 1998 "the heaven of hazard, the heaven of wantonness.\""
"7215" 1998 ""
"7216" 1998 "\"Of Hazard\"--that is the oldest nobility in the world; that gave I back"
"7217" 1998 "to all things; I emancipated them from bondage under purpose."
"7218" 1998 ""
"7219" 1998 "This freedom and celestial serenity did I put like an azure bell above"
"7220" 1998 "all things, when I taught that over them and through them, no \"eternal"
"7221" 1998 "Will\"--willeth."
"7222" 1998 ""
"7223" 1998 "This wantonness and folly did I put in place of that Will, when I taught"
"7224" 1998 "that \"In everything there is one thing impossible--rationality!\""
"7225" 1998 ""
"7226" 1998 "A LITTLE reason, to be sure, a germ of wisdom scattered from star to"
"7227" 1998 "star--this leaven is mixed in all things: for the sake of folly, wisdom"
"7228" 1998 "is mixed in all things!"
"7229" 1998 ""
"7230" 1998 "A little wisdom is indeed possible; but this blessed security have I"
"7231" 1998 "found in all things, that they prefer--to DANCE on the feet of chance."
"7232" 1998 ""
"7233" 1998 "O heaven above me! thou pure, thou lofty heaven! This is now thy purity"
"7234" 1998 "unto me, that there is no eternal reason-spider and reason-cobweb:--"
"7235" 1998 ""
"7236" 1998 "--That thou art to me a dancing-floor for divine chances, that thou art"
"7237" 1998 "to me a table of the Gods, for divine dice and dice-players!--"
"7238" 1998 ""
"7239" 1998 "But thou blushest? Have I spoken unspeakable things? Have I abused, when"
"7240" 1998 "I meant to bless thee?"
"7241" 1998 ""
"7242" 1998 "Or is it the shame of being two of us that maketh thee blush!--Dost thou"
"7243" 1998 "bid me go and be silent, because now--DAY cometh?"
"7244" 1998 ""
"7245" 1998 "The world is deep:--and deeper than e'er the day could read. Not"
"7246" 1998 "everything may be uttered in presence of day. But day cometh: so let us"
"7247" 1998 "part!"
"7248" 1998 ""
"7249" 1998 "O heaven above me, thou modest one! thou glowing one! O thou, my"
"7250" 1998 "happiness before sunrise! The day cometh: so let us part!--"
"7251" 1998 ""
"7252" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"7253" 1998 ""
"7254" 1998 ""
"7255" 1998 ""
"7256" 1998 ""
"7257" 1998 "XLIX. THE BEDWARFING VIRTUE."
"7258" 1998 ""
"7259" 1998 "1."
"7260" 1998 ""
"7261" 1998 "When Zarathustra was again on the continent, he did not go straightway"
"7262" 1998 "to his mountains and his cave, but made many wanderings and"
"7263" 1998 "questionings, and ascertained this and that; so that he said of himself"
"7264" 1998 "jestingly: \"Lo, a river that floweth back unto its source in many"
"7265" 1998 "windings!\" For he wanted to learn what had taken place AMONG MEN during"
"7266" 1998 "the interval: whether they had become greater or smaller. And once, when"
"7267" 1998 "he saw a row of new houses, he marvelled, and said:"
"7268" 1998 ""
"7269" 1998 "\"What do these houses mean? Verily, no great soul put them up as its"
"7270" 1998 "simile!"
"7271" 1998 ""
"7272" 1998 "Did perhaps a silly child take them out of its toy-box? Would that"
"7273" 1998 "another child put them again into the box!"
"7274" 1998 ""
"7275" 1998 "And these rooms and chambers--can MEN go out and in there? They seem to"
"7276" 1998 "be made for silk dolls; or for dainty-eaters, who perhaps let others eat"
"7277" 1998 "with them.\""
"7278" 1998 ""
"7279" 1998 "And Zarathustra stood still and meditated. At last he said sorrowfully:"
"7280" 1998 "\"There hath EVERYTHING become smaller!"
"7281" 1998 ""
"7282" 1998 "Everywhere do I see lower doorways: he who is of MY type can still go"
"7283" 1998 "therethrough, but--he must stoop!"
"7284" 1998 ""
"7285" 1998 "Oh, when shall I arrive again at my home, where I shall no longer have"
"7286" 1998 "to stoop--shall no longer have to stoop BEFORE THE SMALL ONES!\"--And"
"7287" 1998 "Zarathustra sighed, and gazed into the distance.--"
"7288" 1998 ""
"7289" 1998 "The same day, however, he gave his discourse on the bedwarfing virtue."
"7290" 1998 ""
"7291" 1998 "2."
"7292" 1998 ""
"7293" 1998 "I pass through this people and keep mine eyes open: they do not forgive"
"7294" 1998 "me for not envying their virtues."
"7295" 1998 ""
"7296" 1998 "They bite at me, because I say unto them that for small people, small"
"7297" 1998 "virtues are necessary--and because it is hard for me to understand that"
"7298" 1998 "small people are NECESSARY!"
"7299" 1998 ""
"7300" 1998 "Here am I still like a cock in a strange farm-yard, at which even the"
"7301" 1998 "hens peck: but on that account I am not unfriendly to the hens."
"7302" 1998 ""
"7303" 1998 "I am courteous towards them, as towards all small annoyances; to be"
"7304" 1998 "prickly towards what is small, seemeth to me wisdom for hedgehogs."
"7305" 1998 ""
"7306" 1998 "They all speak of me when they sit around their fire in the"
"7307" 1998 "evening--they speak of me, but no one thinketh--of me!"
"7308" 1998 ""
"7309" 1998 "This is the new stillness which I have experienced: their noise around"
"7310" 1998 "me spreadeth a mantle over my thoughts."
"7311" 1998 ""
"7312" 1998 "They shout to one another: \"What is this gloomy cloud about to do to us?"
"7313" 1998 "Let us see that it doth not bring a plague upon us!\""
"7314" 1998 ""
"7315" 1998 "And recently did a woman seize upon her child that was coming unto"
"7316" 1998 "me: \"Take the children away,\" cried she, \"such eyes scorch children's"
"7317" 1998 "souls.\""
"7318" 1998 ""
"7319" 1998 "They cough when I speak: they think coughing an objection to strong"
"7320" 1998 "winds--they divine nothing of the boisterousness of my happiness!"
"7321" 1998 ""
"7322" 1998 "\"We have not yet time for Zarathustra\"--so they object; but what matter"
"7323" 1998 "about a time that \"hath no time\" for Zarathustra?"
"7324" 1998 ""
"7325" 1998 "And if they should altogether praise me, how could I go to sleep on"
"7326" 1998 "THEIR praise? A girdle of spines is their praise unto me: it scratcheth"
"7327" 1998 "me even when I take it off."
"7328" 1998 ""
"7329" 1998 "And this also did I learn among them: the praiser doeth as if he gave"
"7330" 1998 "back; in truth, however, he wanteth more to be given him!"
"7331" 1998 ""
"7332" 1998 "Ask my foot if their lauding and luring strains please it! Verily,"
"7333" 1998 "to such measure and ticktack, it liketh neither to dance nor to stand"
"7334" 1998 "still."
"7335" 1998 ""
"7336" 1998 "To small virtues would they fain lure and laud me; to the ticktack of"
"7337" 1998 "small happiness would they fain persuade my foot."
"7338" 1998 ""
"7339" 1998 "I pass through this people and keep mine eyes open; they have become"
"7340" 1998 "SMALLER, and ever become smaller:--THE REASON THEREOF IS THEIR DOCTRINE"
"7341" 1998 "OF HAPPINESS AND VIRTUE."
"7342" 1998 ""
"7343" 1998 "For they are moderate also in virtue,--because they want comfort. With"
"7344" 1998 "comfort, however, moderate virtue only is compatible."
"7345" 1998 ""
"7346" 1998 "To be sure, they also learn in their way to stride on and stride"
"7347" 1998 "forward: that, I call their HOBBLING.--Thereby they become a hindrance"
"7348" 1998 "to all who are in haste."
"7349" 1998 ""
"7350" 1998 "And many of them go forward, and look backwards thereby, with stiffened"
"7351" 1998 "necks: those do I like to run up against."
"7352" 1998 ""
"7353" 1998 "Foot and eye shall not lie, nor give the lie to each other. But there is"
"7354" 1998 "much lying among small people."
"7355" 1998 ""
"7356" 1998 "Some of them WILL, but most of them are WILLED. Some of them are"
"7357" 1998 "genuine, but most of them are bad actors."
"7358" 1998 ""
"7359" 1998 "There are actors without knowing it amongst them, and actors without"
"7360" 1998 "intending it--, the genuine ones are always rare, especially the genuine"
"7361" 1998 "actors."
"7362" 1998 ""
"7363" 1998 "Of man there is little here: therefore do their women masculinise"
"7364" 1998 "themselves. For only he who is man enough, will--SAVE THE WOMAN in"
"7365" 1998 "woman."
"7366" 1998 ""
"7367" 1998 "And this hypocrisy found I worst amongst them, that even those who"
"7368" 1998 "command feign the virtues of those who serve."
"7369" 1998 ""
"7370" 1998 "\"I serve, thou servest, we serve\"--so chanteth here even the hypocrisy"
"7371" 1998 "of the rulers--and alas! if the first lord be ONLY the first servant!"
"7372" 1998 ""
"7373" 1998 "Ah, even upon their hypocrisy did mine eyes' curiosity alight; and well"
"7374" 1998 "did I divine all their fly-happiness, and their buzzing around sunny"
"7375" 1998 "window-panes."
"7376" 1998 ""
"7377" 1998 "So much kindness, so much weakness do I see. So much justice and pity,"
"7378" 1998 "so much weakness."
"7379" 1998 ""
"7380" 1998 "Round, fair, and considerate are they to one another, as grains of sand"
"7381" 1998 "are round, fair, and considerate to grains of sand."
"7382" 1998 ""
"7383" 1998 "Modestly to embrace a small happiness--that do they call \"submission\"!"
"7384" 1998 "and at the same time they peer modestly after a new small happiness."
"7385" 1998 ""
"7386" 1998 "In their hearts they want simply one thing most of all: that no one hurt"
"7387" 1998 "them. Thus do they anticipate every one's wishes and do well unto every"
"7388" 1998 "one."
"7389" 1998 ""
"7390" 1998 "That, however, is COWARDICE, though it be called \"virtue.\"--"
"7391" 1998 ""
"7392" 1998 "And when they chance to speak harshly, those small people, then do _I_"
"7393" 1998 "hear therein only their hoarseness--every draught of air maketh them"
"7394" 1998 "hoarse."
"7395" 1998 ""
"7396" 1998 "Shrewd indeed are they, their virtues have shrewd fingers. But they lack"
"7397" 1998 "fists: their fingers do not know how to creep behind fists."
"7398" 1998 ""
"7399" 1998 "Virtue for them is what maketh modest and tame: therewith have they made"
"7400" 1998 "the wolf a dog, and man himself man's best domestic animal."
"7401" 1998 ""
"7402" 1998 "\"We set our chair in the MIDST\"--so saith their smirking unto me--\"and"
"7403" 1998 "as far from dying gladiators as from satisfied swine.\""
"7404" 1998 ""
"7405" 1998 "That, however, is--MEDIOCRITY, though it be called moderation.--"
"7406" 1998 ""
"7407" 1998 "3."
"7408" 1998 ""
"7409" 1998 "I pass through this people and let fall many words: but they know"
"7410" 1998 "neither how to take nor how to retain them."
"7411" 1998 ""
"7412" 1998 "They wonder why I came not to revile venery and vice; and verily, I came"
"7413" 1998 "not to warn against pickpockets either!"
"7414" 1998 ""
"7415" 1998 "They wonder why I am not ready to abet and whet their wisdom: as if they"
"7416" 1998 "had not yet enough of wiseacres, whose voices grate on mine ear like"
"7417" 1998 "slate-pencils!"
"7418" 1998 ""
"7419" 1998 "And when I call out: \"Curse all the cowardly devils in you, that"
"7420" 1998 "would fain whimper and fold the hands and adore\"--then do they shout:"
"7421" 1998 "\"Zarathustra is godless.\""
"7422" 1998 ""
"7423" 1998 "And especially do their teachers of submission shout this;--but"
"7424" 1998 "precisely in their ears do I love to cry: \"Yea! I AM Zarathustra, the"
"7425" 1998 "godless!\""
"7426" 1998 ""
"7427" 1998 "Those teachers of submission! Wherever there is aught puny, or sickly,"
"7428" 1998 "or scabby, there do they creep like lice; and only my disgust preventeth"
"7429" 1998 "me from cracking them."
"7430" 1998 ""
"7431" 1998 "Well! This is my sermon for THEIR ears: I am Zarathustra the godless,"
"7432" 1998 "who saith: \"Who is more godless than I, that I may enjoy his teaching?\""
"7433" 1998 ""
"7434" 1998 "I am Zarathustra the godless: where do I find mine equal? And all"
"7435" 1998 "those are mine equals who give unto themselves their Will, and divest"
"7436" 1998 "themselves of all submission."
"7437" 1998 ""
"7438" 1998 "I am Zarathustra the godless! I cook every chance in MY pot. And only"
"7439" 1998 "when it hath been quite cooked do I welcome it as MY food."
"7440" 1998 ""
"7441" 1998 "And verily, many a chance came imperiously unto me: but still more"
"7442" 1998 "imperiously did my WILL speak unto it,--then did it lie imploringly upon"
"7443" 1998 "its knees--"
"7444" 1998 ""
"7445" 1998 "--Imploring that it might find home and heart with me, and saying"
"7446" 1998 "flatteringly: \"See, O Zarathustra, how friend only cometh unto"
"7447" 1998 "friend!\"--"
"7448" 1998 ""
"7449" 1998 "But why talk I, when no one hath MINE ears! And so will I shout it out"
"7450" 1998 "unto all the winds:"
"7451" 1998 ""
"7452" 1998 "Ye ever become smaller, ye small people! Ye crumble away, ye comfortable"
"7453" 1998 "ones! Ye will yet perish--"
"7454" 1998 ""
"7455" 1998 "--By your many small virtues, by your many small omissions, and by your"
"7456" 1998 "many small submissions!"
"7457" 1998 ""
"7458" 1998 "Too tender, too yielding: so is your soil! But for a tree to become"
"7459" 1998 "GREAT, it seeketh to twine hard roots around hard rocks!"
"7460" 1998 ""
"7461" 1998 "Also what ye omit weaveth at the web of all the human future; even your"
"7462" 1998 "naught is a cobweb, and a spider that liveth on the blood of the future."
"7463" 1998 ""
"7464" 1998 "And when ye take, then is it like stealing, ye small virtuous ones;"
"7465" 1998 "but even among knaves HONOUR saith that \"one shall only steal when one"
"7466" 1998 "cannot rob.\""
"7467" 1998 ""
"7468" 1998 "\"It giveth itself\"--that is also a doctrine of submission. But I say"
"7469" 1998 "unto you, ye comfortable ones, that IT TAKETH TO ITSELF, and will ever"
"7470" 1998 "take more and more from you!"
"7471" 1998 ""
"7472" 1998 "Ah, that ye would renounce all HALF-willing, and would decide for"
"7473" 1998 "idleness as ye decide for action!"
"7474" 1998 ""
"7475" 1998 "Ah, that ye understood my word: \"Do ever what ye will--but first be such"
"7476" 1998 "as CAN WILL."
"7477" 1998 ""
"7478" 1998 "Love ever your neighbour as yourselves--but first be such as LOVE"
"7479" 1998 "THEMSELVES--"
"7480" 1998 ""
"7481" 1998 "--Such as love with great love, such as love with great contempt!\" Thus"
"7482" 1998 "speaketh Zarathustra the godless.--"
"7483" 1998 ""
"7484" 1998 "But why talk I, when no one hath MINE ears! It is still an hour too"
"7485" 1998 "early for me here."
"7486" 1998 ""
"7487" 1998 "Mine own forerunner am I among this people, mine own cockcrow in dark"
"7488" 1998 "lanes."
"7489" 1998 ""
"7490" 1998 "But THEIR hour cometh! And there cometh also mine! Hourly do they become"
"7491" 1998 "smaller, poorer, unfruitfuller,--poor herbs! poor earth!"
"7492" 1998 ""
"7493" 1998 "And SOON shall they stand before me like dry grass and prairie, and"
"7494" 1998 "verily, weary of themselves--and panting for FIRE, more than for water!"
"7495" 1998 ""
"7496" 1998 "O blessed hour of the lightning! O mystery before noontide!--Running"
"7497" 1998 "fires will I one day make of them, and heralds with flaming tongues:--"
"7498" 1998 ""
"7499" 1998 "--Herald shall they one day with flaming tongues: It cometh, it is nigh,"
"7500" 1998 "THE GREAT NOONTIDE!"
"7501" 1998 ""
"7502" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"7503" 1998 ""
"7504" 1998 ""
"7505" 1998 ""
"7506" 1998 ""
"7507" 1998 "L. ON THE OLIVE-MOUNT."
"7508" 1998 ""
"7509" 1998 "Winter, a bad guest, sitteth with me at home; blue are my hands with his"
"7510" 1998 "friendly hand-shaking."
"7511" 1998 ""
"7512" 1998 "I honour him, that bad guest, but gladly leave him alone. Gladly do I"
"7513" 1998 "run away from him; and when one runneth WELL, then one escapeth him!"
"7514" 1998 ""
"7515" 1998 "With warm feet and warm thoughts do I run where the wind is calm--to the"
"7516" 1998 "sunny corner of mine olive-mount."
"7517" 1998 ""
"7518" 1998 "There do I laugh at my stern guest, and am still fond of him; because he"
"7519" 1998 "cleareth my house of flies, and quieteth many little noises."
"7520" 1998 ""
"7521" 1998 "For he suffereth it not if a gnat wanteth to buzz, or even two of them;"
"7522" 1998 "also the lanes maketh he lonesome, so that the moonlight is afraid there"
"7523" 1998 "at night."
"7524" 1998 ""
"7525" 1998 "A hard guest is he,--but I honour him, and do not worship, like the"
"7526" 1998 "tenderlings, the pot-bellied fire-idol."
"7527" 1998 ""
"7528" 1998 "Better even a little teeth-chattering than idol-adoration!--so willeth"
"7529" 1998 "my nature. And especially have I a grudge against all ardent, steaming,"
"7530" 1998 "steamy fire-idols."
"7531" 1998 ""
"7532" 1998 "Him whom I love, I love better in winter than in summer; better do I"
"7533" 1998 "now mock at mine enemies, and more heartily, when winter sitteth in my"
"7534" 1998 "house."
"7535" 1998 ""
"7536" 1998 "Heartily, verily, even when I CREEP into bed--: there, still laugheth"
"7537" 1998 "and wantoneth my hidden happiness; even my deceptive dream laugheth."
"7538" 1998 ""
"7539" 1998 "I, a--creeper? Never in my life did I creep before the powerful; and if"
"7540" 1998 "ever I lied, then did I lie out of love. Therefore am I glad even in my"
"7541" 1998 "winter-bed."
"7542" 1998 ""
"7543" 1998 "A poor bed warmeth me more than a rich one, for I am jealous of my"
"7544" 1998 "poverty. And in winter she is most faithful unto me."
"7545" 1998 ""
"7546" 1998 "With a wickedness do I begin every day: I mock at the winter with a cold"
"7547" 1998 "bath: on that account grumbleth my stern house-mate."
"7548" 1998 ""
"7549" 1998 "Also do I like to tickle him with a wax-taper, that he may finally let"
"7550" 1998 "the heavens emerge from ashy-grey twilight."
"7551" 1998 ""
"7552" 1998 "For especially wicked am I in the morning: at the early hour when the"
"7553" 1998 "pail rattleth at the well, and horses neigh warmly in grey lanes:--"
"7554" 1998 ""
"7555" 1998 "Impatiently do I then wait, that the clear sky may finally dawn for me,"
"7556" 1998 "the snow-bearded winter-sky, the hoary one, the white-head,--"
"7557" 1998 ""
"7558" 1998 "--The winter-sky, the silent winter-sky, which often stifleth even its"
"7559" 1998 "sun!"
"7560" 1998 ""
"7561" 1998 "Did I perhaps learn from it the long clear silence? Or did it learn it"
"7562" 1998 "from me? Or hath each of us devised it himself?"
"7563" 1998 ""
"7564" 1998 "Of all good things the origin is a thousandfold,--all good roguish"
"7565" 1998 "things spring into existence for joy: how could they always do so--for"
"7566" 1998 "once only!"
"7567" 1998 ""
"7568" 1998 "A good roguish thing is also the long silence, and to look, like the"
"7569" 1998 "winter-sky, out of a clear, round-eyed countenance:--"
"7570" 1998 ""
"7571" 1998 "--Like it to stifle one's sun, and one's inflexible solar will: verily,"
"7572" 1998 "this art and this winter-roguishness have I learnt WELL!"
"7573" 1998 ""
"7574" 1998 "My best-loved wickedness and art is it, that my silence hath learned not"
"7575" 1998 "to betray itself by silence."
"7576" 1998 ""
"7577" 1998 "Clattering with diction and dice, I outwit the solemn assistants: all"
"7578" 1998 "those stern watchers, shall my will and purpose elude."
"7579" 1998 ""
"7580" 1998 "That no one might see down into my depth and into mine ultimate"
"7581" 1998 "will--for that purpose did I devise the long clear silence."
"7582" 1998 ""
"7583" 1998 "Many a shrewd one did I find: he veiled his countenance and made his"
"7584" 1998 "water muddy, that no one might see therethrough and thereunder."
"7585" 1998 ""
"7586" 1998 "But precisely unto him came the shrewder distrusters and nut-crackers:"
"7587" 1998 "precisely from him did they fish his best-concealed fish!"
"7588" 1998 ""
"7589" 1998 "But the clear, the honest, the transparent--these are for me the wisest"
"7590" 1998 "silent ones: in them, so PROFOUND is the depth that even the clearest"
"7591" 1998 "water doth not--betray it.--"
"7592" 1998 ""
"7593" 1998 "Thou snow-bearded, silent, winter-sky, thou round-eyed whitehead above"
"7594" 1998 "me! Oh, thou heavenly simile of my soul and its wantonness!"
"7595" 1998 ""
"7596" 1998 "And MUST I not conceal myself like one who hath swallowed gold--lest my"
"7597" 1998 "soul should be ripped up?"
"7598" 1998 ""
"7599" 1998 "MUST I not wear stilts, that they may OVERLOOK my long legs--all those"
"7600" 1998 "enviers and injurers around me?"
"7601" 1998 ""
"7602" 1998 "Those dingy, fire-warmed, used-up, green-tinted, ill-natured souls--how"
"7603" 1998 "COULD their envy endure my happiness!"
"7604" 1998 ""
"7605" 1998 "Thus do I show them only the ice and winter of my peaks--and NOT that my"
"7606" 1998 "mountain windeth all the solar girdles around it!"
"7607" 1998 ""
"7608" 1998 "They hear only the whistling of my winter-storms: and know NOT that I"
"7609" 1998 "also travel over warm seas, like longing, heavy, hot south-winds."
"7610" 1998 ""
"7611" 1998 "They commiserate also my accidents and chances:--but MY word saith:"
"7612" 1998 "\"Suffer the chance to come unto me: innocent is it as a little child!\""
"7613" 1998 ""
"7614" 1998 "How COULD they endure my happiness, if I did not put around it"
"7615" 1998 "accidents, and winter-privations, and bear-skin caps, and enmantling"
"7616" 1998 "snowflakes!"
"7617" 1998 ""
"7618" 1998 "--If I did not myself commiserate their PITY, the pity of those enviers"
"7619" 1998 "and injurers!"
"7620" 1998 ""
"7621" 1998 "--If I did not myself sigh before them, and chatter with cold, and"
"7622" 1998 "patiently LET myself be swathed in their pity!"
"7623" 1998 ""
"7624" 1998 "This is the wise waggish-will and good-will of my soul, that it"
"7625" 1998 "CONCEALETH NOT its winters and glacial storms; it concealeth not its"
"7626" 1998 "chilblains either."
"7627" 1998 ""
"7628" 1998 "To one man, lonesomeness is the flight of the sick one; to another, it"
"7629" 1998 "is the flight FROM the sick ones."
"7630" 1998 ""
"7631" 1998 "Let them HEAR me chattering and sighing with winter-cold, all those poor"
"7632" 1998 "squinting knaves around me! With such sighing and chattering do I flee"
"7633" 1998 "from their heated rooms."
"7634" 1998 ""
"7635" 1998 "Let them sympathise with me and sigh with me on account of my"
"7636" 1998 "chilblains: \"At the ice of knowledge will he yet FREEZE TO DEATH!\"--so"
"7637" 1998 "they mourn."
"7638" 1998 ""
"7639" 1998 "Meanwhile do I run with warm feet hither and thither on mine"
"7640" 1998 "olive-mount: in the sunny corner of mine olive-mount do I sing, and mock"
"7641" 1998 "at all pity.--"
"7642" 1998 ""
"7643" 1998 "Thus sang Zarathustra."
"7644" 1998 ""
"7645" 1998 ""
"7646" 1998 ""
"7647" 1998 ""
"7648" 1998 "LI. ON PASSING-BY."
"7649" 1998 ""
"7650" 1998 "Thus slowly wandering through many peoples and divers cities, did"
"7651" 1998 "Zarathustra return by round-about roads to his mountains and his cave."
"7652" 1998 "And behold, thereby came he unawares also to the gate of the GREAT CITY."
"7653" 1998 "Here, however, a foaming fool, with extended hands, sprang forward to"
"7654" 1998 "him and stood in his way. It was the same fool whom the people called"
"7655" 1998 "\"the ape of Zarathustra:\" for he had learned from him something of the"
"7656" 1998 "expression and modulation of language, and perhaps liked also to borrow"
"7657" 1998 "from the store of his wisdom. And the fool talked thus to Zarathustra:"
"7658" 1998 ""
"7659" 1998 "O Zarathustra, here is the great city: here hast thou nothing to seek"
"7660" 1998 "and everything to lose."
"7661" 1998 ""
"7662" 1998 "Why wouldst thou wade through this mire? Have pity upon thy foot! Spit"
"7663" 1998 "rather on the gate of the city, and--turn back!"
"7664" 1998 ""
"7665" 1998 "Here is the hell for anchorites' thoughts: here are great thoughts"
"7666" 1998 "seethed alive and boiled small."
"7667" 1998 ""
"7668" 1998 "Here do all great sentiments decay: here may only rattle-boned"
"7669" 1998 "sensations rattle!"
"7670" 1998 ""
"7671" 1998 "Smellest thou not already the shambles and cookshops of the spirit?"
"7672" 1998 "Steameth not this city with the fumes of slaughtered spirit?"
"7673" 1998 ""
"7674" 1998 "Seest thou not the souls hanging like limp dirty rags?--And they make"
"7675" 1998 "newspapers also out of these rags!"
"7676" 1998 ""
"7677" 1998 "Hearest thou not how spirit hath here become a verbal game? Loathsome"
"7678" 1998 "verbal swill doth it vomit forth!--And they make newspapers also out of"
"7679" 1998 "this verbal swill."
"7680" 1998 ""
"7681" 1998 "They hound one another, and know not whither! They inflame one another,"
"7682" 1998 "and know not why! They tinkle with their pinchbeck, they jingle with"
"7683" 1998 "their gold."
"7684" 1998 ""
"7685" 1998 "They are cold, and seek warmth from distilled waters: they are inflamed,"
"7686" 1998 "and seek coolness from frozen spirits; they are all sick and sore"
"7687" 1998 "through public opinion."
"7688" 1998 ""
"7689" 1998 "All lusts and vices are here at home; but here there are also the"
"7690" 1998 "virtuous; there is much appointable appointed virtue:--"
"7691" 1998 ""
"7692" 1998 "Much appointable virtue with scribe-fingers, and hardy sitting-flesh and"
"7693" 1998 "waiting-flesh, blessed with small breast-stars, and padded, haunchless"
"7694" 1998 "daughters."
"7695" 1998 ""
"7696" 1998 "There is here also much piety, and much faithful spittle-licking and"
"7697" 1998 "spittle-backing, before the God of Hosts."
"7698" 1998 ""
"7699" 1998 "\"From on high,\" drippeth the star, and the gracious spittle; for the"
"7700" 1998 "high, longeth every starless bosom."
"7701" 1998 ""
"7702" 1998 "The moon hath its court, and the court hath its moon-calves: unto all,"
"7703" 1998 "however, that cometh from the court do the mendicant people pray, and"
"7704" 1998 "all appointable mendicant virtues."
"7705" 1998 ""
"7706" 1998 "\"I serve, thou servest, we serve\"--so prayeth all appointable virtue"
"7707" 1998 "to the prince: that the merited star may at last stick on the slender"
"7708" 1998 "breast!"
"7709" 1998 ""
"7710" 1998 "But the moon still revolveth around all that is earthly: so revolveth"
"7711" 1998 "also the prince around what is earthliest of all--that, however, is the"
"7712" 1998 "gold of the shopman."
"7713" 1998 ""
"7714" 1998 "The God of the Hosts of war is not the God of the golden bar; the prince"
"7715" 1998 "proposeth, but the shopman--disposeth!"
"7716" 1998 ""
"7717" 1998 "By all that is luminous and strong and good in thee, O Zarathustra! Spit"
"7718" 1998 "on this city of shopmen and return back!"
"7719" 1998 ""
"7720" 1998 "Here floweth all blood putridly and tepidly and frothily through all"
"7721" 1998 "veins: spit on the great city, which is the great slum where all the"
"7722" 1998 "scum frotheth together!"
"7723" 1998 ""
"7724" 1998 "Spit on the city of compressed souls and slender breasts, of pointed"
"7725" 1998 "eyes and sticky fingers--"
"7726" 1998 ""
"7727" 1998 "--On the city of the obtrusive, the brazen-faced, the pen-demagogues and"
"7728" 1998 "tongue-demagogues, the overheated ambitious:--"
"7729" 1998 ""
"7730" 1998 "Where everything maimed, ill-famed, lustful, untrustful, over-mellow,"
"7731" 1998 "sickly-yellow and seditious, festereth pernicious:--"
"7732" 1998 ""
"7733" 1998 "--Spit on the great city and turn back!--"
"7734" 1998 ""
"7735" 1998 "Here, however, did Zarathustra interrupt the foaming fool, and shut his"
"7736" 1998 "mouth.--"
"7737" 1998 ""
"7738" 1998 "Stop this at once! called out Zarathustra, long have thy speech and thy"
"7739" 1998 "species disgusted me!"
"7740" 1998 ""
"7741" 1998 "Why didst thou live so long by the swamp, that thou thyself hadst to"
"7742" 1998 "become a frog and a toad?"
"7743" 1998 ""
"7744" 1998 "Floweth there not a tainted, frothy, swamp-blood in thine own veins,"
"7745" 1998 "when thou hast thus learned to croak and revile?"
"7746" 1998 ""
"7747" 1998 "Why wentest thou not into the forest? Or why didst thou not till the"
"7748" 1998 "ground? Is the sea not full of green islands?"
"7749" 1998 ""
"7750" 1998 "I despise thy contempt; and when thou warnedst me--why didst thou not"
"7751" 1998 "warn thyself?"
"7752" 1998 ""
"7753" 1998 "Out of love alone shall my contempt and my warning bird take wing; but"
"7754" 1998 "not out of the swamp!--"
"7755" 1998 ""
"7756" 1998 "They call thee mine ape, thou foaming fool: but I call thee my"
"7757" 1998 "grunting-pig,--by thy grunting, thou spoilest even my praise of folly."
"7758" 1998 ""
"7759" 1998 "What was it that first made thee grunt? Because no one sufficiently"
"7760" 1998 "FLATTERED thee:--therefore didst thou seat thyself beside this filth,"
"7761" 1998 "that thou mightest have cause for much grunting,--"
"7762" 1998 ""
"7763" 1998 "--That thou mightest have cause for much VENGEANCE! For vengeance, thou"
"7764" 1998 "vain fool, is all thy foaming; I have divined thee well!"
"7765" 1998 ""
"7766" 1998 "But thy fools'-word injureth ME, even when thou art right! And even if"
"7767" 1998 "Zarathustra's word WERE a hundred times justified, thou wouldst ever--DO"
"7768" 1998 "wrong with my word!"
"7769" 1998 ""
"7770" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra. Then did he look on the great city and sighed,"
"7771" 1998 "and was long silent. At last he spake thus:"
"7772" 1998 ""
"7773" 1998 "I loathe also this great city, and not only this fool. Here and there--"
"7774" 1998 "there is nothing to better, nothing to worsen."
"7775" 1998 ""
"7776" 1998 "Woe to this great city!--And I would that I already saw the pillar of"
"7777" 1998 "fire in which it will be consumed!"
"7778" 1998 ""
"7779" 1998 "For such pillars of fire must precede the great noontide. But this hath"
"7780" 1998 "its time and its own fate.--"
"7781" 1998 ""
"7782" 1998 "This precept, however, give I unto thee, in parting, thou fool: Where"
"7783" 1998 "one can no longer love, there should one--PASS BY!--"
"7784" 1998 ""
"7785" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra, and passed by the fool and the great city."
"7786" 1998 ""
"7787" 1998 ""
"7788" 1998 ""
"7789" 1998 ""
"7790" 1998 "LII. THE APOSTATES."
"7791" 1998 ""
"7792" 1998 "1."
"7793" 1998 ""
"7794" 1998 "Ah, lieth everything already withered and grey which but lately stood"
"7795" 1998 "green and many-hued on this meadow! And how much honey of hope did I"
"7796" 1998 "carry hence into my beehives!"
"7797" 1998 ""
"7798" 1998 "Those young hearts have already all become old--and not old even! only"
"7799" 1998 "weary, ordinary, comfortable:--they declare it: \"We have again become"
"7800" 1998 "pious.\""
"7801" 1998 ""
"7802" 1998 "Of late did I see them run forth at early morn with valorous steps: but"
"7803" 1998 "the feet of their knowledge became weary, and now do they malign even"
"7804" 1998 "their morning valour!"
"7805" 1998 ""
"7806" 1998 "Verily, many of them once lifted their legs like the dancer; to them"
"7807" 1998 "winked the laughter of my wisdom:--then did they bethink themselves."
"7808" 1998 "Just now have I seen them bent down--to creep to the cross."
"7809" 1998 ""
"7810" 1998 "Around light and liberty did they once flutter like gnats and young"
"7811" 1998 "poets. A little older, a little colder: and already are they mystifiers,"
"7812" 1998 "and mumblers and mollycoddles."
"7813" 1998 ""
"7814" 1998 "Did perhaps their hearts despond, because lonesomeness had swallowed me"
"7815" 1998 "like a whale? Did their ear perhaps hearken yearningly-long for me IN"
"7816" 1998 "VAIN, and for my trumpet-notes and herald-calls?"
"7817" 1998 ""
"7818" 1998 "--Ah! Ever are there but few of those whose hearts have persistent"
"7819" 1998 "courage and exuberance; and in such remaineth also the spirit patient."
"7820" 1998 "The rest, however, are COWARDLY."
"7821" 1998 ""
"7822" 1998 "The rest: these are always the great majority, the common-place, the"
"7823" 1998 "superfluous, the far-too many--those all are cowardly!--"
"7824" 1998 ""
"7825" 1998 "Him who is of my type, will also the experiences of my type meet on the"
"7826" 1998 "way: so that his first companions must be corpses and buffoons."
"7827" 1998 ""
"7828" 1998 "His second companions, however--they will call themselves his"
"7829" 1998 "BELIEVERS,--will be a living host, with much love, much folly, much"
"7830" 1998 "unbearded veneration."
"7831" 1998 ""
"7832" 1998 "To those believers shall he who is of my type among men not bind his"
"7833" 1998 "heart; in those spring-times and many-hued meadows shall he not believe,"
"7834" 1998 "who knoweth the fickly faint-hearted human species!"
"7835" 1998 ""
"7836" 1998 "COULD they do otherwise, then would they also WILL otherwise. The"
"7837" 1998 "half-and-half spoil every whole. That leaves become withered,--what is"
"7838" 1998 "there to lament about that!"
"7839" 1998 ""
"7840" 1998 "Let them go and fall away, O Zarathustra, and do not lament! Better even"
"7841" 1998 "to blow amongst them with rustling winds,--"
"7842" 1998 ""
"7843" 1998 "--Blow amongst those leaves, O Zarathustra, that everything WITHERED may"
"7844" 1998 "run away from thee the faster!--"
"7845" 1998 ""
"7846" 1998 "2."
"7847" 1998 ""
"7848" 1998 "\"We have again become pious\"--so do those apostates confess; and some of"
"7849" 1998 "them are still too pusillanimous thus to confess."
"7850" 1998 ""
"7851" 1998 "Unto them I look into the eye,--before them I say it unto their face and"
"7852" 1998 "unto the blush on their cheeks: Ye are those who again PRAY!"
"7853" 1998 ""
"7854" 1998 "It is however a shame to pray! Not for all, but for thee, and me, and"
"7855" 1998 "whoever hath his conscience in his head. For THEE it is a shame to pray!"
"7856" 1998 ""
"7857" 1998 "Thou knowest it well: the faint-hearted devil in thee, which would"
"7858" 1998 "fain fold its arms, and place its hands in its bosom, and take it"
"7859" 1998 "easier:--this faint-hearted devil persuadeth thee that \"there IS a God!\""
"7860" 1998 ""
"7861" 1998 "THEREBY, however, dost thou belong to the light-dreading type, to whom"
"7862" 1998 "light never permitteth repose: now must thou daily thrust thy head"
"7863" 1998 "deeper into obscurity and vapour!"
"7864" 1998 ""
"7865" 1998 "And verily, thou choosest the hour well: for just now do the nocturnal"
"7866" 1998 "birds again fly abroad. The hour hath come for all light-dreading"
"7867" 1998 "people, the vesper hour and leisure hour, when they do not--\"take"
"7868" 1998 "leisure.\""
"7869" 1998 ""
"7870" 1998 "I hear it and smell it: it hath come--their hour for hunt and"
"7871" 1998 "procession, not indeed for a wild hunt, but for a tame, lame, snuffling,"
"7872" 1998 "soft-treaders', soft-prayers' hunt,--"
"7873" 1998 ""
"7874" 1998 "--For a hunt after susceptible simpletons: all mouse-traps for the heart"
"7875" 1998 "have again been set! And whenever I lift a curtain, a night-moth rusheth"
"7876" 1998 "out of it."
"7877" 1998 ""
"7878" 1998 "Did it perhaps squat there along with another night-moth? For everywhere"
"7879" 1998 "do I smell small concealed communities; and wherever there are closets"
"7880" 1998 "there are new devotees therein, and the atmosphere of devotees."
"7881" 1998 ""
"7882" 1998 "They sit for long evenings beside one another, and say: \"Let us again"
"7883" 1998 "become like little children and say, 'good God!'\"--ruined in mouths and"
"7884" 1998 "stomachs by the pious confectioners."
"7885" 1998 ""
"7886" 1998 "Or they look for long evenings at a crafty, lurking cross-spider, that"
"7887" 1998 "preacheth prudence to the spiders themselves, and teacheth that \"under"
"7888" 1998 "crosses it is good for cobweb-spinning!\""
"7889" 1998 ""
"7890" 1998 "Or they sit all day at swamps with angle-rods, and on that account think"
"7891" 1998 "themselves PROFOUND; but whoever fisheth where there are no fish, I do"
"7892" 1998 "not even call him superficial!"
"7893" 1998 ""
"7894" 1998 "Or they learn in godly-gay style to play the harp with a hymn-poet,"
"7895" 1998 "who would fain harp himself into the heart of young girls:--for he hath"
"7896" 1998 "tired of old girls and their praises."
"7897" 1998 ""
"7898" 1998 "Or they learn to shudder with a learned semi-madcap, who waiteth in"
"7899" 1998 "darkened rooms for spirits to come to him--and the spirit runneth away"
"7900" 1998 "entirely!"
"7901" 1998 ""
"7902" 1998 "Or they listen to an old roving howl-and growl-piper, who hath learnt"
"7903" 1998 "from the sad winds the sadness of sounds; now pipeth he as the wind, and"
"7904" 1998 "preacheth sadness in sad strains."
"7905" 1998 ""
"7906" 1998 "And some of them have even become night-watchmen: they know now how to"
"7907" 1998 "blow horns, and go about at night and awaken old things which have long"
"7908" 1998 "fallen asleep."
"7909" 1998 ""
"7910" 1998 "Five words about old things did I hear yester-night at the garden-wall:"
"7911" 1998 "they came from such old, sorrowful, arid night-watchmen."
"7912" 1998 ""
"7913" 1998 "\"For a father he careth not sufficiently for his children: human fathers"
"7914" 1998 "do this better!\"--"
"7915" 1998 ""
"7916" 1998 "\"He is too old! He now careth no more for his children,\"--answered the"
"7917" 1998 "other night-watchman."
"7918" 1998 ""
"7919" 1998 "\"HATH he then children? No one can prove it unless he himself prove it!"
"7920" 1998 "I have long wished that he would for once prove it thoroughly.\""
"7921" 1998 ""
"7922" 1998 "\"Prove? As if HE had ever proved anything! Proving is difficult to him;"
"7923" 1998 "he layeth great stress on one's BELIEVING him.\""
"7924" 1998 ""
"7925" 1998 "\"Ay! Ay! Belief saveth him; belief in him. That is the way with old"
"7926" 1998 "people! So it is with us also!\"--"
"7927" 1998 ""
"7928" 1998 "--Thus spake to each other the two old night-watchmen and light-scarers,"
"7929" 1998 "and tooted thereupon sorrowfully on their horns: so did it happen"
"7930" 1998 "yester-night at the garden-wall."
"7931" 1998 ""
"7932" 1998 "To me, however, did the heart writhe with laughter, and was like to"
"7933" 1998 "break; it knew not where to go, and sunk into the midriff."
"7934" 1998 ""
"7935" 1998 "Verily, it will be my death yet--to choke with laughter when I see asses"
"7936" 1998 "drunken, and hear night-watchmen thus doubt about God."
"7937" 1998 ""
"7938" 1998 "Hath the time not LONG since passed for all such doubts? Who may"
"7939" 1998 "nowadays awaken such old slumbering, light-shunning things!"
"7940" 1998 ""
"7941" 1998 "With the old Deities hath it long since come to an end:--and verily, a"
"7942" 1998 "good joyful Deity-end had they!"
"7943" 1998 ""
"7944" 1998 "They did not \"begloom\" themselves to death--that do people fabricate! On"
"7945" 1998 "the contrary, they--LAUGHED themselves to death once on a time!"
"7946" 1998 ""
"7947" 1998 "That took place when the unGodliest utterance came from a God"
"7948" 1998 "himself--the utterance: \"There is but one God! Thou shalt have no other"
"7949" 1998 "Gods before me!\"--"
"7950" 1998 ""
"7951" 1998 "--An old grim-beard of a God, a jealous one, forgot himself in such"
"7952" 1998 "wise:--"
"7953" 1998 ""
"7954" 1998 "And all the Gods then laughed, and shook upon their thrones, and"
"7955" 1998 "exclaimed: \"Is it not just divinity that there are Gods, but no God?\""
"7956" 1998 ""
"7957" 1998 "He that hath an ear let him hear.--"
"7958" 1998 ""
"7959" 1998 "Thus talked Zarathustra in the city he loved, which is surnamed \"The"
"7960" 1998 "Pied Cow.\" For from here he had but two days to travel to reach once"
"7961" 1998 "more his cave and his animals; his soul, however, rejoiced unceasingly"
"7962" 1998 "on account of the nighness of his return home."
"7963" 1998 ""
"7964" 1998 ""
"7965" 1998 ""
"7966" 1998 ""
"7967" 1998 "LIII. THE RETURN HOME."
"7968" 1998 ""
"7969" 1998 "O lonesomeness! My HOME, lonesomeness! Too long have I lived wildly in"
"7970" 1998 "wild remoteness, to return to thee without tears!"
"7971" 1998 ""
"7972" 1998 "Now threaten me with the finger as mothers threaten; now smile upon me"
"7973" 1998 "as mothers smile; now say just: \"Who was it that like a whirlwind once"
"7974" 1998 "rushed away from me?--"
"7975" 1998 ""
"7976" 1998 "--Who when departing called out: 'Too long have I sat with lonesomeness;"
"7977" 1998 "there have I unlearned silence!' THAT hast thou learned now--surely?"
"7978" 1998 ""
"7979" 1998 "O Zarathustra, everything do I know; and that thou wert MORE FORSAKEN"
"7980" 1998 "amongst the many, thou unique one, than thou ever wert with me!"
"7981" 1998 ""
"7982" 1998 "One thing is forsakenness, another matter is lonesomeness: THAT hast"
"7983" 1998 "thou now learned! And that amongst men thou wilt ever be wild and"
"7984" 1998 "strange:"
"7985" 1998 ""
"7986" 1998 "--Wild and strange even when they love thee: for above all they want to"
"7987" 1998 "be TREATED INDULGENTLY!"
"7988" 1998 ""
"7989" 1998 "Here, however, art thou at home and house with thyself; here canst thou"
"7990" 1998 "utter everything, and unbosom all motives; nothing is here ashamed of"
"7991" 1998 "concealed, congealed feelings."
"7992" 1998 ""
"7993" 1998 "Here do all things come caressingly to thy talk and flatter thee: for"
"7994" 1998 "they want to ride upon thy back. On every simile dost thou here ride to"
"7995" 1998 "every truth."
"7996" 1998 ""
"7997" 1998 "Uprightly and openly mayest thou here talk to all things: and verily,"
"7998" 1998 "it soundeth as praise in their ears, for one to talk to all"
"7999" 1998 "things--directly!"
"8000" 1998 ""
"8001" 1998 "Another matter, however, is forsakenness. For, dost thou remember, O"
"8002" 1998 "Zarathustra? When thy bird screamed overhead, when thou stoodest in the"
"8003" 1998 "forest, irresolute, ignorant where to go, beside a corpse:--"
"8004" 1998 ""
"8005" 1998 "--When thou spakest: 'Let mine animals lead me! More dangerous have I"
"8006" 1998 "found it among men than among animals:'--THAT was forsakenness!"
"8007" 1998 ""
"8008" 1998 "And dost thou remember, O Zarathustra? When thou sattest in thine isle,"
"8009" 1998 "a well of wine giving and granting amongst empty buckets, bestowing and"
"8010" 1998 "distributing amongst the thirsty:"
"8011" 1998 ""
"8012" 1998 "--Until at last thou alone sattest thirsty amongst the drunken ones, and"
"8013" 1998 "wailedst nightly: 'Is taking not more blessed than giving? And stealing"
"8014" 1998 "yet more blessed than taking?'--THAT was forsakenness!"
"8015" 1998 ""
"8016" 1998 "And dost thou remember, O Zarathustra? When thy stillest hour came and"
"8017" 1998 "drove thee forth from thyself, when with wicked whispering it said:"
"8018" 1998 "'Speak and succumb!'--"
"8019" 1998 ""
"8020" 1998 "--When it disgusted thee with all thy waiting and silence, and"
"8021" 1998 "discouraged thy humble courage: THAT was forsakenness!\"--"
"8022" 1998 ""
"8023" 1998 "O lonesomeness! My home, lonesomeness! How blessedly and tenderly"
"8024" 1998 "speaketh thy voice unto me!"
"8025" 1998 ""
"8026" 1998 "We do not question each other, we do not complain to each other; we go"
"8027" 1998 "together openly through open doors."
"8028" 1998 ""
"8029" 1998 "For all is open with thee and clear; and even the hours run here on"
"8030" 1998 "lighter feet. For in the dark, time weigheth heavier upon one than in"
"8031" 1998 "the light."
"8032" 1998 ""
"8033" 1998 "Here fly open unto me all being's words and word-cabinets: here all"
"8034" 1998 "being wanteth to become words, here all becoming wanteth to learn of me"
"8035" 1998 "how to talk."
"8036" 1998 ""
"8037" 1998 "Down there, however--all talking is in vain! There, forgetting and"
"8038" 1998 "passing-by are the best wisdom: THAT have I learned now!"
"8039" 1998 ""
"8040" 1998 "He who would understand everything in man must handle everything. But"
"8041" 1998 "for that I have too clean hands."
"8042" 1998 ""
"8043" 1998 "I do not like even to inhale their breath; alas! that I have lived so"
"8044" 1998 "long among their noise and bad breaths!"
"8045" 1998 ""
"8046" 1998 "O blessed stillness around me! O pure odours around me! How from a deep"
"8047" 1998 "breast this stillness fetcheth pure breath! How it hearkeneth, this"
"8048" 1998 "blessed stillness!"
"8049" 1998 ""
"8050" 1998 "But down there--there speaketh everything, there is everything misheard."
"8051" 1998 "If one announce one's wisdom with bells, the shopmen in the market-place"
"8052" 1998 "will out-jingle it with pennies!"
"8053" 1998 ""
"8054" 1998 "Everything among them talketh; no one knoweth any longer how to"
"8055" 1998 "understand. Everything falleth into the water; nothing falleth any"
"8056" 1998 "longer into deep wells."
"8057" 1998 ""
"8058" 1998 "Everything among them talketh, nothing succeedeth any longer and"
"8059" 1998 "accomplisheth itself. Everything cackleth, but who will still sit"
"8060" 1998 "quietly on the nest and hatch eggs?"
"8061" 1998 ""
"8062" 1998 "Everything among them talketh, everything is out-talked. And that which"
"8063" 1998 "yesterday was still too hard for time itself and its tooth, hangeth"
"8064" 1998 "to-day, outchamped and outchewed, from the mouths of the men of to-day."
"8065" 1998 ""
"8066" 1998 "Everything among them talketh, everything is betrayed. And what was once"
"8067" 1998 "called the secret and secrecy of profound souls, belongeth to-day to the"
"8068" 1998 "street-trumpeters and other butterflies."
"8069" 1998 ""
"8070" 1998 "O human hubbub, thou wonderful thing! Thou noise in dark streets! Now"
"8071" 1998 "art thou again behind me:--my greatest danger lieth behind me!"
"8072" 1998 ""
"8073" 1998 "In indulging and pitying lay ever my greatest danger; and all human"
"8074" 1998 "hubbub wisheth to be indulged and tolerated."
"8075" 1998 ""
"8076" 1998 "With suppressed truths, with fool's hand and befooled heart, and rich in"
"8077" 1998 "petty lies of pity:--thus have I ever lived among men."
"8078" 1998 ""
"8079" 1998 "Disguised did I sit amongst them, ready to misjudge MYSELF that I might"
"8080" 1998 "endure THEM, and willingly saying to myself: \"Thou fool, thou dost not"
"8081" 1998 "know men!\""
"8082" 1998 ""
"8083" 1998 "One unlearneth men when one liveth amongst them: there is too much"
"8084" 1998 "foreground in all men--what can far-seeing, far-longing eyes do THERE!"
"8085" 1998 ""
"8086" 1998 "And, fool that I was, when they misjudged me, I indulged them on that"
"8087" 1998 "account more than myself, being habitually hard on myself, and often"
"8088" 1998 "even taking revenge on myself for the indulgence."
"8089" 1998 ""
"8090" 1998 "Stung all over by poisonous flies, and hollowed like the stone by"
"8091" 1998 "many drops of wickedness: thus did I sit among them, and still said to"
"8092" 1998 "myself: \"Innocent is everything petty of its pettiness!\""
"8093" 1998 ""
"8094" 1998 "Especially did I find those who call themselves \"the good,\" the most"
"8095" 1998 "poisonous flies; they sting in all innocence, they lie in all innocence;"
"8096" 1998 "how COULD they--be just towards me!"
"8097" 1998 ""
"8098" 1998 "He who liveth amongst the good--pity teacheth him to lie. Pity maketh"
"8099" 1998 "stifling air for all free souls. For the stupidity of the good is"
"8100" 1998 "unfathomable."
"8101" 1998 ""
"8102" 1998 "To conceal myself and my riches--THAT did I learn down there: for every"
"8103" 1998 "one did I still find poor in spirit. It was the lie of my pity, that I"
"8104" 1998 "knew in every one,"
"8105" 1998 ""
"8106" 1998 "--That I saw and scented in every one, what was ENOUGH of spirit for"
"8107" 1998 "him, and what was TOO MUCH!"
"8108" 1998 ""
"8109" 1998 "Their stiff wise men: I call them wise, not stiff--thus did I learn to"
"8110" 1998 "slur over words."
"8111" 1998 ""
"8112" 1998 "The grave-diggers dig for themselves diseases. Under old rubbish rest"
"8113" 1998 "bad vapours. One should not stir up the marsh. One should live on"
"8114" 1998 "mountains."
"8115" 1998 ""
"8116" 1998 "With blessed nostrils do I again breathe mountain-freedom. Freed at last"
"8117" 1998 "is my nose from the smell of all human hubbub!"
"8118" 1998 ""
"8119" 1998 "With sharp breezes tickled, as with sparkling wine, SNEEZETH my soul--"
"8120" 1998 "sneezeth, and shouteth self-congratulatingly: \"Health to thee!\""
"8121" 1998 ""
"8122" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"8123" 1998 ""
"8124" 1998 ""
"8125" 1998 ""
"8126" 1998 ""
"8127" 1998 "LIV. THE THREE EVIL THINGS."
"8128" 1998 ""
"8129" 1998 "1."
"8130" 1998 ""
"8131" 1998 "In my dream, in my last morning-dream, I stood to-day on a promontory--"
"8132" 1998 "beyond the world; I held a pair of scales, and WEIGHED the world."
"8133" 1998 ""
"8134" 1998 "Alas, that the rosy dawn came too early to me: she glowed me awake, the"
"8135" 1998 "jealous one! Jealous is she always of the glows of my morning-dream."
"8136" 1998 ""
"8137" 1998 "Measurable by him who hath time, weighable by a good weigher, attainable"
"8138" 1998 "by strong pinions, divinable by divine nut-crackers: thus did my dream"
"8139" 1998 "find the world:--"
"8140" 1998 ""
"8141" 1998 "My dream, a bold sailor, half-ship, half-hurricane, silent as the"
"8142" 1998 "butterfly, impatient as the falcon: how had it the patience and leisure"
"8143" 1998 "to-day for world-weighing!"
"8144" 1998 ""
"8145" 1998 "Did my wisdom perhaps speak secretly to it, my laughing, wide-awake"
"8146" 1998 "day-wisdom, which mocketh at all \"infinite worlds\"? For it saith: \"Where"
"8147" 1998 "force is, there becometh NUMBER the master: it hath more force.\""
"8148" 1998 ""
"8149" 1998 "How confidently did my dream contemplate this finite world, not"
"8150" 1998 "new-fangledly, not old-fangledly, not timidly, not entreatingly:--"
"8151" 1998 ""
"8152" 1998 "--As if a big round apple presented itself to my hand, a ripe golden"
"8153" 1998 "apple, with a coolly-soft, velvety skin:--thus did the world present"
"8154" 1998 "itself unto me:--"
"8155" 1998 ""
"8156" 1998 "--As if a tree nodded unto me, a broad-branched, strong-willed tree,"
"8157" 1998 "curved as a recline and a foot-stool for weary travellers: thus did the"
"8158" 1998 "world stand on my promontory:--"
"8159" 1998 ""
