"8160" 1998 "--As if delicate hands carried a casket towards me--a casket open for"
"8161" 1998 "the delectation of modest adoring eyes: thus did the world present"
"8162" 1998 "itself before me to-day:--"
"8163" 1998 ""
"8164" 1998 "--Not riddle enough to scare human love from it, not solution enough"
"8165" 1998 "to put to sleep human wisdom:--a humanly good thing was the world to me"
"8166" 1998 "to-day, of which such bad things are said!"
"8167" 1998 ""
"8168" 1998 "How I thank my morning-dream that I thus at to-day's dawn, weighed"
"8169" 1998 "the world! As a humanly good thing did it come unto me, this dream and"
"8170" 1998 "heart-comforter!"
"8171" 1998 ""
"8172" 1998 "And that I may do the like by day, and imitate and copy its best, now"
"8173" 1998 "will I put the three worst things on the scales, and weigh them humanly"
"8174" 1998 "well.--"
"8175" 1998 ""
"8176" 1998 "He who taught to bless taught also to curse: what are the three best"
"8177" 1998 "cursed things in the world? These will I put on the scales."
"8178" 1998 ""
"8179" 1998 "VOLUPTUOUSNESS, PASSION FOR POWER, and SELFISHNESS: these three things"
"8180" 1998 "have hitherto been best cursed, and have been in worst and falsest"
"8181" 1998 "repute--these three things will I weigh humanly well."
"8182" 1998 ""
"8183" 1998 "Well! Here is my promontory, and there is the sea--IT rolleth hither"
"8184" 1998 "unto me, shaggily and fawningly, the old, faithful, hundred-headed"
"8185" 1998 "dog-monster that I love!--"
"8186" 1998 ""
"8187" 1998 "Well! Here will I hold the scales over the weltering sea: and also a"
"8188" 1998 "witness do I choose to look on--thee, the anchorite-tree, thee, the"
"8189" 1998 "strong-odoured, broad-arched tree that I love!--"
"8190" 1998 ""
"8191" 1998 "On what bridge goeth the now to the hereafter? By what constraint doth"
"8192" 1998 "the high stoop to the low? And what enjoineth even the highest still--to"
"8193" 1998 "grow upwards?--"
"8194" 1998 ""
"8195" 1998 "Now stand the scales poised and at rest: three heavy questions have I"
"8196" 1998 "thrown in; three heavy answers carrieth the other scale."
"8197" 1998 ""
"8198" 1998 "2."
"8199" 1998 ""
"8200" 1998 "Voluptuousness: unto all hair-shirted despisers of the body, a sting and"
"8201" 1998 "stake; and, cursed as \"the world,\" by all backworldsmen: for it mocketh"
"8202" 1998 "and befooleth all erring, misinferring teachers."
"8203" 1998 ""
"8204" 1998 "Voluptuousness: to the rabble, the slow fire at which it is burnt;"
"8205" 1998 "to all wormy wood, to all stinking rags, the prepared heat and stew"
"8206" 1998 "furnace."
"8207" 1998 ""
"8208" 1998 "Voluptuousness: to free hearts, a thing innocent and free, the"
"8209" 1998 "garden-happiness of the earth, all the future's thanks-overflow to the"
"8210" 1998 "present."
"8211" 1998 ""
"8212" 1998 "Voluptuousness: only to the withered a sweet poison; to the lion-willed,"
"8213" 1998 "however, the great cordial, and the reverently saved wine of wines."
"8214" 1998 ""
"8215" 1998 "Voluptuousness: the great symbolic happiness of a higher happiness"
"8216" 1998 "and highest hope. For to many is marriage promised, and more than"
"8217" 1998 "marriage,--"
"8218" 1998 ""
"8219" 1998 "--To many that are more unknown to each other than man and woman:--and"
"8220" 1998 "who hath fully understood HOW UNKNOWN to each other are man and woman!"
"8221" 1998 ""
"8222" 1998 "Voluptuousness:--but I will have hedges around my thoughts, and"
"8223" 1998 "even around my words, lest swine and libertine should break into my"
"8224" 1998 "gardens!--"
"8225" 1998 ""
"8226" 1998 "Passion for power: the glowing scourge of the hardest of the heart-hard;"
"8227" 1998 "the cruel torture reserved for the cruellest themselves; the gloomy"
"8228" 1998 "flame of living pyres."
"8229" 1998 ""
"8230" 1998 "Passion for power: the wicked gadfly which is mounted on the vainest"
"8231" 1998 "peoples; the scorner of all uncertain virtue; which rideth on every"
"8232" 1998 "horse and on every pride."
"8233" 1998 ""
"8234" 1998 "Passion for power: the earthquake which breaketh and upbreaketh all"
"8235" 1998 "that is rotten and hollow; the rolling, rumbling, punitive demolisher"
"8236" 1998 "of whited sepulchres; the flashing interrogative-sign beside premature"
"8237" 1998 "answers."
"8238" 1998 ""
"8239" 1998 "Passion for power: before whose glance man creepeth and croucheth and"
"8240" 1998 "drudgeth, and becometh lower than the serpent and the swine:--until at"
"8241" 1998 "last great contempt crieth out of him--,"
"8242" 1998 ""
"8243" 1998 "Passion for power: the terrible teacher of great contempt, which"
"8244" 1998 "preacheth to their face to cities and empires: \"Away with thee!\"--until"
"8245" 1998 "a voice crieth out of themselves: \"Away with ME!\""
"8246" 1998 ""
"8247" 1998 "Passion for power: which, however, mounteth alluringly even to the pure"
"8248" 1998 "and lonesome, and up to self-satisfied elevations, glowing like a love"
"8249" 1998 "that painteth purple felicities alluringly on earthly heavens."
"8250" 1998 ""
"8251" 1998 "Passion for power: but who would call it PASSION, when the height"
"8252" 1998 "longeth to stoop for power! Verily, nothing sick or diseased is there in"
"8253" 1998 "such longing and descending!"
"8254" 1998 ""
"8255" 1998 "That the lonesome height may not for ever remain lonesome and"
"8256" 1998 "self-sufficing; that the mountains may come to the valleys and the winds"
"8257" 1998 "of the heights to the plains:--"
"8258" 1998 ""
"8259" 1998 "Oh, who could find the right prenomen and honouring name for such"
"8260" 1998 "longing! \"Bestowing virtue\"--thus did Zarathustra once name the"
"8261" 1998 "unnamable."
"8262" 1998 ""
"8263" 1998 "And then it happened also,--and verily, it happened for the first"
"8264" 1998 "time!--that his word blessed SELFISHNESS, the wholesome, healthy"
"8265" 1998 "selfishness, that springeth from the powerful soul:--"
"8266" 1998 ""
"8267" 1998 "--From the powerful soul, to which the high body appertaineth, the"
"8268" 1998 "handsome, triumphing, refreshing body, around which everything becometh"
"8269" 1998 "a mirror:"
"8270" 1998 ""
"8271" 1998 "--The pliant, persuasive body, the dancer, whose symbol and epitome"
"8272" 1998 "is the self-enjoying soul. Of such bodies and souls the self-enjoyment"
"8273" 1998 "calleth itself \"virtue.\""
"8274" 1998 ""
"8275" 1998 "With its words of good and bad doth such self-enjoyment shelter itself"
"8276" 1998 "as with sacred groves; with the names of its happiness doth it banish"
"8277" 1998 "from itself everything contemptible."
"8278" 1998 ""
"8279" 1998 "Away from itself doth it banish everything cowardly; it saith:"
"8280" 1998 "\"Bad--THAT IS cowardly!\" Contemptible seem to it the ever-solicitous,"
"8281" 1998 "the sighing, the complaining, and whoever pick up the most trifling"
"8282" 1998 "advantage."
"8283" 1998 ""
"8284" 1998 "It despiseth also all bitter-sweet wisdom: for verily, there is also"
"8285" 1998 "wisdom that bloometh in the dark, a night-shade wisdom, which ever"
"8286" 1998 "sigheth: \"All is vain!\""
"8287" 1998 ""
"8288" 1998 "Shy distrust is regarded by it as base, and every one who wanteth oaths"
"8289" 1998 "instead of looks and hands: also all over-distrustful wisdom,--for such"
"8290" 1998 "is the mode of cowardly souls."
"8291" 1998 ""
"8292" 1998 "Baser still it regardeth the obsequious, doggish one, who immediately"
"8293" 1998 "lieth on his back, the submissive one; and there is also wisdom that is"
"8294" 1998 "submissive, and doggish, and pious, and obsequious."
"8295" 1998 ""
"8296" 1998 "Hateful to it altogether, and a loathing, is he who will never defend"
"8297" 1998 "himself, he who swalloweth down poisonous spittle and bad looks, the"
"8298" 1998 "all-too-patient one, the all-endurer, the all-satisfied one: for that is"
"8299" 1998 "the mode of slaves."
"8300" 1998 ""
"8301" 1998 "Whether they be servile before Gods and divine spurnings, or before men"
"8302" 1998 "and stupid human opinions: at ALL kinds of slaves doth it spit, this"
"8303" 1998 "blessed selfishness!"
"8304" 1998 ""
"8305" 1998 "Bad: thus doth it call all that is spirit-broken, and"
"8306" 1998 "sordidly-servile--constrained, blinking eyes, depressed hearts, and the"
"8307" 1998 "false submissive style, which kisseth with broad cowardly lips."
"8308" 1998 ""
"8309" 1998 "And spurious wisdom: so doth it call all the wit that slaves, and"
"8310" 1998 "hoary-headed and weary ones affect; and especially all the cunning,"
"8311" 1998 "spurious-witted, curious-witted foolishness of priests!"
"8312" 1998 ""
"8313" 1998 "The spurious wise, however, all the priests, the world-weary, and those"
"8314" 1998 "whose souls are of feminine and servile nature--oh, how hath their game"
"8315" 1998 "all along abused selfishness!"
"8316" 1998 ""
"8317" 1998 "And precisely THAT was to be virtue and was to be called virtue--to"
"8318" 1998 "abuse selfishness! And \"selfless\"--so did they wish themselves with good"
"8319" 1998 "reason, all those world-weary cowards and cross-spiders!"
"8320" 1998 ""
"8321" 1998 "But to all those cometh now the day, the change, the sword of judgment,"
"8322" 1998 "THE GREAT NOONTIDE: then shall many things be revealed!"
"8323" 1998 ""
"8324" 1998 "And he who proclaimeth the EGO wholesome and holy, and selfishness"
"8325" 1998 "blessed, verily, he, the prognosticator, speaketh also what he knoweth:"
"8326" 1998 "\"BEHOLD, IT COMETH, IT IS NIGH, THE GREAT NOONTIDE!\""
"8327" 1998 ""
"8328" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"8329" 1998 ""
"8330" 1998 ""
"8331" 1998 ""
"8332" 1998 ""
"8333" 1998 "LV. THE SPIRIT OF GRAVITY."
"8334" 1998 ""
"8335" 1998 "1."
"8336" 1998 ""
"8337" 1998 "My mouthpiece--is of the people: too coarsely and cordially do I"
"8338" 1998 "talk for Angora rabbits. And still stranger soundeth my word unto all"
"8339" 1998 "ink-fish and pen-foxes."
"8340" 1998 ""
"8341" 1998 "My hand--is a fool's hand: woe unto all tables and walls, and whatever"
"8342" 1998 "hath room for fool's sketching, fool's scrawling!"
"8343" 1998 ""
"8344" 1998 "My foot--is a horse-foot; therewith do I trample and trot over stick and"
"8345" 1998 "stone, in the fields up and down, and am bedevilled with delight in all"
"8346" 1998 "fast racing."
"8347" 1998 ""
"8348" 1998 "My stomach--is surely an eagle's stomach? For it preferreth lamb's"
"8349" 1998 "flesh. Certainly it is a bird's stomach."
"8350" 1998 ""
"8351" 1998 "Nourished with innocent things, and with few, ready and impatient"
"8352" 1998 "to fly, to fly away--that is now my nature: why should there not be"
"8353" 1998 "something of bird-nature therein!"
"8354" 1998 ""
"8355" 1998 "And especially that I am hostile to the spirit of gravity, that is"
"8356" 1998 "bird-nature:--verily, deadly hostile, supremely hostile, originally"
"8357" 1998 "hostile! Oh, whither hath my hostility not flown and misflown!"
"8358" 1998 ""
"8359" 1998 "Thereof could I sing a song--and WILL sing it: though I be alone in an"
"8360" 1998 "empty house, and must sing it to mine own ears."
"8361" 1998 ""
"8362" 1998 "Other singers are there, to be sure, to whom only the full house"
"8363" 1998 "maketh the voice soft, the hand eloquent, the eye expressive, the heart"
"8364" 1998 "wakeful:--those do I not resemble.--"
"8365" 1998 ""
"8366" 1998 "2."
"8367" 1998 ""
"8368" 1998 "He who one day teacheth men to fly will have shifted all landmarks; to"
"8369" 1998 "him will all landmarks themselves fly into the air; the earth will he"
"8370" 1998 "christen anew--as \"the light body.\""
"8371" 1998 ""
"8372" 1998 "The ostrich runneth faster than the fastest horse, but it also thrusteth"
"8373" 1998 "its head heavily into the heavy earth: thus is it with the man who"
"8374" 1998 "cannot yet fly."
"8375" 1998 ""
"8376" 1998 "Heavy unto him are earth and life, and so WILLETH the spirit of gravity!"
"8377" 1998 "But he who would become light, and be a bird, must love himself:--thus"
"8378" 1998 "do _I_ teach."
"8379" 1998 ""
"8380" 1998 "Not, to be sure, with the love of the sick and infected, for with them"
"8381" 1998 "stinketh even self-love!"
"8382" 1998 ""
"8383" 1998 "One must learn to love oneself--thus do I teach--with a wholesome and"
"8384" 1998 "healthy love: that one may endure to be with oneself, and not go roving"
"8385" 1998 "about."
"8386" 1998 ""
"8387" 1998 "Such roving about christeneth itself \"brotherly love\"; with these words"
"8388" 1998 "hath there hitherto been the best lying and dissembling, and especially"
"8389" 1998 "by those who have been burdensome to every one."
"8390" 1998 ""
"8391" 1998 "And verily, it is no commandment for to-day and to-morrow to LEARN to"
"8392" 1998 "love oneself. Rather is it of all arts the finest, subtlest, last and"
"8393" 1998 "patientest."
"8394" 1998 ""
"8395" 1998 "For to its possessor is all possession well concealed, and of all"
"8396" 1998 "treasure-pits one's own is last excavated--so causeth the spirit of"
"8397" 1998 "gravity."
"8398" 1998 ""
"8399" 1998 "Almost in the cradle are we apportioned with heavy words and worths:"
"8400" 1998 "\"good\" and \"evil\"--so calleth itself this dowry. For the sake of it we"
"8401" 1998 "are forgiven for living."
"8402" 1998 ""
"8403" 1998 "And therefore suffereth one little children to come unto one, to forbid"
"8404" 1998 "them betimes to love themselves--so causeth the spirit of gravity."
"8405" 1998 ""
"8406" 1998 "And we--we bear loyally what is apportioned unto us, on hard shoulders,"
"8407" 1998 "over rugged mountains! And when we sweat, then do people say to us:"
"8408" 1998 "\"Yea, life is hard to bear!\""
"8409" 1998 ""
"8410" 1998 "But man himself only is hard to bear! The reason thereof is that he"
"8411" 1998 "carrieth too many extraneous things on his shoulders. Like the camel"
"8412" 1998 "kneeleth he down, and letteth himself be well laden."
"8413" 1998 ""
"8414" 1998 "Especially the strong load-bearing man in whom reverence resideth. Too"
"8415" 1998 "many EXTRANEOUS heavy words and worths loadeth he upon himself--then"
"8416" 1998 "seemeth life to him a desert!"
"8417" 1998 ""
"8418" 1998 "And verily! Many a thing also that is OUR OWN is hard to bear! And many"
"8419" 1998 "internal things in man are like the oyster--repulsive and slippery and"
"8420" 1998 "hard to grasp;--"
"8421" 1998 ""
"8422" 1998 "So that an elegant shell, with elegant adornment, must plead for"
"8423" 1998 "them. But this art also must one learn: to HAVE a shell, and a fine"
"8424" 1998 "appearance, and sagacious blindness!"
"8425" 1998 ""
"8426" 1998 "Again, it deceiveth about many things in man, that many a shell is poor"
"8427" 1998 "and pitiable, and too much of a shell. Much concealed goodness and power"
"8428" 1998 "is never dreamt of; the choicest dainties find no tasters!"
"8429" 1998 ""
"8430" 1998 "Women know that, the choicest of them: a little fatter a little leaner--"
"8431" 1998 "oh, how much fate is in so little!"
"8432" 1998 ""
"8433" 1998 "Man is difficult to discover, and unto himself most difficult of all;"
"8434" 1998 "often lieth the spirit concerning the soul. So causeth the spirit of"
"8435" 1998 "gravity."
"8436" 1998 ""
"8437" 1998 "He, however, hath discovered himself who saith: This is MY good and"
"8438" 1998 "evil: therewith hath he silenced the mole and the dwarf, who say: \"Good"
"8439" 1998 "for all, evil for all.\""
"8440" 1998 ""
"8441" 1998 "Verily, neither do I like those who call everything good, and this world"
"8442" 1998 "the best of all. Those do I call the all-satisfied."
"8443" 1998 ""
"8444" 1998 "All-satisfiedness, which knoweth how to taste everything,--that is"
"8445" 1998 "not the best taste! I honour the refractory, fastidious tongues and"
"8446" 1998 "stomachs, which have learned to say \"I\" and \"Yea\" and \"Nay.\""
"8447" 1998 ""
"8448" 1998 "To chew and digest everything, however--that is the genuine"
"8449" 1998 "swine-nature! Ever to say YE-A--that hath only the ass learnt, and those"
"8450" 1998 "like it!--"
"8451" 1998 ""
"8452" 1998 "Deep yellow and hot red--so wanteth MY taste--it mixeth blood with all"
"8453" 1998 "colours. He, however, who whitewasheth his house, betrayeth unto me a"
"8454" 1998 "whitewashed soul."
"8455" 1998 ""
"8456" 1998 "With mummies, some fall in love; others with phantoms: both alike"
"8457" 1998 "hostile to all flesh and blood--oh, how repugnant are both to my taste!"
"8458" 1998 "For I love blood."
"8459" 1998 ""
"8460" 1998 "And there will I not reside and abide where every one spitteth and"
"8461" 1998 "speweth: that is now MY taste,--rather would I live amongst thieves and"
"8462" 1998 "perjurers. Nobody carrieth gold in his mouth."
"8463" 1998 ""
"8464" 1998 "Still more repugnant unto me, however, are all lickspittles; and the"
"8465" 1998 "most repugnant animal of man that I found, did I christen \"parasite\": it"
"8466" 1998 "would not love, and would yet live by love."
"8467" 1998 ""
"8468" 1998 "Unhappy do I call all those who have only one choice: either to become"
"8469" 1998 "evil beasts, or evil beast-tamers. Amongst such would I not build my"
"8470" 1998 "tabernacle."
"8471" 1998 ""
"8472" 1998 "Unhappy do I also call those who have ever to WAIT,--they are repugnant"
"8473" 1998 "to my taste--all the toll-gatherers and traders, and kings, and other"
"8474" 1998 "landkeepers and shopkeepers."
"8475" 1998 ""
"8476" 1998 "Verily, I learned waiting also, and thoroughly so,--but only waiting for"
"8477" 1998 "MYSELF. And above all did I learn standing and walking and running and"
"8478" 1998 "leaping and climbing and dancing."
"8479" 1998 ""
"8480" 1998 "This however is my teaching: he who wisheth one day to fly, must first"
"8481" 1998 "learn standing and walking and running and climbing and dancing:--one"
"8482" 1998 "doth not fly into flying!"
"8483" 1998 ""
"8484" 1998 "With rope-ladders learned I to reach many a window, with nimble legs did"
"8485" 1998 "I climb high masts: to sit on high masts of perception seemed to me no"
"8486" 1998 "small bliss;--"
"8487" 1998 ""
"8488" 1998 "--To flicker like small flames on high masts: a small light, certainly,"
"8489" 1998 "but a great comfort to cast-away sailors and ship-wrecked ones!"
"8490" 1998 ""
"8491" 1998 "By divers ways and wendings did I arrive at my truth; not by one ladder"
"8492" 1998 "did I mount to the height where mine eye roveth into my remoteness."
"8493" 1998 ""
"8494" 1998 "And unwillingly only did I ask my way--that was always counter to my"
"8495" 1998 "taste! Rather did I question and test the ways themselves."
"8496" 1998 ""
"8497" 1998 "A testing and a questioning hath been all my travelling:--and verily,"
"8498" 1998 "one must also LEARN to answer such questioning! That, however,--is my"
"8499" 1998 "taste:"
"8500" 1998 ""
"8501" 1998 "--Neither a good nor a bad taste, but MY taste, of which I have no"
"8502" 1998 "longer either shame or secrecy."
"8503" 1998 ""
"8504" 1998 "\"This--is now MY way,--where is yours?\" Thus did I answer those who"
"8505" 1998 "asked me \"the way.\" For THE way--it doth not exist!"
"8506" 1998 ""
"8507" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"8508" 1998 ""
"8509" 1998 ""
"8510" 1998 ""
"8511" 1998 ""
"8512" 1998 "LVI. OLD AND NEW TABLES."
"8513" 1998 ""
"8514" 1998 "1."
"8515" 1998 ""
"8516" 1998 "Here do I sit and wait, old broken tables around me and also new"
"8517" 1998 "half-written tables. When cometh mine hour?"
"8518" 1998 ""
"8519" 1998 "--The hour of my descent, of my down-going: for once more will I go unto"
"8520" 1998 "men."
"8521" 1998 ""
"8522" 1998 "For that hour do I now wait: for first must the signs come unto me that"
"8523" 1998 "it is MINE hour--namely, the laughing lion with the flock of doves."
"8524" 1998 ""
"8525" 1998 "Meanwhile do I talk to myself as one who hath time. No one telleth me"
"8526" 1998 "anything new, so I tell myself mine own story."
"8527" 1998 ""
"8528" 1998 "2."
"8529" 1998 ""
"8530" 1998 "When I came unto men, then found I them resting on an old infatuation:"
"8531" 1998 "all of them thought they had long known what was good and bad for men."
"8532" 1998 ""
"8533" 1998 "An old wearisome business seemed to them all discourse about virtue; and"
"8534" 1998 "he who wished to sleep well spake of \"good\" and \"bad\" ere retiring to"
"8535" 1998 "rest."
"8536" 1998 ""
"8537" 1998 "This somnolence did I disturb when I taught that NO ONE YET KNOWETH what"
"8538" 1998 "is good and bad:--unless it be the creating one!"
"8539" 1998 ""
"8540" 1998 "--It is he, however, who createth man's goal, and giveth to the earth"
"8541" 1998 "its meaning and its future: he only EFFECTETH it THAT aught is good or"
"8542" 1998 "bad."
"8543" 1998 ""
"8544" 1998 "And I bade them upset their old academic chairs, and wherever that old"
"8545" 1998 "infatuation had sat; I bade them laugh at their great moralists, their"
"8546" 1998 "saints, their poets, and their Saviours."
"8547" 1998 ""
"8548" 1998 "At their gloomy sages did I bid them laugh, and whoever had sat"
"8549" 1998 "admonishing as a black scarecrow on the tree of life."
"8550" 1998 ""
"8551" 1998 "On their great grave-highway did I seat myself, and even beside the"
"8552" 1998 "carrion and vultures--and I laughed at all their bygone and its mellow"
"8553" 1998 "decaying glory."
"8554" 1998 ""
"8555" 1998 "Verily, like penitential preachers and fools did I cry wrath and shame"
"8556" 1998 "on all their greatness and smallness. Oh, that their best is so very"
"8557" 1998 "small! Oh, that their worst is so very small! Thus did I laugh."
"8558" 1998 ""
"8559" 1998 "Thus did my wise longing, born in the mountains, cry and laugh in me; a"
"8560" 1998 "wild wisdom, verily!--my great pinion-rustling longing."
"8561" 1998 ""
"8562" 1998 "And oft did it carry me off and up and away and in the midst of"
"8563" 1998 "laughter; then flew I quivering like an arrow with sun-intoxicated"
"8564" 1998 "rapture:"
"8565" 1998 ""
"8566" 1998 "--Out into distant futures, which no dream hath yet seen, into warmer"
"8567" 1998 "souths than ever sculptor conceived,--where gods in their dancing are"
"8568" 1998 "ashamed of all clothes:"
"8569" 1998 ""
"8570" 1998 "(That I may speak in parables and halt and stammer like the poets: and"
"8571" 1998 "verily I am ashamed that I have still to be a poet!)"
"8572" 1998 ""
"8573" 1998 "Where all becoming seemed to me dancing of Gods, and wantoning of Gods,"
"8574" 1998 "and the world unloosed and unbridled and fleeing back to itself:--"
"8575" 1998 ""
"8576" 1998 "--As an eternal self-fleeing and re-seeking of one another of many Gods,"
"8577" 1998 "as the blessed self-contradicting, recommuning, and refraternising with"
"8578" 1998 "one another of many Gods:--"
"8579" 1998 ""
"8580" 1998 "Where all time seemed to me a blessed mockery of moments, where"
"8581" 1998 "necessity was freedom itself, which played happily with the goad of"
"8582" 1998 "freedom:--"
"8583" 1998 ""
"8584" 1998 "Where I also found again mine old devil and arch-enemy, the spirit"
"8585" 1998 "of gravity, and all that it created: constraint, law, necessity and"
"8586" 1998 "consequence and purpose and will and good and evil:--"
"8587" 1998 ""
"8588" 1998 "For must there not be that which is danced OVER, danced beyond? Must"
"8589" 1998 "there not, for the sake of the nimble, the nimblest,--be moles and"
"8590" 1998 "clumsy dwarfs?--"
"8591" 1998 ""
"8592" 1998 "3."
"8593" 1998 ""
"8594" 1998 "There was it also where I picked up from the path the word \"Superman,\""
"8595" 1998 "and that man is something that must be surpassed."
"8596" 1998 ""
"8597" 1998 "--That man is a bridge and not a goal--rejoicing over his noontides and"
"8598" 1998 "evenings, as advances to new rosy dawns:"
"8599" 1998 ""
"8600" 1998 "--The Zarathustra word of the great noontide, and whatever else I have"
"8601" 1998 "hung up over men like purple evening-afterglows."
"8602" 1998 ""
"8603" 1998 "Verily, also new stars did I make them see, along with new nights;"
"8604" 1998 "and over cloud and day and night, did I spread out laughter like a"
"8605" 1998 "gay-coloured canopy."
"8606" 1998 ""
"8607" 1998 "I taught them all MY poetisation and aspiration: to compose and collect"
"8608" 1998 "into unity what is fragment in man, and riddle and fearful chance;--"
"8609" 1998 ""
"8610" 1998 "--As composer, riddle-reader, and redeemer of chance, did I teach them"
"8611" 1998 "to create the future, and all that HATH BEEN--to redeem by creating."
"8612" 1998 ""
"8613" 1998 "The past of man to redeem, and every \"It was\" to transform, until the"
"8614" 1998 "Will saith: \"But so did I will it! So shall I will it--\""
"8615" 1998 ""
"8616" 1998 "--This did I call redemption; this alone taught I them to call"
"8617" 1998 "redemption.--"
"8618" 1998 ""
"8619" 1998 "Now do I await MY redemption--that I may go unto them for the last time."
"8620" 1998 ""
"8621" 1998 "For once more will I go unto men: AMONGST them will my sun set; in dying"
"8622" 1998 "will I give them my choicest gift!"
"8623" 1998 ""
"8624" 1998 "From the sun did I learn this, when it goeth down, the exuberant one:"
"8625" 1998 "gold doth it then pour into the sea, out of inexhaustible riches,--"
"8626" 1998 ""
"8627" 1998 "--So that the poorest fisherman roweth even with GOLDEN oars! For this"
"8628" 1998 "did I once see, and did not tire of weeping in beholding it.--"
"8629" 1998 ""
"8630" 1998 "Like the sun will also Zarathustra go down: now sitteth he here"
"8631" 1998 "and waiteth, old broken tables around him, and also new"
"8632" 1998 "tables--half-written."
"8633" 1998 ""
"8634" 1998 "4."
"8635" 1998 ""
"8636" 1998 "Behold, here is a new table; but where are my brethren who will carry it"
"8637" 1998 "with me to the valley and into hearts of flesh?--"
"8638" 1998 ""
"8639" 1998 "Thus demandeth my great love to the remotest ones: BE NOT CONSIDERATE OF"
"8640" 1998 "THY NEIGHBOUR! Man is something that must be surpassed."
"8641" 1998 ""
"8642" 1998 "There are many divers ways and modes of surpassing: see THOU thereto!"
"8643" 1998 "But only a buffoon thinketh: \"man can also be OVERLEAPT.\""
"8644" 1998 ""
"8645" 1998 "Surpass thyself even in thy neighbour: and a right which thou canst"
"8646" 1998 "seize upon, shalt thou not allow to be given thee!"
"8647" 1998 ""
"8648" 1998 "What thou doest can no one do to thee again. Lo, there is no requital."
"8649" 1998 ""
"8650" 1998 "He who cannot command himself shall obey. And many a one CAN command"
"8651" 1998 "himself, but still sorely lacketh self-obedience!"
"8652" 1998 ""
"8653" 1998 "5."
"8654" 1998 ""
"8655" 1998 "Thus wisheth the type of noble souls: they desire to have nothing"
"8656" 1998 "GRATUITOUSLY, least of all, life."
"8657" 1998 ""
"8658" 1998 "He who is of the populace wisheth to live gratuitously; we others,"
"8659" 1998 "however, to whom life hath given itself--we are ever considering WHAT we"
"8660" 1998 "can best give IN RETURN!"
"8661" 1998 ""
"8662" 1998 "And verily, it is a noble dictum which saith: \"What life promiseth US,"
"8663" 1998 "that promise will WE keep--to life!\""
"8664" 1998 ""
"8665" 1998 "One should not wish to enjoy where one doth not contribute to the"
"8666" 1998 "enjoyment. And one should not WISH to enjoy!"
"8667" 1998 ""
"8668" 1998 "For enjoyment and innocence are the most bashful things. Neither like"
"8669" 1998 "to be sought for. One should HAVE them,--but one should rather SEEK for"
"8670" 1998 "guilt and pain!--"
"8671" 1998 ""
"8672" 1998 "6."
"8673" 1998 ""
"8674" 1998 "O my brethren, he who is a firstling is ever sacrificed. Now, however,"
"8675" 1998 "are we firstlings!"
"8676" 1998 ""
"8677" 1998 "We all bleed on secret sacrificial altars, we all burn and broil in"
"8678" 1998 "honour of ancient idols."
"8679" 1998 ""
"8680" 1998 "Our best is still young: this exciteth old palates. Our flesh is tender,"
"8681" 1998 "our skin is only lambs' skin:--how could we not excite old idol-priests!"
"8682" 1998 ""
"8683" 1998 "IN OURSELVES dwelleth he still, the old idol-priest, who broileth our"
"8684" 1998 "best for his banquet. Ah, my brethren, how could firstlings fail to be"
"8685" 1998 "sacrifices!"
"8686" 1998 ""
"8687" 1998 "But so wisheth our type; and I love those who do not wish to preserve"
"8688" 1998 "themselves, the down-going ones do I love with mine entire love: for"
"8689" 1998 "they go beyond.--"
"8690" 1998 ""
"8691" 1998 "7."
"8692" 1998 ""
"8693" 1998 "To be true--that CAN few be! And he who can, will not! Least of all,"
"8694" 1998 "however, can the good be true."
"8695" 1998 ""
"8696" 1998 "Oh, those good ones! GOOD MEN NEVER SPEAK THE TRUTH. For the spirit,"
"8697" 1998 "thus to be good, is a malady."
"8698" 1998 ""
"8699" 1998 "They yield, those good ones, they submit themselves; their heart"
"8700" 1998 "repeateth, their soul obeyeth: HE, however, who obeyeth, DOTH NOT LISTEN"
"8701" 1998 "TO HIMSELF!"
"8702" 1998 ""
"8703" 1998 "All that is called evil by the good, must come together in order that"
"8704" 1998 "one truth may be born. O my brethren, are ye also evil enough for THIS"
"8705" 1998 "truth?"
"8706" 1998 ""
"8707" 1998 "The daring venture, the prolonged distrust, the cruel Nay, the tedium,"

"8709" 1998 "such seed, however--is truth produced!"
"8710" 1998 ""
"8711" 1998 "BESIDE the bad conscience hath hitherto grown all KNOWLEDGE! Break up,"
"8712" 1998 "break up, ye discerning ones, the old tables!"
"8713" 1998 ""
"8714" 1998 "8."
"8715" 1998 ""
"8716" 1998 "When the water hath planks, when gangways and railings o'erspan the"
"8717" 1998 "stream, verily, he is not believed who then saith: \"All is in flux.\""
"8718" 1998 ""
"8719" 1998 "But even the simpletons contradict him. \"What?\" say the simpletons, \"all"
"8720" 1998 "in flux? Planks and railings are still OVER the stream!"
"8721" 1998 ""
"8722" 1998 "\"OVER the stream all is stable, all the values of things, the bridges"
"8723" 1998 "and bearings, all 'good' and 'evil': these are all STABLE!\"--"
"8724" 1998 ""
"8725" 1998 "Cometh, however, the hard winter, the stream-tamer, then learn even the"
"8726" 1998 "wittiest distrust, and verily, not only the simpletons then say: \"Should"
"8727" 1998 "not everything--STAND STILL?\""
"8728" 1998 ""
"8729" 1998 "\"Fundamentally standeth everything still\"--that is an appropriate winter"
"8730" 1998 "doctrine, good cheer for an unproductive period, a great comfort for"
"8731" 1998 "winter-sleepers and fireside-loungers."
"8732" 1998 ""
"8733" 1998 "\"Fundamentally standeth everything still\"--: but CONTRARY thereto,"
"8734" 1998 "preacheth the thawing wind!"
"8735" 1998 ""
"8736" 1998 "The thawing wind, a bullock, which is no ploughing bullock--a furious"

"8738" 1998 "however--BREAKETH GANGWAYS!"
"8739" 1998 ""
"8740" 1998 "O my brethren, is not everything AT PRESENT IN FLUX? Have not all"
"8741" 1998 "railings and gangways fallen into the water? Who would still HOLD ON to"
"8742" 1998 "\"good\" and \"evil\"?"
"8743" 1998 ""
"8744" 1998 "\"Woe to us! Hail to us! The thawing wind bloweth!\"--Thus preach, my"
"8745" 1998 "brethren, through all the streets!"
"8746" 1998 ""
"8747" 1998 "9."
"8748" 1998 ""
"8749" 1998 "There is an old illusion--it is called good and evil. Around soothsayers"
"8750" 1998 "and astrologers hath hitherto revolved the orbit of this illusion."
"8751" 1998 ""

"8754" 1998 ""
"8755" 1998 "Then again did one distrust all soothsayers and astrologers; and"

"8757" 1998 "willest!\""
"8758" 1998 ""
"8759" 1998 "O my brethren, concerning the stars and the future there hath hitherto"
"8760" 1998 "been only illusion, and not knowledge; and THEREFORE concerning good and"

"8763" 1998 "10."
"8764" 1998 ""

"8779" 1998 "11."
"8780" 1998 ""
"8781" 1998 "It is my sympathy with all the past that I see it is abandoned,--"
"8782" 1998 ""
"8783" 1998 "--Abandoned to the favour, the spirit and the madness of every"
"8784" 1998 "generation that cometh, and reinterpreteth all that hath been as its"

"8786" 1998 ""

"8801" 1998 ""
"8802" 1998 "For many noble ones are needed, and many kinds of noble ones, FOR A NEW"

"8805" 1998 ""

"8817" 1998 ""

"8848" 1998 "13."
"8849" 1998 ""

"8859" 1998 ""

"8880" 1998 ""

"8892" 1998 ""

"8896" 1998 "15."
"8897" 1998 ""

"8901" 1998 ""
"8902" 1998 "\"Let the world be as it is! Raise not a finger against it!\""

"8915" 1998 ""

"8939" 1998 "And such is always the nature of weak men: they lose themselves on their"

"8951" 1998 ""

"8958" 1998 "17."
"8959" 1998 ""

"8994" 1998 ""
"8995" 1998 "O my brethren, there are tables which weariness framed, and tables"

"8998" 1998 ""
"8999" 1998 "See this languishing one! Only a span-breadth is he from his goal; but"

"9002" 1998 ""

"9005" 1998 ""
"9006" 1998 "Now gloweth the sun upon him, and the dogs lick at his sweat: but he"

"9008" 1998 ""
"9009" 1998 "--A span-breadth from his goal, to languish! Verily, ye will have to"

"9011" 1998 ""

"9014" 1998 ""

"9018" 1998 ""
"9019" 1998 "Only, my brethren, see that ye scare the dogs away from him, the idle"

"9021" 1998 ""

"9024" 1998 ""
"9025" 1998 "19."
"9026" 1998 ""
"9027" 1998 "I form circles around me and holy boundaries; ever fewer ascend with"

"9030" 1998 ""
"9031" 1998 "But wherever ye would ascend with me, O my brethren, take care lest a"

"9033" 1998 ""
"9034" 1998 "A parasite: that is a reptile, a creeping, cringing reptile, that trieth"

"9036" 1998 ""
"9037" 1998 "And THIS is its art: it divineth where ascending souls are weary, in"

"9039" 1998 "loathsome nest."
"9040" 1998 ""
"9041" 1998 "Where the strong are weak, where the noble are all-too-gentle--there"
"9042" 1998 "buildeth it its loathsome nest; the parasite liveth where the great have"
"9043" 1998 "small sore-places."
"9044" 1998 ""
"9045" 1998 "What is the highest of all species of being, and what is the lowest?"
"9046" 1998 "The parasite is the lowest species; he, however, who is of the highest"
"9047" 1998 "species feedeth most parasites."

"9345" 1998 "LVII. THE CONVALESCENT."
"9346" 1998 ""
"9347" 1998 "1."
"9348" 1998 ""
"9349" 1998 "One morning, not long after his return to his cave, Zarathustra sprang"
"9350" 1998 "up from his couch like a madman, crying with a frightful voice, and"
"9351" 1998 "acting as if some one still lay on the couch who did not wish to rise."
"9352" 1998 "Zarathustra's voice also resounded in such a manner that his animals"
"9353" 1998 "came to him frightened, and out of all the neighbouring caves and"
"9354" 1998 "lurking-places all the creatures slipped away--flying, fluttering,"
"9355" 1998 "creeping or leaping, according to their variety of foot or wing."
"9356" 1998 "Zarathustra, however, spake these words:"
"9357" 1998 ""
"9358" 1998 "Up, abysmal thought out of my depth! I am thy cock and morning dawn,"
"9359" 1998 "thou overslept reptile: Up! Up! My voice shall soon crow thee awake!"
"9360" 1998 ""
"9361" 1998 "Unbind the fetters of thine ears: listen! For I wish to hear thee! Up!"
"9362" 1998 "Up! There is thunder enough to make the very graves listen!"
"9363" 1998 ""
"9364" 1998 "And rub the sleep and all the dimness and blindness out of thine eyes!"
"9365" 1998 "Hear me also with thine eyes: my voice is a medicine even for those born"
"9366" 1998 "blind."
"9367" 1998 ""
"9368" 1998 "And once thou art awake, then shalt thou ever remain awake. It is not"
"9369" 1998 "MY custom to awake great-grandmothers out of their sleep that I may bid"
"9370" 1998 "them--sleep on!"
"9371" 1998 ""
"9372" 1998 "Thou stirrest, stretchest thyself, wheezest? Up! Up! Not wheeze, shalt"
"9373" 1998 "thou,--but speak unto me! Zarathustra calleth thee, Zarathustra the"
"9374" 1998 "godless!"
"9375" 1998 ""
"9376" 1998 "I, Zarathustra, the advocate of living, the advocate of suffering, the"
"9377" 1998 "advocate of the circuit--thee do I call, my most abysmal thought!"
"9378" 1998 ""
"9379" 1998 "Joy to me! Thou comest,--I hear thee! Mine abyss SPEAKETH, my lowest"
"9380" 1998 "depth have I turned over into the light!"
"9381" 1998 ""
"9382" 1998 "Joy to me! Come hither! Give me thy hand--ha! let be! aha!--Disgust,"
"9383" 1998 "disgust, disgust--alas to me!"
"9384" 1998 ""
"9385" 1998 "2."
"9386" 1998 ""
"9387" 1998 "Hardly, however, had Zarathustra spoken these words, when he fell down"
"9388" 1998 "as one dead, and remained long as one dead. When however he again came"
"9389" 1998 "to himself, then was he pale and trembling, and remained lying; and for"
"9390" 1998 "long he would neither eat nor drink. This condition continued for seven"
"9391" 1998 "days; his animals, however, did not leave him day nor night, except that"
"9392" 1998 "the eagle flew forth to fetch food. And what it fetched and foraged,"
"9393" 1998 "it laid on Zarathustra's couch: so that Zarathustra at last lay among"
"9394" 1998 "yellow and red berries, grapes, rosy apples, sweet-smelling herbage, and"
"9395" 1998 "pine-cones. At his feet, however, two lambs were stretched, which the"
"9396" 1998 "eagle had with difficulty carried off from their shepherds."
"9397" 1998 ""
"9398" 1998 "At last, after seven days, Zarathustra raised himself upon his couch,"
"9399" 1998 "took a rosy apple in his hand, smelt it and found its smell pleasant."
"9400" 1998 "Then did his animals think the time had come to speak unto him."
"9401" 1998 ""
"9402" 1998 "\"O Zarathustra,\" said they, \"now hast thou lain thus for seven days with"
"9403" 1998 "heavy eyes: wilt thou not set thyself again upon thy feet?"
"9404" 1998 ""
"9405" 1998 "Step out of thy cave: the world waiteth for thee as a garden. The wind"
"9406" 1998 "playeth with heavy fragrance which seeketh for thee; and all brooks"
"9407" 1998 "would like to run after thee."
"9408" 1998 ""
"9409" 1998 "All things long for thee, since thou hast remained alone for seven"

"9411" 1998 ""

"9413" 1998 "Like leavened dough layest thou, thy soul arose and swelled beyond all"
"9414" 1998 "its bounds.--\""
"9415" 1998 ""
"9416" 1998 "--O mine animals, answered Zarathustra, talk on thus and let me listen!"
"9417" 1998 "It refresheth me so to hear your talk: where there is talk, there is the"
"9418" 1998 "world as a garden unto me."
"9419" 1998 ""
"9420" 1998 "How charming it is that there are words and tones; are not words and"

"9422" 1998 ""

"9424" 1998 "back-world."
"9425" 1998 ""

"9427" 1998 "smallest gap is most difficult to bridge over."
"9428" 1998 ""

"9431" 1998 ""
"9432" 1998 "Have not names and tones been given unto things that man may refresh"
"9433" 1998 "himself with them? It is a beautiful folly, speaking; therewith danceth"

"9435" 1998 ""
"9436" 1998 "How lovely is all speech and all falsehoods of tones! With tones danceth"

"9438" 1998 ""

"9441" 1998 "and flee--and return."
"9442" 1998 ""
"9443" 1998 "Everything goeth, everything returneth; eternally rolleth the wheel"

"9445" 1998 "eternally runneth on the year of existence."
"9446" 1998 ""
"9447" 1998 "Everything breaketh, everything is integrated anew; eternally buildeth"

"9451" 1998 ""

"9454" 1998 ""
"9455" 1998 "--O ye wags and barrel-organs! answered Zarathustra, and smiled once"

"9457" 1998 ""
"9458" 1998 "--And how that monster crept into my throat and choked me! But I bit off"

"9464" 1998 ""
"9465" 1998 "AND YE LOOKED ON AT IT ALL? O mine animals, are ye also cruel? Did"

"9467" 1998 "animal."
"9468" 1998 ""
"9469" 1998 "At tragedies, bull-fights, and crucifixions hath he hitherto been"

"9472" 1998 ""

"9474" 1998 "and his tongue hangeth out of his mouth for very lusting. He, however,"

"9476" 1998 ""
"9477" 1998 "The little man, especially the poet--how passionately doth he accuse"

"9480" 1998 ""
"9481" 1998 "Such accusers of life--them life overcometh with a glance of the eye."
"9482" 1998 "\"Thou lovest me?\" saith the insolent one; \"wait a little, as yet have I"
"9483" 1998 "no time for thee.\""
"9484" 1998 ""
"9485" 1998 "Towards himself man is the cruellest animal; and in all who call"
"9486" 1998 "themselves \"sinners\" and \"bearers of the cross\" and \"penitents,\" do not"
"9487" 1998 "overlook the voluptuousness in their plaints and accusations!"
"9488" 1998 ""
"9489" 1998 "And I myself--do I thereby want to be man's accuser? Ah, mine animals,"
"9490" 1998 "this only have I learned hitherto, that for man his baddest is necessary"
"9491" 1998 "for his best,--"
"9492" 1998 ""
"9493" 1998 "--That all that is baddest is the best POWER, and the hardest stone for"
"9494" 1998 "the highest creator; and that man must become better AND badder:--"
"9495" 1998 ""
"9496" 1998 "Not to THIS torture-stake was I tied, that I know man is bad,--but I"

"9498" 1998 ""
"9499" 1998 "\"Ah, that his baddest is so very small! Ah, that his best is so very"
"9500" 1998 "small!\""
"9501" 1998 ""
"9502" 1998 "The great disgust at man--IT strangled me and had crept into my throat:"
"9503" 1998 "and what the soothsayer had presaged: \"All is alike, nothing is worth"
"9504" 1998 "while, knowledge strangleth.\""
"9505" 1998 ""
"9506" 1998 "A long twilight limped on before me, a fatally weary, fatally"
"9507" 1998 "intoxicated sadness, which spake with yawning mouth."
"9508" 1998 ""
"9509" 1998 "\"Eternally he returneth, the man of whom thou art weary, the small"
"9510" 1998 "man\"--so yawned my sadness, and dragged its foot and could not go to"
"9511" 1998 "sleep."
"9512" 1998 ""
"9513" 1998 "A cavern, became the human earth to me; its breast caved in; everything"
"9514" 1998 "living became to me human dust and bones and mouldering past."
"9515" 1998 ""
"9516" 1998 "My sighing sat on all human graves, and could no longer arise: my"
"9517" 1998 "sighing and questioning croaked and choked, and gnawed and nagged day"
"9518" 1998 "and night:"
"9519" 1998 ""
"9520" 1998 "--\"Ah, man returneth eternally! The small man returneth eternally!\""
"9521" 1998 ""
"9522" 1998 "Naked had I once seen both of them, the greatest man and the smallest"
"9523" 1998 "man: all too like one another--all too human, even the greatest man!"
"9524" 1998 ""
"9525" 1998 "All too small, even the greatest man!--that was my disgust at man! And"
"9526" 1998 "the eternal return also of the smallest man!--that was my disgust at all"
"9527" 1998 "existence!"
"9528" 1998 ""
"9529" 1998 "Ah, Disgust! Disgust! Disgust!--Thus spake Zarathustra, and sighed and"
"9530" 1998 "shuddered; for he remembered his sickness. Then did his animals prevent"
"9531" 1998 "him from speaking further."
"9532" 1998 ""
"9533" 1998 "\"Do not speak further, thou convalescent!\"--so answered his animals,"
"9534" 1998 "\"but go out where the world waiteth for thee like a garden."
"9535" 1998 ""
"9536" 1998 "Go out unto the roses, the bees, and the flocks of doves! Especially,"
"9537" 1998 "however, unto the singing-birds, to learn SINGING from them!"
"9538" 1998 ""
"9539" 1998 "For singing is for the convalescent; the sound ones may talk. And"
"9540" 1998 "when the sound also want songs, then want they other songs than the"
"9541" 1998 "convalescent.\""
"9542" 1998 ""
"9543" 1998 "--\"O ye wags and barrel-organs, do be silent!\" answered Zarathustra, and"
"9544" 1998 "smiled at his animals. \"How well ye know what consolation I devised for"
"9545" 1998 "myself in seven days!"
"9546" 1998 ""
"9547" 1998 "That I have to sing once more--THAT consolation did I devise for myself,"
"9548" 1998 "and THIS convalescence: would ye also make another lyre-lay thereof?\""
"9549" 1998 ""
"9550" 1998 "--\"Do not talk further,\" answered his animals once more; \"rather, thou"
"9551" 1998 "convalescent, prepare for thyself first a lyre, a new lyre!"
"9552" 1998 ""
"9553" 1998 "For behold, O Zarathustra! For thy new lays there are needed new lyres."
"9554" 1998 ""
"9555" 1998 "Sing and bubble over, O Zarathustra, heal thy soul with new lays: that"
"9556" 1998 "thou mayest bear thy great fate, which hath not yet been any one's fate!"
"9557" 1998 ""
"9558" 1998 "For thine animals know it well, O Zarathustra, who thou art and must"
"9559" 1998 "become: behold, THOU ART THE TEACHER OF THE ETERNAL RETURN,--that is now"
"9560" 1998 "THY fate!"
"9561" 1998 ""
"9562" 1998 "That thou must be the first to teach this teaching--how could this great"
"9563" 1998 "fate not be thy greatest danger and infirmity!"
"9564" 1998 ""
"9565" 1998 "Behold, we know what thou teachest: that all things eternally return,"
"9566" 1998 "and ourselves with them, and that we have already existed times without"
"9567" 1998 "number, and all things with us."
"9568" 1998 ""
"9569" 1998 "Thou teachest that there is a great year of Becoming, a prodigy of a"
"9570" 1998 "great year; it must, like a sand-glass, ever turn up anew, that it may"
"9571" 1998 "anew run down and run out:--"
"9572" 1998 ""
"9573" 1998 "--So that all those years are like one another in the greatest and also"
"9574" 1998 "in the smallest, so that we ourselves, in every great year, are like"
"9575" 1998 "ourselves in the greatest and also in the smallest."
"9576" 1998 ""
"9577" 1998 "And if thou wouldst now die, O Zarathustra, behold, we know also how"
"9578" 1998 "thou wouldst then speak to thyself:--but thine animals beseech thee not"
"9579" 1998 "to die yet!"
"9580" 1998 ""
"9581" 1998 "Thou wouldst speak, and without trembling, buoyant rather with bliss,"
"9582" 1998 "for a great weight and worry would be taken from thee, thou patientest"
"9583" 1998 "one!--"
"9584" 1998 ""
"9585" 1998 "'Now do I die and disappear,' wouldst thou say, 'and in a moment I am"
"9586" 1998 "nothing. Souls are as mortal as bodies."
"9587" 1998 ""
"9588" 1998 "But the plexus of causes returneth in which I am intertwined,--it will"
"9589" 1998 "again create me! I myself pertain to the causes of the eternal return."
"9590" 1998 ""
"9591" 1998 "I come again with this sun, with this earth, with this eagle, with this"
"9592" 1998 "serpent--NOT to a new life, or a better life, or a similar life:"
"9593" 1998 ""
"9594" 1998 "--I come again eternally to this identical and selfsame life, in its"
"9595" 1998 "greatest and its smallest, to teach again the eternal return of all"
"9596" 1998 "things,--"
"9597" 1998 ""
"9598" 1998 "--To speak again the word of the great noontide of earth and man, to"
"9599" 1998 "announce again to man the Superman."
"9600" 1998 ""
"9601" 1998 "I have spoken my word. I break down by my word: so willeth mine eternal"
"9602" 1998 "fate--as announcer do I succumb!"
"9603" 1998 ""
"9604" 1998 "The hour hath now come for the down-goer to bless himself. Thus--ENDETH"
"9605" 1998 "Zarathustra's down-going.'\"--"
"9606" 1998 ""
"9607" 1998 "When the animals had spoken these words they were silent and waited, so"
"9608" 1998 "that Zarathustra might say something to them: but Zarathustra did not"
"9609" 1998 "hear that they were silent. On the contrary, he lay quietly with closed"
"9610" 1998 "eyes like a person sleeping, although he did not sleep; for he communed"
"9611" 1998 "just then with his soul. The serpent, however, and the eagle, when they"
"9612" 1998 "found him silent in such wise, respected the great stillness around him,"
"9613" 1998 "and prudently retired."
"9614" 1998 ""
"9615" 1998 ""
"9616" 1998 ""
"9617" 1998 ""
"9618" 1998 "LVIII. THE GREAT LONGING."
"9619" 1998 ""
"9620" 1998 "O my soul, I have taught thee to say \"to-day\" as \"once on a time\" and"
"9621" 1998 "\"formerly,\" and to dance thy measure over every Here and There and"
"9622" 1998 "Yonder."
"9623" 1998 ""
"9624" 1998 "O my soul, I delivered thee from all by-places, I brushed down from thee"
"9625" 1998 "dust and spiders and twilight."
"9626" 1998 ""
"9627" 1998 "O my soul, I washed the petty shame and the by-place virtue from thee,"
"9628" 1998 "and persuaded thee to stand naked before the eyes of the sun."
"9629" 1998 ""
"9630" 1998 "With the storm that is called \"spirit\" did I blow over thy surging"
"9631" 1998 "sea; all clouds did I blow away from it; I strangled even the strangler"
"9632" 1998 "called \"sin.\""
"9633" 1998 ""
"9634" 1998 "O my soul, I gave thee the right to say Nay like the storm, and to say"
"9635" 1998 "Yea as the open heaven saith Yea: calm as the light remainest thou, and"
"9636" 1998 "now walkest through denying storms."
"9637" 1998 ""
"9638" 1998 "O my soul, I restored to thee liberty over the created and the"
"9639" 1998 "uncreated; and who knoweth, as thou knowest, the voluptuousness of the"
"9640" 1998 "future?"
"9641" 1998 ""
"9642" 1998 "O my soul, I taught thee the contempt which doth not come like"
"9643" 1998 "worm-eating, the great, the loving contempt, which loveth most where it"
"9644" 1998 "contemneth most."
"9645" 1998 ""
"9646" 1998 "O my soul, I taught thee so to persuade that thou persuadest even the"
"9647" 1998 "grounds themselves to thee: like the sun, which persuadeth even the sea"
"9648" 1998 "to its height."
"9649" 1998 ""
"9650" 1998 "O my soul, I have taken from thee all obeying and knee-bending and"
"9651" 1998 "homage-paying; I have myself given thee the names, \"Change of need\" and"
"9652" 1998 "\"Fate.\""
"9653" 1998 ""
"9654" 1998 "O my soul, I have given thee new names and gay-coloured playthings,"
"9655" 1998 "I have called thee \"Fate\" and \"the Circuit of circuits\" and \"the"
"9656" 1998 "Navel-string of time\" and \"the Azure bell.\""
"9657" 1998 ""
"9658" 1998 "O my soul, to thy domain gave I all wisdom to drink, all new wines, and"
"9659" 1998 "also all immemorially old strong wines of wisdom."
"9660" 1998 ""
"9661" 1998 "O my soul, every sun shed I upon thee, and every night and every silence"
"9662" 1998 "and every longing:--then grewest thou up for me as a vine."
"9663" 1998 ""
"9664" 1998 "O my soul, exuberant and heavy dost thou now stand forth, a vine with"
"9665" 1998 "swelling udders and full clusters of brown golden grapes:--"
"9666" 1998 ""
"9667" 1998 "--Filled and weighted by thy happiness, waiting from superabundance, and"
"9668" 1998 "yet ashamed of thy waiting."
"9669" 1998 ""
"9670" 1998 "O my soul, there is nowhere a soul which could be more loving and more"
"9671" 1998 "comprehensive and more extensive! Where could future and past be closer"
"9672" 1998 "together than with thee?"
"9673" 1998 ""
"9674" 1998 "O my soul, I have given thee everything, and all my hands have become"
"9675" 1998 "empty by thee:--and now! Now sayest thou to me, smiling and full of"
"9676" 1998 "melancholy: \"Which of us oweth thanks?--"
"9677" 1998 ""
"9678" 1998 "--Doth the giver not owe thanks because the receiver received? Is"
"9679" 1998 "bestowing not a necessity? Is receiving not--pitying?\"--"
"9680" 1998 ""
"9681" 1998 "O my soul, I understand the smiling of thy melancholy: thine"
"9682" 1998 "over-abundance itself now stretcheth out longing hands!"
"9683" 1998 ""
"9684" 1998 "Thy fulness looketh forth over raging seas, and seeketh and waiteth: the"
"9685" 1998 "longing of over-fulness looketh forth from the smiling heaven of thine"
"9686" 1998 "eyes!"
"9687" 1998 ""
"9688" 1998 "And verily, O my soul! Who could see thy smiling and not melt"
"9689" 1998 "into tears? The angels themselves melt into tears through the"
"9690" 1998 "over-graciousness of thy smiling."
"9691" 1998 ""
"9692" 1998 "Thy graciousness and over-graciousness, is it which will not complain"
"9693" 1998 "and weep: and yet, O my soul, longeth thy smiling for tears, and thy"
"9694" 1998 "trembling mouth for sobs."
"9695" 1998 ""
"9696" 1998 "\"Is not all weeping complaining? And all complaining, accusing?\" Thus"
"9697" 1998 "speakest thou to thyself; and therefore, O my soul, wilt thou rather"
"9698" 1998 "smile than pour forth thy grief--"
"9699" 1998 ""
"9700" 1998 "--Than in gushing tears pour forth all thy grief concerning thy"
"9701" 1998 "fulness, and concerning the craving of the vine for the vintager and"
"9702" 1998 "vintage-knife!"
"9703" 1998 ""
"9704" 1998 "But wilt thou not weep, wilt thou not weep forth thy purple melancholy,"
"9705" 1998 "then wilt thou have to SING, O my soul!--Behold, I smile myself, who"
"9706" 1998 "foretell thee this:"
"9707" 1998 ""
"9708" 1998 "--Thou wilt have to sing with passionate song, until all seas turn calm"
"9709" 1998 "to hearken unto thy longing,--"
"9710" 1998 ""
"9711" 1998 "--Until over calm longing seas the bark glideth, the golden marvel,"
"9712" 1998 "around the gold of which all good, bad, and marvellous things frisk:--"
"9713" 1998 ""
"9714" 1998 "--Also many large and small animals, and everything that hath light"
"9715" 1998 "marvellous feet, so that it can run on violet-blue paths,--"
"9716" 1998 ""
"9717" 1998 "--Towards the golden marvel, the spontaneous bark, and its master: he,"
"9718" 1998 "however, is the vintager who waiteth with the diamond vintage-knife,--"
"9719" 1998 ""
"9720" 1998 "--Thy great deliverer, O my soul, the nameless one--for whom future"
"9721" 1998 "songs only will find names! And verily, already hath thy breath the"
"9722" 1998 "fragrance of future songs,--"
"9723" 1998 ""
"9724" 1998 "--Already glowest thou and dreamest, already drinkest thou thirstily at"
"9725" 1998 "all deep echoing wells of consolation, already reposeth thy melancholy"
"9726" 1998 "in the bliss of future songs!--"
"9727" 1998 ""
"9728" 1998 "O my soul, now have I given thee all, and even my last possession, and"
"9729" 1998 "all my hands have become empty by thee:--THAT I BADE THEE SING, behold,"
"9730" 1998 "that was my last thing to give!"
"9731" 1998 ""
"9732" 1998 "That I bade thee sing,--say now, say: WHICH of us now--oweth thanks?--"
"9733" 1998 "Better still, however: sing unto me, sing, O my soul! And let me thank"
"9734" 1998 "thee!--"
"9735" 1998 ""
"9736" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"9737" 1998 ""
"9738" 1998 ""
"9739" 1998 ""
"9740" 1998 ""
"9741" 1998 "LIX. THE SECOND DANCE-SONG."
"9742" 1998 ""
"9743" 1998 "1."
"9744" 1998 ""
"9745" 1998 "\"Into thine eyes gazed I lately, O Life: gold saw I gleam in thy"
"9746" 1998 "night-eyes,--my heart stood still with delight:"
"9747" 1998 ""
"9748" 1998 "--A golden bark saw I gleam on darkened waters, a sinking, drinking,"
"9749" 1998 "reblinking, golden swing-bark!"
"9750" 1998 ""
"9751" 1998 "At my dance-frantic foot, dost thou cast a glance, a laughing,"
"9752" 1998 "questioning, melting, thrown glance:"
"9753" 1998 ""
"9754" 1998 "Twice only movedst thou thy rattle with thy little hands--then did my"
"9755" 1998 "feet swing with dance-fury.--"
"9756" 1998 ""
"9757" 1998 "My heels reared aloft, my toes they hearkened,--thee they would know:"
"9758" 1998 "hath not the dancer his ear--in his toe!"
"9759" 1998 ""
"9760" 1998 "Unto thee did I spring: then fledst thou back from my bound; and towards"
"9761" 1998 "me waved thy fleeing, flying tresses round!"
"9762" 1998 ""
"9763" 1998 "Away from thee did I spring, and from thy snaky tresses: then stoodst"
"9764" 1998 "thou there half-turned, and in thine eye caresses."
"9765" 1998 ""
"9766" 1998 "With crooked glances--dost thou teach me crooked courses; on crooked"
"9767" 1998 "courses learn my feet--crafty fancies!"
"9768" 1998 ""
"9769" 1998 "I fear thee near, I love thee far; thy flight allureth me, thy seeking"
"9770" 1998 "secureth me:--I suffer, but for thee, what would I not gladly bear!"
"9771" 1998 ""
"9772" 1998 "For thee, whose coldness inflameth, whose hatred misleadeth, whose"
"9773" 1998 "flight enchaineth, whose mockery--pleadeth:"
"9774" 1998 ""
"9775" 1998 "--Who would not hate thee, thou great bindress, inwindress, temptress,"
"9776" 1998 "seekress, findress! Who would not love thee, thou innocent, impatient,"
"9777" 1998 "wind-swift, child-eyed sinner!"
"9778" 1998 ""
"9779" 1998 "Whither pullest thou me now, thou paragon and tomboy? And now foolest"
"9780" 1998 "thou me fleeing; thou sweet romp dost annoy!"
"9781" 1998 ""
"9782" 1998 "I dance after thee, I follow even faint traces lonely. Where art thou?"
"9783" 1998 "Give me thy hand! Or thy finger only!"
"9784" 1998 ""
"9785" 1998 "Here are caves and thickets: we shall go astray!--Halt! Stand still!"
"9786" 1998 "Seest thou not owls and bats in fluttering fray?"
"9787" 1998 ""
"9788" 1998 "Thou bat! Thou owl! Thou wouldst play me foul? Where are we? From the"
"9789" 1998 "dogs hast thou learned thus to bark and howl."
"9790" 1998 ""
"9791" 1998 "Thou gnashest on me sweetly with little white teeth; thine evil eyes"
"9792" 1998 "shoot out upon me, thy curly little mane from underneath!"
"9793" 1998 ""
"9794" 1998 "This is a dance over stock and stone: I am the hunter,--wilt thou be my"
"9795" 1998 "hound, or my chamois anon?"
"9796" 1998 ""
"9797" 1998 "Now beside me! And quickly, wickedly springing! Now up! And over!--Alas!"
"9798" 1998 "I have fallen myself overswinging!"
"9799" 1998 ""
"9800" 1998 "Oh, see me lying, thou arrogant one, and imploring grace! Gladly would I"
"9801" 1998 "walk with thee--in some lovelier place!"
"9802" 1998 ""
"9803" 1998 "--In the paths of love, through bushes variegated, quiet, trim! Or there"
"9804" 1998 "along the lake, where gold-fishes dance and swim!"
"9805" 1998 ""
"9806" 1998 "Thou art now a-weary? There above are sheep and sun-set stripes: is it"
"9807" 1998 "not sweet to sleep--the shepherd pipes?"
"9808" 1998 ""
"9809" 1998 "Thou art so very weary? I carry thee thither; let just thine arm sink!"
"9810" 1998 "And art thou thirsty--I should have something; but thy mouth would not"
"9811" 1998 "like it to drink!--"
"9812" 1998 ""
"9813" 1998 "--Oh, that cursed, nimble, supple serpent and lurking-witch! Where art"
"9814" 1998 "thou gone? But in my face do I feel through thy hand, two spots and red"
"9815" 1998 "blotches itch!"
"9816" 1998 ""
"9817" 1998 "I am verily weary of it, ever thy sheepish shepherd to be. Thou witch,"
"9818" 1998 "if I have hitherto sung unto thee, now shalt THOU--cry unto me!"
"9819" 1998 ""
"9820" 1998 "To the rhythm of my whip shalt thou dance and cry! I forget not my"
"9821" 1998 "whip?--Not I!\"--"
"9822" 1998 ""
"9823" 1998 "2."
"9824" 1998 ""
"9825" 1998 "Then did Life answer me thus, and kept thereby her fine ears closed:"
"9826" 1998 ""
"9827" 1998 "\"O Zarathustra! Crack not so terribly with thy whip! Thou knowest surely"
"9828" 1998 "that noise killeth thought,--and just now there came to me such delicate"
"9829" 1998 "thoughts."
"9830" 1998 ""
"9831" 1998 "We are both of us genuine ne'er-do-wells and ne'er-do-ills. Beyond"
"9832" 1998 "good and evil found we our island and our green meadow--we two alone!"
"9833" 1998 "Therefore must we be friendly to each other!"
"9834" 1998 ""
"9835" 1998 "And even should we not love each other from the bottom of our"
"9836" 1998 "hearts,--must we then have a grudge against each other if we do not love"
"9837" 1998 "each other perfectly?"
"9838" 1998 ""
"9839" 1998 "And that I am friendly to thee, and often too friendly, that knowest"
"9840" 1998 "thou: and the reason is that I am envious of thy Wisdom. Ah, this mad"
"9841" 1998 "old fool, Wisdom!"
"9842" 1998 ""
"9843" 1998 "If thy Wisdom should one day run away from thee, ah! then would also my"
"9844" 1998 "love run away from thee quickly.\"--"
"9845" 1998 ""
"9846" 1998 "Thereupon did Life look thoughtfully behind and around, and said softly:"
"9847" 1998 "\"O Zarathustra, thou art not faithful enough to me!"
"9848" 1998 ""
"9849" 1998 "Thou lovest me not nearly so much as thou sayest; I know thou thinkest"
"9850" 1998 "of soon leaving me."
"9851" 1998 ""
"9852" 1998 "There is an old heavy, heavy, booming-clock: it boometh by night up to"
"9853" 1998 "thy cave:--"
"9854" 1998 ""
"9855" 1998 "--When thou hearest this clock strike the hours at midnight, then"
"9856" 1998 "thinkest thou between one and twelve thereon--"
"9857" 1998 ""
"9858" 1998 "--Thou thinkest thereon, O Zarathustra, I know it--of soon leaving"
"9859" 1998 "me!\"--"
"9860" 1998 ""
"9861" 1998 "\"Yea,\" answered I, hesitatingly, \"but thou knowest it also\"--And I"
"9862" 1998 "said something into her ear, in amongst her confused, yellow, foolish"
"9863" 1998 "tresses."
"9864" 1998 ""
"9865" 1998 "\"Thou KNOWEST that, O Zarathustra? That knoweth no one--\""
"9866" 1998 ""

"9869" 1998 "was Life dearer unto me than all my Wisdom had ever been.--"
"9870" 1998 ""
"9871" 1998 "Thus spake Zarathustra."
"9872" 1998 ""

"9876" 1998 ""

"9924" 1998 "LX. THE SEVEN SEALS."
"9925" 1998 ""
"9926" 1998 "(OR THE YEA AND AMEN LAY.)"
"9927" 1998 ""
"9928" 1998 "1."
"9929" 1998 ""
"9930" 1998 "If I be a diviner and full of the divining spirit which wandereth on"
"9931" 1998 "high mountain-ridges, 'twixt two seas,--"
"9932" 1998 ""
"9933" 1998 "Wandereth 'twixt the past and the future as a heavy cloud--hostile to"
"9934" 1998 "sultry plains, and to all that is weary and can neither die nor live:"
"9935" 1998 ""
"9936" 1998 "Ready for lightning in its dark bosom, and for the redeeming flash of"

"9939" 1998 ""

"9941" 1998 "hang like a heavy tempest on the mountain, who shall one day kindle the"

"9943" 1998 ""
"9944" 1998 "Oh, how could I not be ardent for Eternity and for the marriage-ring of"
"9945" 1998 "rings--the ring of the return?"
"9946" 1998 ""
"9947" 1998 "Never yet have I found the woman by whom I should like to have children,"
"9948" 1998 "unless it be this woman whom I love: for I love thee, O Eternity!"
"9949" 1998 ""
"9950" 1998 "FOR I LOVE THEE, O ETERNITY!"
"9951" 1998 ""
"9952" 1998 "2."
"9953" 1998 ""
"9954" 1998 "If ever my wrath hath burst graves, shifted landmarks, or rolled old"

"9956" 1998 ""
"9957" 1998 "If ever my scorn hath scattered mouldered words to the winds, and if I"
"9958" 1998 "have come like a besom to cross-spiders, and as a cleansing wind to old"

"9960" 1998 ""
"9961" 1998 "If ever I have sat rejoicing where old Gods lie buried, world-blessing,"

"9963" 1998 ""
"9964" 1998 "--For even churches and Gods'-graves do I love, if only heaven looketh"
"9965" 1998 "through their ruined roofs with pure eyes; gladly do I sit like grass"

"9967" 1998 ""
"9968" 1998 "Oh, how could I not be ardent for Eternity, and for the marriage-ring of"

"9970" 1998 ""
"9971" 1998 "Never yet have I found the woman by whom I should like to have children,"

"9973" 1998 ""
"9974" 1998 "FOR I LOVE THEE, O ETERNITY!"
"9975" 1998 ""
"9976" 1998 "3."
"9977" 1998 ""
"9978" 1998 "If ever a breath hath come to me of the creative breath, and of the"

"9980" 1998 ""
"9981" 1998 "If ever I have laughed with the laughter of the creative lightning,"
"9982" 1998 "to which the long thunder of the deed followeth, grumblingly, but"
"9983" 1998 "obediently:"
"9984" 1998 ""

"9986" 1998 "the earth, so that the earth quaked and ruptured, and snorted forth"
"9987" 1998 "fire-streams:--"
"9988" 1998 ""
"9989" 1998 "--For a divine table is the earth, and trembling with new creative"

"9991" 1998 ""
"9992" 1998 "Oh, how could I not be ardent for Eternity, and for the marriage-ring of"
"9993" 1998 "rings--the ring of the return?"
"9994" 1998 ""
"9995" 1998 "Never yet have I found the woman by whom I should like to have children,"
"9996" 1998 "unless it be this woman whom I love: for I love thee, O Eternity!"
"9997" 1998 ""
"9998" 1998 "FOR I LOVE THEE, O ETERNITY!"
"9999" 1998 ""
"10000" 1998 "4."
